Sha'arei Kedusha

Introduction

Thus said the young Chayyim son of the honorable Rabbi Yoseph Vital ZLH"H (may his memory be for life in the world to come).
I have seen those who seek to ascend, but they are few. They long to climb up, but the ladder is hidden from their view. They contemplate the books of the ancients, seeking to discover the paths of life; the way upon which to tread and the deeds that will uplift their soul to its supernal root, so that they may adhere to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, who is Eternal Perfection, blessed is He; similar to the prophets who spent all their days adhering to their Maker. Through that adhesion the Holy Spirit rested upon them and showed them the path where light dwells, enlightening their eyes in the secrets of Torah, as King David, peace be upon him, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 119</i> “Unveil my eyes, that I may behold wonders from Your Torah.” The Holy Spirit guided them on a straight path to the “Inhabited City” that is prepared for those who ascend. After the prophets came the ancient <i>Chassidim</i>. These were hermits who sought to follow in the footsteps of the prophets and emulate them. Living in caverns and deserts, they secluded themselves from society. Some remained secluded in their homes but behaved like those in the deserts. Day and night they never ceased praising their Creator through studying His Torah and singing the Psalms of King David, peace be upon him, which gladden the heart. This they did constantly, until their mind adhered to the supernal lights with powerful and mighty yearning. This was their practice all their days, until they rose to the level of receiving the Holy Spirit, prophesying unceasingly. However, since each one acted alone and the character of one person is dissimilar to that of another, the means and methods of how these holy men served <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, blessed is He, were lost to us, so that we cannot emulate their ways.
Because of this, the hearts and knowledge of the following generations dwindled and people who attained the Holy Spirit vanished. These holy men went to their resting places, leaving us groaning from thirst and hunger. Finally, hopelessness of ever exploring this wondrous wisdom sprouted in the hearts of men. Only two or three grains may be found in a stalk of wheat; one in a city or two in a clan, who seek water, but there is none, for all vision has been sealed. This is because the methods of how to approach and come close to the inner holiness were never written in a book.
Later, there arose men who sought to attain spiritual levels by invoking the angels, through the power of invoking their holy names. However, they hoped for light and beheld darkness; for the angels they conjured were of a very low order, who were appointed to affect matters of this lowly world. This being so, they are composed of both good and evil and themselves perceive neither Truth nor the supernal lights. Therefore, they revealed matters that were mixed with good and evil, truth and error and vain things; matters, such as mystical cures, alchemy (the art of transforming silver into gold and copper or tin into silver), amulets, oaths and incantations. Furthermore, these people fell to imbibing wine and strong drink. If only they would have been as devoted to studying Torah and doing mitzvot! They would have learned from the example of the four great sages of Israel who entered Paradise.<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The word paradise is a corruption of the Hebrew word Pardes.</i> Not one of them left unscathed, except for the saintly Rabbi Akiva, and even in his case, the attendant angels attempted to eject him. Had not <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה helped him, he would not have entered in peace and left in peace. If even the greatest sages of Israel were thus endangered, how much more so, we, who cannot begin to compare to them?
Truth be told, these holy sages aspired to attain very great levels, bordering on prophecy. Therefore, they were placed in harm’s way. However, in regard to us, would that we should merit even a tiny glimmer of the Holy spirit, such as the revelation of Eliyahu the Prophet, which many have merited to attain, as well known; or such as the revelation of the souls of the righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i>, as mentioned often in <i>Sefer HaTikkunim</i>-The book of Rectifications.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">The subject of the revelation of the souls of the righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i> is discussed at further length in Kuntres HaShitatchut of Rabbi DovBer of Lubavitch, translated into English under the title Visiting the Gravesites of the Righteous.</i> Furthermore, even in our times, I have witnessed holy men who merited attaining all this. Moreover, there is such a level that a person’s own soul, because of its great refinement, is revealed to him and directs him in all matters. All these ways are within reach to those who are worthy of them, even in our times. Still and all, great discernment and much experience are necessary in order that it be established upon truth, for perhaps a different spirit visited him; one that is impure. All this will be explained in Part Three, Gate Eight.
Due to all the above, I feel compelled to free true seekers of their difficulties, by supporting their right hand and instructing them concerning the path they should follow. Therefore, I have decided to compose this book, small in quantity but great in quality; may it enlighten the eyes of the wise. I have called it, “Gates of Holiness.” In it, I will explain hidden matters that have never been openly taught in previous generations. I have received these teachings directly from the mouth of the holy man of God, the messenger of <i>HaShem</i> of <i>Hosts</i> – יהו"ה צבאות, my master and teacher, Rabbi Yitzchak Luria, the holy Ari’zal. Being that these are concealed and hidden matters that have forever been kept secret, I will, therefore, reveal only a hands-breadth while concealing two thousand cubits. Thus, with great difficulty, I will unlock the gates of holiness and push them open just a crack, merely the width of a pin. May it be that those who are worthy, merit entering the inner sanctum. <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה is good and will not deprive goodness from those who walk in purity.
I have divided the book into four parts:
Part One – Regarding saintly and ascetic conduct that leads to the attainment of the Holy Spirit. This part is divided into six gates. Part Two – Words of rebuke, including an explanation of reward and punishment in connection to the positive and negative commandments-<i>mitzvot</i>. This part is divided into eight gates. Part Three – Regarding how to attain the Holy Spirit. This part is divided into eight parts. Part Four – Regarding methods of meditative “unifications” (<i>Yichudim</i>) through which the Holy Spirit may be attained. I have personally tried and tested these and have found them to be effective. However, I will only enumerate their details briefly, by way of signposts that point the way.

The First Part is divided into six gates. The first, to make known the enormity  of the defect caused by human sin relative to the mitzvot. The second, how the defect is perpetuated by various middot (emotional characteristics or intelligences). The third, explanation of a righteous or beloved name. The fourth, explanation of the level of the tzaddiq (righteous person, saint) in detail. The fifth, explanation of the level of the hasid (beloved or loyal person) in detail. The sixth, a very brief explanation of the meditation of hasids, summarizing each of the gates which are in this part.
The Second Part...

Part 1





Shaar 1

Part One
Gate One <b>The blemishes caused by transgressing the <i>mitzvot</i> of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Torah</b>
Let me instill you with wisdom and enlighten you regarding the great damage that befalls a Jew who transgresses any of the 365 <i>mitzvot</i> that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה forbade us from doing or desists from fulfilling any of the 248 positive <i>mitzvot</i> that He commanded us to do.
As known, the physical body of man is not his actual identity. It is merely called human flesh, as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Job 10:11</i> “You clothed me with skin and flesh and covered me with bones and veins.” Furthermore, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 30:32</i> “It may not be applied to the flesh of man etc.” From this we understand that man is the inner aspect, whereas, the body (the flesh) is similar to a garment. The intellectual soul of man, which is his true identity, is invested in the body as long as he remains in this physical world. However, upon death, he is divested of the garment of the body and instead, becomes clothed in a spiritual, rarified and pure garment. This is as scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Zechariah 3:4</i> “Remove the soiled garments from upon him;” and he said to him, “Behold, I have removed your iniquity from upon you and dressed you in a pure garment.” This garment is called, “The Raiment of the Rabbis.”
Just as the tailor makes a garment according to the form of a person’s body, so <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, blessed is He, made the body, which is the garment for the soul, in the form of the image of the soul. That is, He made 248 organs plus 365 veins and arteries that connect them. The blood and life-force surge from organ to organ by means of these arteries that are similar to pipes. Once the body was formed, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה blew the spirit of life into it.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 2:7</i> This spirit is comprised of 248 spiritual organs and 365 spiritual veins that are invested within the 248 organs and 365 veins of the physical body. With this, the organs of the soul act through the organs of the body, which are their tools, like an axe in the hand of the lumberjack. Proof of this, is the fact that the physical organs only perform their functions so long as the soul resides within them; the eyes see and the ears hear etc. However, upon the departure of the soul, the eyes dim and all sense and feeling vanishes from the 248 organs.
In like manner, the 365 spiritual veins of the soul are invested within the 365 physical veins and distribute the physical sustenance of the blood to the 248 organs of the body, together with the spiritual sustenance within it, to sustain the 248 organs of the soul. Upon death, when the soul departs, life-force ceases to be drawn to the body. As a result, the physical veins and organs fall apart, decompose and become as if they never were. From this we see that the actual identity of a person is his intellectual soul and that it resides within the body, which acts as its garment while the soul remains in this world.
Know that when the first man sinned by eating the fruit of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil, both his body and soul took on a composition of good and evil. This is the matter of “the contamination of the serpent,”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 146a and elsewhere.</i> that was instilled in Eve and Adam. This dross brought about illness, disease and death, both spiritually and physically. This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 2:17</i> “For on the day that you eat from it, you shall surely die” – meaning the death of the soul, as well as the death of the body.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">The literal translation of the verse is, “Die, you shall die,” that is, both physical and spiritual death.</i>
We will now explain the matter of the good and evil that became mixed in them. (Examine what is written in Part Three, gates two and three, and you will understand what is written in this gate.) Behold, when man sinned with the tree of the knowledge of good and evil, he caused this admixture to permeate all worlds.<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer HaMashalim of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as The Book of Allegories 1-4, and elsewhere.</i> Due to this, there is nothing that does not include both good and evil in it.
Therefore, the body of man was formed from the four elements of the physical world<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah, Ch. 4.</i> that have both good and evil included in them. These are fire, air, water and earth. However, man’s body was formed from the choicest portion of these elements.<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">The physical body of man is the most refined matter in all of physical creation, as opposed to the grosser physicality of all other creatures.</i> Nevertheless, this choice portion also has an admixture of evil in it. Man’s four humors (that is, the white, black, red and green humors)<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">The white humor is phlegm, the black humor is the gall produced by the spleen, the red humor is blood and the green humor is the gall of the gallbladder. These humors affect the physical health and balance of a person, as well as his character and disposition. </i> were formed from the grossest portion of these elements. For the body to be healthy, these humors must be balanced. However, if there is an imbalance, and any one of them overpowers the positive characteristics of the others with its negative characteristics, the result is illness and disease. If it is even more overpowering, death may result.
As explained, the admixture of good and evil permeated all worlds, even the upper, spiritual worlds. This being the case, the soul of man was also affected, for was it not hewn from the same four spiritual elements from which all the supernal beings were formed? These four elements are the four letters of the name <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">For a more expansive explanation of the Name HaShem-יהו"ה, and the manner in which all novel creations are brought forth by and dependent upon the Singular Preexistent Intrinsic and Essential Being of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, see Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated under the title HaShem is One.</i> blessed is He and blessed is His name. About this it says,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 37:9 </i> “From the four spirits, come O spirit etc.” This “spirit” that comes is the essential soul of man from the side of goodness. However, God made everything with its opposite.<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 7:14</i> Just as the upper spiritual worlds are the source of goodness and purity, so He created a source of evil and impurity. This is the <i>Sitra Achera</i> (The Other Side) which is called <i>Adam BliYa’al</i> (The Incorrigible Man).<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:12 – “אדם בליעל” – The term “<i>BliYa’al</i>-בליעל” divides into the two words “without a yoke-<i>Bli Ol</i>-בלי עול,” meaning, without the yoke of Heaven, and can also be read “without ascent-<i>Bli Ya’al</i>-בלי יעל,” meaning, the animalistic inclination in man, that descends downward, as stated (Eccl. 3:21), “Who realizes that the spirit of man is the one that ascends on high while the spirit of the beast is the one that descends below down into the earth.”</i> It is made up of four sources of destruction<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">See Mishnah Bava Kama 1:1 – “The four Fathers of Damages” (אבות נזיקין). </i> and four indicators of plague,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">See Mishna Nega’im 1:1 – “The indicators of plague (מראות נגעים), are two, which in fact are four.”</i> which are its four bad elements. From there, an evil soul, which is called, “The Evil Inclination” (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>), is drawn to man. If this soul overpowers the good soul, destruction, plagues and spiritual illnesses befall it. Moreover, if it is too overpowering, it can even cause spiritual death, God forbid.
Now, the pure soul, which is compared to the fruit, consists of 613 organs and veins and resides within the 613 organs and veins of the impure soul, which is compared to the shell (<i>Kelipah</i>) covering over the fruit. In turn, they both reside within the 613 organs and veins of the body. Thus, the organs of the pure soul reside within the organs of the impure soul and the organs of the impure soul reside within the organs of the body. In order to exist, each of these two souls needs spiritual sustenance. However, the spiritual sustenance of the holy soul is drawn to it through the fulfillment of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Torah, which consists of 613 <i>mitzvot</i>, corresponding to the 613 organs of the soul. Thus, the Torah is called “bread (<i>Lechem</i>-לחם),”<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">The term “bread-<i>Lechem</i>-לחם-78” has a numerical value of “He was, and He is, and He will be-<i>Hayah v’Hoveh v’Yihiyeh</i>-היה והוה ויהיה-78,” and is a reference to the inner sustenance of the eternal Truth of the Torah of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. This is called “The Inner Bread” (<i>Lechem HaPanim</i>-לחם הפנים) which is a constant in the Holy Temple, as it states (Exodus 25:30), “And you shall set showbread (<i>Lechem HaPanim</i>-לח״ם הפנים) upon the table, before Me, always (<i>Tamid</i>-תמיד).” (See Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 4, section entitled “The First Vowel <i>Cholem</i>-חל״ם.”)</i> as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 9:5</i> “Come, partake of My bread.” Each of the 248 organs receives sustenance from a specific <i>mitzvah</i> that relates to that organ. However, if a Jew lacks the fulfillment of any <i>mitzvah</i>, the organ specific to that <i>mitzvah</i> will lack the sustenance drawn to it from the four letters of the Name <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה. This is indicated by the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Nehemiah 9:6</i> “You (<i>HaShem</i>) give life to all.” All the <i>mitzvot</i> depend on these four letters, as our sages of blessed memory said,<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 24a; Zohar III 110b, 222b; 273b, and elsewhere</i> “The letters <i>Yod</i> (י) <i>Hey</i> (ה) coupled with the word, ‘My name’ (שמי) of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 3:15</i> ‘This is My name and this is My memorial (זה שמי וזה זכרי) have the numerical value of 365. The letters <i>Vav</i> (ו) <i>Hey</i> (ה) coupled with the word, ‘My memorial’ (זכרי) of the same verse, have the numerical value of 248.’”
Likewise, as mentioned above, the roots of the four elements of the holy soul are drawn from these four letters. Therefore, if a person totally lacks a specific <i>mitzvah</i>, the corresponding organ of his holy soul starves to death and departs, God forbid. In turn, when this holiness departs from it, the spirit of impurity from the four elements of the impure soul fills the void and becomes vested in it. This is the secret of the Rabbinic dictum,<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Rashi to Genesis 25:23; See Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 42a; Megillah 6a; Zohar II 236a, 238b.</i> “Tyre did not become a great metropolis until Jerusalem was destroyed.” Thus, the organ now receives its sustenance from the “impure bread” that was exiled from there.
This is the meaning of the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Berachot 18b; Zohar III 123a</i> “The wicked are considered to be dead during their lifetime.”<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Similarly, it states (Proverbs 12:9), “Better is the lowly one who is His servant, than a pompous one who lacks bread (<i>Lechem</i>-לחם),” referring the the aforementioned spiritual sustenance. (See Tzava’at HaRivash (HaRav Yisroel Ba’al Shem Tov) translated as The Way of The Baal Shem Tov, Section 114.)</i> This is because the holy soul from the Living God has withdrawn from them. Rather, death, which is called, “The ultimate source of impurities,”<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Rashi to Numbers 19:22 and elsewhere. (אבי אבות הטומאה)</i> rests upon them.<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">That is, their life is not a life.</i> Conversely, regarding a Jew who desists from transgressing the 365 negative <i>mitzvot</i>, the sages stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Kiddushin 39a</i> “A person who desists from transgressing a negative <i>mitzvah</i> is rewarded as if he performed a positive <i>mitzvah</i>.” In other words, by not transgressing, he empowers the spiritual sustenance that is drawn through the positive <i>mitzvot</i>, as mentioned above, to flow through the “pipes,” which are the 365 veins of the soul, thus enlivening its 248 organs. However, if he transgresses any of them, the pipe specific to that transgression becomes blocked due to the contamination of the sustenance from the <i>Kelipah</i>, which adheres to the walls of the pipe. When the pipe withers, the organ that receives from it withers with it. This is so, even if the life-force is not totally withdrawn from it, similar to one who lacks a positive <i>mitzvah</i>. Nonetheless, it becomes blemished.
This being the case, every Jew should make every effort to fulfill as many of the 613 <i>mitzvot</i> that he can. Furthermore, when he fulfills a positive <i>mitzvah</i>, he should have in mind to rid the specific organ of his soul which correlates to that <i>mitzvah</i>, of the dross of that <i>Kelipah</i>. Once the dross has been removed, the holy organ of the <i>mitzvah</i> may rest upon him. This is the secret of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 32:27</i> “Their sins were upon their bones,” because when the one rises, the other falls. Likewise, when an opportunity to transgress comes about, he should restrain himself from doing it and have in mind that by doing so, the dross in the specific vein of his soul which correlates to that transgression withdraws. With this, the blockage will be removed and the spiritual influence which is drawn by way of that spiritual pipe will be able to flow through. In this way, his soul becomes a seat and a vehicle for <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה holiness, blessed is He. This is the secret of,<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Bereshit Rabbah 47:6</i> “The forefathers are the Chariot (<i>Merkavah</i>).”

Shaar 2

Gate Two
<b>Concerning the blemishes that come about through bad character traits</b>
The character traits are naturally embedded in the lowly, elemental soul of man. This soul is comprised of four aspects; inanimate, vegetative, animate and articulate.<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Inanimate-<i>Domem-</i>דומם, vegetative-<i>Tzome’ach-</i>צומח, animate-<i>Chay</i>-חי, and articulate-<i>Medaber</i>-מדבר.</i> They too are a composite of good and evil. Therefore, the good and bad character traits depend on this soul. They constitute a seat, foundation and root for the upper, intellectual soul, upon which the 613 <i>mitzvot</i> of the Torah depend, as mentioned above in gate one. Because of this, the character traits are not included as part and parcel of the 613 <i>mitzvot</i>. Nonetheless, they are essential prerequisites to their fulfillment or negation, for the simple reason that the intellectual soul is powerless to fulfill the <i>mitzvot</i> with the 613 organs of the body, except through the agency of the elemental soul which is connected to the body. This is the secret meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 17:14</i> “For the soul of every flesh; its blood is its life.” This being the case, bad character traits are actually much worse than the transgressions themselves.
We may now understand why our sages, of blessed memory, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 27b; Zohar II 182b; Zohar III 179b, 234b; Tikkunim 89b; Zohar Chadash Noach; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot 2:3</i> “When a person loses his temper, it is as if he is actually worshipping idolatry” – which is a negation of all 613 <i>mitzvot</i> of the Torah! Furthermore, they said,<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 5a</i> “Whosoever has a haughty spirit is likened to one who denies the fundamental truth of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה existence. He is worthy of being cut down like an <i>Asherah</i> grove.”<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">This was a grove used for the ancient idolatry of tree worship.</i> There are many such quotes. Contemplate this greatly and consider that since the character traits are root-causes and fundamental characteristics imbedded in the natural soul, they are not counted amongst the 613 <i>mitzvot</i> that depend on the intellectual soul. We therefore find that greater caution must be taken to safeguard oneself from bad character traits, than even from fulfilling the positive <i>mitzvot</i> or desisting from committing the negative <i>mitzvot</i>. This is because if a Jew has good character traits, he will not find it difficult to fulfill all the <i>mitzvot</i>.
With this, we may now understand some astounding comments made by our sages, of blessed memory, regarding character traits, such as the statement that humility and a sense of lowliness bring about the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach</i> <i>HaKodesh</i>), in which the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>) rests upon a person. Furthermore, Eliyahu said,<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">Kallah Rabbati Ch. 5</i> “Only a person who is not short-tempered will be given the ability to explain the meanings of Torah. Moreover, I too, will not be revealed except to one who is not short-tempered.” Likewise, our sages of blessed memory said,<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 88b</i> “Who is worthy of life in the coming world? Whosoever is lowly and humble.” There are many such statements. Note that they mention good character traits rather than fulfilling the <i>mitzvot</i>. Set your eyes upon these goals and you shall surely find success.
However, just as the four physical elements are the roots from which the 613 organs of the body were formed, so likewise, the physical life-force of these four elements are the foundations of all the good and bad character traits, which are the means by which the Torah and the 613 <i>mitzvot</i>, that come from the four-letter Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, may be fulfilled or negated. It is the intellectual soul, which is comprised of the four spiritual elements from which its 613 organs were hewn, that fulfills the <i>mitzvot</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">This means that in order for the Divine soul to perform the physical <i>mitzvot</i>, it must act through the agency of the four elements of the animal soul (which are the physical life-force of the body and the source of all the natural character traits). This is because the Divine soul is invested in the animal soul and the animal soul is invested in the body, as will be explained.  </i> Contemplate this well and you will understand that the basis for the fulfillment or negation of the <i>mitzvot</i> are good and bad character traits.
We have already explained that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה composed everything of two opposites, good and evil. Just as there are four bodily elements composed of good and bad; the white, green, black and red humors, and these powers either establish a physically healthy body (“Matter”) or damage it, so is it regarding the life-force of the natural, elemental soul (“Form”). Its four elements are also comprised of both good and evil which affect its health through good character traits, or its illness, through bad character traits that are drawn from its four evil, impure <i>Kelipot</i> (Husks). When a Jew rids himself of these bad character traits, then, in their stead, the four letters of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Name become invested in the natural soul and become a life-giving light for it. Thus, the natural soul and the physical body become a vehicle for <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה holiness in the world of Action (<i>Asiyah</i>) [which is the <i>Nefesh</i> level of the intellectual soul]. This, literally, is similar to what was explained about the intellectual soul when it fulfills the <i>mitzvot</i>.
Moreover, keep in mind that, besides this, through occupying oneself in the study of the four levels of Torah, which form the acronym פרדס-<B>P</B>a<B>RD</B>e<B>S</B> (The Orchard), which are <i><B>P</B>eshat</i>, <i><B>R</B>emez</i>, <i><B>D</B>erush</i>, and <i><B>S</B>od</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">That is, פ-<i><B>P</B>eshat</i> is the straightforward, simple meaning of the verses; ר-<i><B>R</B>emez</i> is the meaning that is intimated but not explicitly stated in the verses; ד-<i><B>D</B>eroosh</i> is the meaning arrived at through deeper investigation and analysis of the verses; ס-<i><B>S</B>od</i> is the esoteric secrets of the verses.</i> the <i>Ruach</i> level of one’s intellectual soul becomes a seat for the four letters of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Name in the world of Formation (<i>Yetzirah</i>). Likewise, through contemplation and mental focus, the <i>Neshamah</i> level of his intellectual soul becomes a seat for the four letters of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Name in the world of Creation (<i>Beriyah</i>).
Returning to the explanation of the acquisition of good character traits through the clarification of the four elements; know that all the bad character traits are rooted in the evil and <i>Kelipah</i> of the four levels of the elemental soul. Because of this, all bad character traits may be categorized into four kinds, as follows:
<b>A) The Element of Fire:</b> This element is the source of arrogance, which is called, “A Coarse Spirit.”<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Gas Ru’ach</i> – גס רוח</i> This is because it is the lightest and highest of all the elements. It includes anger, because, when his will is not done, an arrogant person becomes angered. If he would always be humble and recognize his own limitations and shortcomings, he would not lose his temper. From this we see that arrogance and anger are one and the same quality. This character trait has three offshoots;<br>1) Being short-tempered. If not for haughtiness, a person would never be short-tempered, similar to what we explained about anger.<br>2) Seeking to dominate others and be honored by them. This is because he believes he is their superior.<br>3) Hatred toward anyone who actually is his superior. This too is an offshoot of arrogance.
<b>B) The Element of Wind (Air)</b> This element is the source of the kind of speech that is called, “Idle Chatter.” That is, talking about frivolous matters that have no bearing on anything, neither spiritually nor physically. This character trait has four offshoots;
<br>1) Speaking words of flattery.
<br>2) Speaking falsehoods.
<br>3) Speaking badly (the evil tongue) of others.
<br>4) Speaking words of boasting and self-aggrandizement to others.
<b>C) The Element of Water</b> This element is the source of lust and the desire for pleasure. This is because water causes all manner of pleasurable things to grow. This character trait has two offshoots;
<br>1) Envy. This leads to stealing another’s property or seducing his wife or the theft of anything that someone else possesses that he wants to delight in.
<br>2) Jealousy. If his friend is wealthy or the like, which he wishes he could be; he will harbor jealousy toward him.
<b>D) The Element of Earth</b> This element is the source of depression in all its details. It has one offshoot;
<br>1) Slothfulness. This causes him to be lazy in studying Torah or fulfilling the <i>mitzvot</i>, either because he is depressed by the difficulty of acquiring the vanities of this world or because of troubles that befall him. Such a person will never be happy with his lot, in any matter. Moreover, no matter how wealthy he becomes, it will never satisfy him.
From the above, we find that there are four sources of all the bad character traits. These are arrogance (including anger, which adheres to it), idle chatter, lust for pleasure, and depression. Their sources are the four <i>Kelipot</i> of the <i>Yetzer</i> <i>HaRa</i> (The Evil Inclination) in the elemental soul. The opposites of these are four good character traits whose sources are the four good elements of the elemental soul. These are:<br>1) Humility. This is a total sense of unimportance. Such a person distances himself from any kind of anger, because anger is a result of haughtiness.
<br>2) Silence. Except when he is occupied in the study of Torah and <i>mitzvot</i> or in the physical needs of the body or for the needs of others, he acts as if mute, as one who cannot open his mouth.
<br>3) He despises all physical pleasure or unnecessary excesses.
<br>4) He is always happy with his lot. This is because he realizes that it all is from <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה above, and everything that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה brings about is for the good.<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 60b; Midrash Bereishit Rabba 51:3, and elsewhere; Also see Tzava’at HaRivash translated as The Way of The Baal Shem Tov, Section 2.</i> This attitude also results in alacrity with perfect joy in serving his Creator, as scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 119:162</i> “I rejoice in Your words as one who has discovered vast treasure.” Similarly, our sages stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:15</i> “Make Torah study your permanent priority and your occupation a temporary one.”
We see that when bad character traits are embedded in a Jew, they obstruct him from fulfilling Torah and <i>mitzvot</i>. Even if he does fulfill them, it will not be for the sake of Heaven and they will be very burdensome to him. About such a person scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 11</i> “A golden ring in the snout of a pig,” because his impurity is still within him, vested within the <i>Kelipot</i>. This is as our sages, of blessed memory said,<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 75 </i> “If a person is meritorious, his Torah learning becomes a life-giving elixir. However, if he is not meritorious, it becomes fatally poisonous.” However, if a person rises up to overcome his evil inclination and battles against it, until through great effort he rids himself of his bad character traits, and thus truly fulfills Torah and <i>mitzvot</i>; he is called a “Perfect <i>Tzaddik</i>,” a “God Fearing Person” and a “Mighty Warrior who conquers his evil inclination.” Moreover, if a Jew advances in this, accustoming himself to it to an even greater degree, until he completely rids himself of all bad traits, to the point that his soul no longer lusts after them at all, and he acquires good traits to the point that they literally become natural to him, in that he no longer needs to battle against the evil inclination, since both his body and elemental soul have become thoroughly cleansed of all physical dross, as <i>Sefer HaTikkunim</i> comments<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikun 31 and 48</i> on the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 3:5</i> “Take your shoes off your feet” in regard to Moshe; then the four letters of the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה become invested in him and he becomes a holy seat for <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה chariot (<i>Merkavah</i>), blessed is He. Such a person is called a “Friend of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה out of love.” He is called a “Perfect <i>Chassid</i>” – one who is perfect with every kind of perfection.

Shaar 3

Gate Three
<b>A thorough explanation of the levels of “<i>Tzaddik</i>” and “<i>Chassid</i>” and how one should act in order to attain them</b>
If a Jew wishes to purify and sanctify himself and truly accept the yoke of the Heavenly kingdom upon himself, let him prepare himself with all his might to perform all 613 <i>mitzvot</i> with alacrity. Through their fulfillment the 613 organs and veins of his soul will become perfected, as mentioned above. This is because if he lacks even one of the 248 positive <i>mitzvot</i>, he still lacks an organ of his soul. About such a person scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 1:15</i> “A lacking which is incalculable,” which is worse than the matter of, “Anyone who has a blemish may not approach.”<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">This is because, as explained above, a blemish in a <i>mitzvah</i> is not the complete absence of the <i>mitzvah</i>. Therefore, one who lacks a positive <i>mitzvah</i> altogether, is worse off than one who performs it, but in a blemished and imperfect manner. Nonetheless, though his positive <i>mitzvot</i> are blemished, and since he does not transgress the negative <i>mitzvot</i>, he does not fall into the category of an actual “<i>Baal Moom</i>,” that is, a truly blemished person.   </i>
<br>However, a Jew who fulfills the positive <i>mitzvot</i>, but has transgressed even one of the 365 negative <i>mitzvot</i>, is within the category of an actual “<i>Baal Moom</i>” – a blemished person. This is because the pipe (or vein) that draws sustenance to the organs has become bent [thereby obstructing the flow]. About such as person the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 1:15</i> “irreparably crooked.” However, the meaning of the verse is that it is only irreparable once the soul has departed from this world, because one cannot perform the <i>mitzvot</i> that he lacks or repent and thereby rectify the transgressions that he committed, except while he still is in this world. This is as scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 9:10</i> “Whatever you can accomplish while you are able, do it, for there is neither deed nor accounting nor knowledge nor wisdom in the grave to which you are going.” “Deed” here, refers to performing the positive <i>mitzvot</i>, “Accounting” refers to repenting over the negative ones and “knowledge” refers to the knowledge gained through the study of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Torah. None of these are possible “in the grave to which you are going.”
<br>From here we see that as long as a Jew has not fulfilled the 613 <i>mitzvot</i>, he is in the category of an “Imperfect <i>Tzaddik</i>.” It is not without warrant, that our teacher Moshe, peace be upon him, prayed for permission to enter the land 515 times, corresponding to the numerical value of the word, “and I pleaded for grace-<i>VaEtchanan-</i>ואתחנן-515.<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Dvarim Rabba 11:1</i> He sought to perfect his soul by keeping the 613 <i>mitzvot</i> [many of which only apply in the land of Israel].
<br>If a Jew fulfills all the <i>mitzvot</i>, but has not also fully acquired all the good character traits, in that he must constantly battle and conquer his <i>Yetzer HaRa</i>, such a person is in the category of a “Perfect <i>Tzaddik</i> who conquers his <i>Yetzer</i>.”
<br>However, once all the good character traits become so totally imbedded in a person that they become his nature, so that he performs the 613 <i>mitzvot</i> with joy that comes from love, without any resistance from the <i>Yetzer HaRa,</i> because his physicality has become totally refined, he is called a “Perfect <i>Chassid</i>.” Similarly, King David said,<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 109</i> “My heart is empty within me.”<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">This means that he rid himself totally of the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>) by starving it to death. (See Talmud Bavli, Bava Batra 17a; Brachot 61b; Talmud Yerushalmi Brachot 9:5; Sotah 5:5; Orchot Tzaddikim 26:82; Tanya, Ch. 1)</i> Furthermore, he said,<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 131</i> “<i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, my heart was not proud, nor were my eyes haughty. Neither did I pursue matters that were too great or wondrous for me. Have I not calmed and stilled my soul like an infant nursing from his mother? My soul is like a nursing infant.” This is to say that he appears as if all his good character traits were already naturally embedded in him when he first came out of his mother’s womb. Therefore, because good character traits and the performance of the <i>mitzvot</i> had become so embedded in King David’s nature, he called himself a <i>Chassid</i>, as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 86</i> “Guard my soul, for I am a <i>Chassid</i>.”
Moreover, our sages, of blessed memory, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Baba Kama 30</i> “Whosoever desires to become a <i>Chassid</i> should fulfill the words of <i>Pirkei Avot</i> – which speak regarding the acquisition of good character traits. For example, our sages, of blessed memory, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">Avot 2:1</i> “Rabbi [Yehudah the Prince] said, “What is the straight path that a person should follow? Everything that is both beautiful to the doer and beautiful to him from others etc.” Akaviah ben Mehalalel said,<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Avot 3:1</i> “Contemplate three matters and you will never come to the possibility of transgressing. Know from whence you came and where you are going and before whom you are destined to give an accounting. From whence did you come? – From a putrid drop. Where are you going? – To a place of dust, maggots and worms. Before whom are you destined to give an accounting? – Before the King, King of kings, The Holy One, blessed is He.” Likewise, Rabbi Levitas of Yavneh said,<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Avot 4:4</i> “Be very, very humble, for the hope of man is maggots.” What Akaviah meant when he said, “and you will never come to the possibility of transgressing” is that you will never be subject to the <i>Yetzer HaRa</i> which causes a person to transgress, because your <i>Yetzer HaRa</i> will cease to be. However, if the <i>Yetzer HaRa</i> still exists and one merely restrains himself by force of willpower, he should have stated, “you will not transgress.”
Generally, what comes out of this is that a <i>Tzaddik</i> is a person who has a <i>Yetzer HaRa</i> but fulfills the 613 <i>mitzvot</i> by overcoming it. On the other hand, a person who has acquired good character traits completely, as his nature, fulfills the <i>mitzvot</i> because his <i>Yetzer HaRa</i> has been abrogated. Such a person is called a “Perfect <i>Chassid.</i>”
In addition, there is a level of piety (<i>Chassidut</i>) even higher than this, which is the highest of all levels. Such a person is called “Holy.” This level is mentioned often in <i>Sefer HaTikkunim</i> and in the <i>Zohar</i>, especially in <i>Parashat Kee Teitzei</i> of <i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 281a</i> as follows:
“It is not without warrant that the Holy One, blessed is He, said, ‘Whosoever occupies himself in the study of Torah, in doing acts of lovingkindness and in praying with the congregation, I regard it as if he redeemed Me and My children from exile amongst the nations of the world.’ Now, how many people occupy themselves in the study of Torah, in doing acts of lovingkindness and in praying with the congregation, but nonetheless, the Holy One, blessed is He, His Indwelling Presence (the <i>Shechinah</i>) and Israel are not redeemed!? However, the meaning here is that a person should be occupied in the study of Torah for the sole purpose of uniting the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>) to the Holy One, blessed is He. As we have established, “Acts of lovingkindness” here, means that a true <i>Chassid</i> is one who is kind<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">That is, he performs kindness-<i>Chessed</i>-חסד, and is thus called a one who is kind-<i>Chassid</i>-חסיד toward his Master.</i> toward his Master. That is, his intent in doing all the <i>mitzvot</i> is to liberate the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>) from exile. By doing so, he acts kindly toward the Holy One, blessed is He. By acting kindly toward <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Indwelling Presence, he is acting kindly toward <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה Himself, blessed is He. When Israel sinned, the Holy One, blessed is He, wanted to punish them, but their “Mother” – the <i>Shechinah –</i> protected them. Because of this, they descended into evil ways. What did the Holy One, blessed is He, do? He banished the children of the King, along with the Queen [the <i>Shechinah</i>] and He swore that He would not return to His place until the Queen returns to Her place. Thus, whosoever repents with the sole intention of liberating the <i>Shechinah</i> through Torah and <i>mitzvot</i>; such a person acts kindly toward his Master. It is as if he liberates <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, His <i>Shechinah</i> and His children from exile. Eliyahu and all the heads of the upper academies declared, ‘<i>Raaya Mehemna-</i>Faithful Shepherd [Moshe], you are such a person. You are the son of the King and Queen. Actually, your manner of toil for the Holy One, blessed is He, is even beyond one who acts kindly toward his Master. Rather, you are like a son who invests his whole being and strength into liberating his father and mother; who is willing to give up his very life for their sake. However, a person who is not in the category of being the son of the King, but who, nonetheless, does a kindness to the King and Queen, such a person is considered to be kindly toward his Master.’ <i>Raaya Mehemna-</i>the Faithful Shepherd (Moshe) stood up and bowed before the Holy One, blessed is He. He wept and said, ‘May it be <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה will to regard me as a son. May it be that He will consider my actions on behalf of the Holy One, blessed is He and His <i>Shechinah</i>, like a son who toils on behalf of his father and mother because he loves them more than his own body, soul [<i>Nefesh</i>], spirit [<i>Ruach</i>] and super-soul [<i>Neshamah</i>], who regards all his possessions as worthless, except for the purpose of serving the will of his Father and Mother and liberating them. Though I realize that [in reality] everything is <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה possession [and that I have nothing of my own], nonetheless, the Merciful One desires the heart.’”
Now, the above is as Scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:18</i> “You have disregarded The Rock that bore you.” Moreover, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 68:35</i> “Give strength to God.” This is in accordance to the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Berachot 17a</i> “Rabbi Yochanan says, ‘Happy is he who toils in Torah and brings satisfaction to the One who formed him.’ – meaning that he does not toil in the study of Torah in order to receive reward at all. Rather, his intent is solely to bring satisfaction to the One who formed him, about Whom it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 63:9</i> “In all their suffering, He suffered.” That is, wherever Israel were exiled, the <i>Shechinah</i> went with them. She is our Mother, about whom it says,<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 50:1</i> “Thus says <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, ‘Where is your Mother’s bill of divorce [as proof] that I have banished her? To which of my creditors did I sell you? Truly, you were sold through your sins and through your transgressions, and she was banished with you.’” [It is, specifically, the <i>Shechinah</i> that] is called “The One Who formed us,” as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:18</i> “You have disregarded The Rock who bore you.” [The word for rock here is <i>Tzoor</i> (צור), which also means the “source of form,” just as a child is formed in its mother’s womb.] This is why Rabbi Yochanan said that such a person brings satisfaction “to The One who formed him,” rather than saying “to The Holy One, blessed is He.”
From this we see that when a <i>Chassid</i> is occupied in the study of Torah or in performing the <i>mitzvot</i> or in good character traits; if even a hint of motivation to receive a reward is mixed into it, he is a <i>Chassid</i> for himself, as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 11:17</i> “A man of kindness (<i>Ish Chessed</i>) brings goodness upon himself.” This is because when he fulfills the <i>mitzvot</i>, he brings goodness upon himself. Therefore, he is called a “Man of <i>Chessed</i>” rather than a “<i>Chassid</i>,” because he does himself the kindness. Only a person whose sole motivation is to do a kindness for his Master can be truly called a “<i>Chassid</i>” and a “Holy Man.” This is because he has become purified from all impurities and has sanctified himself in <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה holiness, blessed is He. We find that the term קדושה-<i>Kedushah</i> (holiness) means “preparation,” as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 11:18</i> “Prepare<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">The word here for “prepare yourselves” is “<i>Hitkadshoo</i>-sanctify yourselves” (התקדשו).</i> yourselves for tomorrow and you shall eat meat.” This is because such a person makes himself the vehicle for <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה holiness, blessed is He. As mentioned above, rather than caring about his own glory, he only cares about his Master’s glory.
When Rabbi Pinchas ben Yair said,<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Sotah 9:15 </i> “Caution brings to zeal, zeal brings to cleanliness, cleanliness brings to separateness, separateness brings to purity, purity brings to holiness, holiness brings to fear of sin, fear of sin brings to humility, humility brings to <i>Chassidut</i>, <i>Chassidut</i> brings to the Holy Spirit and the Holy Spirit brings to resurrecting the dead” – he was referring to this. This, specifically, is the perfect <i>Chassidut</i> that follows holiness and leads to the Holy Spirit. Because he totally cleaves to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, he will merit to attain the revelation of the secrets of Torah and to prophesy about the future. This is as Rabbi Meir said,<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Pirkei Avot 6:1</i> “Whosoever is occupied in Torah for the sake of its name (that is, for its sake, rather than for his own sake) merits many things. Moreover, the existence of the whole world is worthwhile because of him. He is called friend, beloved, a lover of God, a lover of the creatures, the delight of God and the delight of the creatures. The Torah garbs him in humility and awe. It prepares him to be a <i>Tzaddik</i>, a <i>Chassid</i>, upright and trustworthy. It distances him from sin and brings him close to merit. He benefits others with counsel and wisdom, understanding and strength, as it says,<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 8:14</i> ‘Mine is counsel and wisdom; I am understanding, strength is mine.’ The Torah gives him kingship, governance and penetrating judgment. The secrets of the Torah are revealed to him. He becomes like an overflowing spring and like an ever-flowing river. He becomes modest, long-suffering and forgiving of insults. The Torah magnifies him and elevates him above all things.” Moreover, when Rabbi Meir said, “For its name (<i>Lishmah</i>-לשמה),” he meant for the “Name” of the Torah, in that it is the Torah of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, that is, the name of the Holy One, blessed is He, in that the entire Torah is composed of the names and titles of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, the Holy One, blessed is He.<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Mishpatim 124a; Zoharei Chamah there; Ramban’s introduction to his commentary to Torah; Also see Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem is One, as well as Shaarei Orah of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, and elsewhere.</i>

Shaar 4

Gate Four
<b>The detailed explanation of the level of <i>Tzaddik</i></b>
To be a <i>Tzaddik</i>, (that is, someone who successfully battles his evil inclination-<i>Yetzer HaRa</i> and keeps it in check), one must be zealous in fulfilling all the <i>mitzvot</i> that apply in our times, with all his might. Now, since there are several opinions regarding how to enumerate the 613 <i>mitzvot</i>, I will present them first according to Rambam (Maimonides), of blessed memory. Following this I will present additional <i>mitzvot</i> according to the count of other Torah authorities and the <i>Zohar,</i> including the enumeration of the positive <i>mitzvot</i> of the Torah, as well as the positive <i>mitzvot</i> of the Scribes. These will be divided into five sections:
1) <i>Mitzvot</i> that are applicable during the prayers of the regular weekdays. 2) <i>Mitzvot</i> that are dependent on time-factors. 3) <i>Mitzvot</i> that are applicable when the opportunity arises. 4) <i>Mitzvot</i> that a person must pursue to fulfill them. 5) <i>Mitzvot</i> that are not within a person’s ability to pursue. Rather, the Holy One, blessed is he, brings about the opportunity to fulfill them. They are as follows:
1) To realize <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה existence<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer HaMitzvoth, positive mitzvah 1</i> when reciting the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:4 – The <i>Shema Yisroel</i>.</i> “Listen Israel, <i>HaShem</i>יהו"ה- is our God;” to realize <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה unity when completing the verse with the words, “<i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה is One;”<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 2</i> to put fringes (<i>Tzitzit</i>) upon a four-cornered garment and to wrap oneself in it;<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 14</i> to don the head <i>Tefillin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 12</i> according to the opinions of Rashi, Rabbeinu Tam, Shimoosha Rabba [and Raavad], to don the arm <i>Tefillin</i> in like manner;<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 13</i> to recite the <i>Shema Yisrael</i> twice daily;<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos mitzvah 10</i> to pray the <i>Amidah</i> prayer every day; to remember what <i>Amalek</i> did to us every day when answering, “<i>Amen, Yehei Shmei Rabbah</i>” during <i>Kaddish</i> and when reciting,<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">In the blessings of the <i>Shema</i> recital</i> “Draw us close to Your Great Name, [<i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה] our King,” as scripture says,<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 17:16</i> “For a hand is [raised in oath] by the throne of God, ‘<i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה will wage war against <i>Amalek</i> from generation to generation;’”<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 189</i> to confess every day<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 73</i> after the <i>Amidah</i> prayer and during the prayer of, “<i>Shema Koleinu</i>;” and that the <i>Cohanim</i> should bless the congregation of Israel every day.<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Ibid. pos. mitzvah 26</i>

The following <i>mitzvot</i> are of Rabbinic origin:
Lighting the Shabbat candles;<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 25b; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Shabbat 5:1</i> lighting the Chanukah lights;<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 21b; Mishneh Torah, Megillah v’Chanukah 3:3; </i> hearing the reading of the book of Esther;<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Megillah 3a; Mishneh Torah, Megillah v’Chanukah 1:1</i> washing one’s hands when waking from sleep and before meals;<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 60b; Shabbat 108b; Chullin 106a; Mishneh Torah, Brachot Ch. 6.</i> the laws of enclosures (<i>Eruvin</i>),<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Tracate Eruvin; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Eruvin</i> including enclosures of courtyards (<i>Eiruv Chatzeirot</i>)<i>,</i> enclosures of localities on Shabbat for the purpose of a <i>mitzvah</i> (<i>Eiruv Techumin</i>)<i>,</i> enclosures for the purpose of cooking on a holiday for Shabbat (<i>Eiruv Tavshilin</i>)<i>,</i> enclosures between alleyways (<i>Shitoophei Mevouoth</i>); The four fast days<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Tractate Ta’anit</i> of the 17th of Tammuz, the 9th of Av, the 3rd of Tishrei, the 10th of Tevet, as well as the fast of Esther, and fasting on special decreed fast days of public emergency.<sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">The seventh mitzvah of Rabbinical origin is the recitation of blessings on things from which one derives benefit (Birchat HaNehenin), which is mentioned later in Part Three, Gate Eight. See Talmud Bavli, Brachot 35a; Menachot 43b and elsewhere.</i>
The following are Torah <i>mitzvoth</i> according to other Torah authorities and according to the Holy Zohar:
To recall the exodus from Egypt while reciting the verses about <i>Tzitzit</i> day and night;<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 12b; Exodus 13:3; Deuteronomy 16:3</i> to remember the Shabbat day every day;<sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 20:7</i> to remember the day of the giving of the Torah;<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 4:9</i> to remember that we angered <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה in the desert;<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 9:7</i> to remember the incident involving Miriam;<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 24:9</i> to make a special blessing before reading the Torah;<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 21a</i> to look upon the <i>Tzitzit</i> while reciting “and you shall look upon it;”<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 15:39; Talmud Bavli, Brachot 12b; Menachot 43b</i> to fully repent;<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah</i> to have fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה when reciting the order of the sacrifices in the morning and when reciting the <i>Pesookei D’Zimra</i> which follow them; to love <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה during the blessing of “An eternal love etc.,”<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">In the liturgy of the blessings of the Shema</i> and during the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:5, the first paragraph of the Shema recital</i> “And you shall love <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה your God” etc., to bless Him with “<i>Yishtabach</i>” and in “<i>Yotzer Ohr</i>” and in “<i>Yotzer HaMeorot</i>” and during the seven blessings that accompany the “<i>Shema</i>” morning and evening; to sanctify <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה name by potentially giving over one’s soul unto death when reciting the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:4, the Shema</i> “Listen Israel, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה is our G-d, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה is one;” to sanctify His name when reciting “<i>Nakdeeshach</i>;” to give one’s soul over unto death and to adhere to Him when reciting the verse, “To You <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, I give over my soul;”<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 200b, 202b; Zohar III 120b – The Nefilat Apayim prayer</i> to know that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה is God when reciting the verse, “<i>Shema</i> <i>Yisroel</i> – Listen Israel, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is our God, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is one,” to delight on Shabbat;<sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 118a; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Shabbat Ch. 30</i> to do the <i>Havdalah</i> ceremony at the end of the Holidays, to say the <i>Hallel</i> prayers at their specific times; to swear in His Name to fulfill a mitzvah; to recite special blessings when enjoying anything of the world;<sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 35a</i> to afflict oneself with the five afflictions of the day of atonement-<i>Yom Kippur</i>;<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Yoma 8:1; Taanit 1:6; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Shevitat Asor 1</i> to burn the leavening on the 14th day of Nissan;<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Pesachim 2:1</i> to honor those who are advanced in years or in wisdom;<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 19:32; Talmud Bavli, Kiddushin 32b and on; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Talmud Torah, Ch. 6; Sefer HaMitzvot pos. mitzvah 209; Zohar HaRakia, pos. mitzvah 24</i> to be modest in the lavatory;<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 57; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot, 5:6</i> to praise Divine justice on all occasions;<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Gadol pos. mitzvah 17; Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 5</i> to give offerings to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה from the choicest of our goods; to build a house of prayer;<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Tefilah 11:1</i> to destroy the name of idolatry,<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Avoda Zarah 7:1</i> to only mention them for disgrace, to chop down an <i>Asherah</i> grove,<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 39</i> to burn an <i>Asherah</i> grove,<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 40</i> to break their idols,<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 38</i> to destroy their high places,<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 41</i> to destroy their alters,<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 42</i> to destroy instruments used for idolatry;<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 43</i> to separate from one’s wife before her menstrual period;<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Niddah 63b; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Issurei Bi’ah 4:12</i> to refrain from marital relations during her menstrual period;<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Issurei Bi’ah 4</i> to have awe and fear of Torah scholars;<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 22b; Bechorot 6b; Bava Kamma 41b; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Talmud Torah 5:1; Sefer HaYirah 200 and elsewhere. </i> to circumcise one’s heart;<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 10:16; Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 9</i> to love being rebuked;<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Tamid 28a; Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 9</i> to go beyond the letter of the law in keeping the <i>mitzvot</i>;<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Metziya 30b; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah 5:11; Hilchot De’ot 1:5</i> to walk wholeheartedly with <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה your God, and not go in the ways of the Chaldeans;<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 18:13; Sefer Mitzvot Katan, pos. mitzvah 10</i> to love one’s fellow Jew;<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 19:18; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot 6:3; Sefer HaMitzvot pos. mitzvah 206; Sefer Mitzvot Gadol pos. mitzvah 9; Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 8 and elsewhere.</i> especially to always judge others favorably even when they are not before you;<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:6; Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 127b; Sifra Kedoshim Ch. 4; Orchot Tzaddikim 25</i> to try to make peace between people;<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Pe’ah 1:1; Avot 1:12; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot 5:7</i> to give charity to the poor;<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 25:36; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Matnot Aniyim 7:1</i> To return any fixed interest charged to a Jew;<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Malveh v’Loveh 4:6-7</i> to fulfill the laws that relate to saving a life and the perpetuation of life;<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah 5:1 and elsewhere.</i> to annul the vows of one’s wife and children;<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Nedarim 3; Tur and Shulchan Aruch 341 and elsewhere.</i> to instruct, render, and teach Torah law;<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Talmud Torah 4-5</i> that a judge must fulfill the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 23:7</i> “Distance yourself from a false word;”<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer HaMitzvot neg. mitzvah 281; Sefer Yereim 235</i> to render proper Torah judgments in the laws that govern partnerships, divisions of land and inheritances, and all other types of legal claims and suits.
The following positive <i>mitzvot</i> are of rabbinical origin:
To make vessels kosher through boiling them;<sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan, pos. mitzvah 198</i> to ritually immerse new vessels in a ritual bath (<i>Mikvah</i>);<sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan, pos. mitzvah 199</i> to search for any leavened bread (<i>Chametz</i>) on the night of the fourteenth of Nissan;<sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Chametz u’Matzah 2:3</i> to eat the bitter herb (<i>Maror</i>) on the first night of Passover;<sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Chametz u’Matzah 7:12</i> to recite blessings on all the <i>mitzvot</i>, and to bless <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, for all the miracles and occurrences that happen to him;<sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Katan pos. mitzvah 150</i> to read from the Torah scroll at the times that were affixed by Moshe, peace be upon him, on the Shabbat and festivals etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">256</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Kamma 82a</i>

Shaar 5

Gate Five
<b>The Level of a Chassid</b>
In explanation of matters that are constant, are very important and need great caution, as clarified from the words of our sages of blessed memory, in Talmud, Midrash, in the Tractate on fear of sin (<i>Yirat Cheit</i>), the Tractate on upright behavior (<i>Derech Eretz</i>) and in Zohar: It was explained in previous chapters that there are three levels:
1) The acquisition of good character traits in one’s elemental soul until they become completely natural to him. 2) Desisting from the evil of the 365 negative <i>mitzvot</i>, in the intellectual soul. 3) Fulfilling the 248 positive <i>mitzvot</i> that are called, “Do good.”<sup class="footnote-marker">257</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 34:15 – “Turn away from evil, and do good (סור מרע ועשה טוב).”</i> Now, there also is an intermediate level, which is the acquisition of character traits that are close to desisting from doing the negative commandments. These are gleaned from the words of the Prophets and the words of Scripture.
A) Character traits that are particularly serious and despicable, which obstruct a Jew from cleaving to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He, are arrogance, anger, impatience, depression, hatred, jealousy, lust, covetousness, lording over others, seeking honor, and boasting. Their opposites are lowliness to the endth degree, to never become angered even with members of your household, to never be pedantic and demanding of others, to be insulted without returning insults, to always be happy even in times of trouble, to love everyone including non-Jews, to not be jealous over anything, since after all, our days on earth are like a passing shadow, to despise all the vanities of this world, to live a life of Torah and <i>mitzvot</i> even if it means eating bread with salt and only drinking water, not to desire any of the vanities of this world, to flee from a position of power, which puts a person into an early grave. Also, do not be demonstrative of your righteousness, for by doing so, not only will you lose your reward in the coming world, but you also will be punished over it in purgatory.
B) Desisting from forbidden character traits. These are speaking badly of others, gossiping, embarrassing others, calling your fellow by a negative nickname, mockery, speaking lies, flattery, deceit, idle chatter, pointing out a person’s faults to others, delighting in the downfall of others, causing strife amongst brothers, profiting from the honor of the Torah, and looking at nakedness.
C) Desisting from committing severe negative <i>mitzvot</i> that are accompanied by the cutting off of the soul, death by the hands of heaven or death by the hands of the earthly court. Of these, profaning the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה is the worst of all. It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">258</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 32:22</i> “You shall be clean to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה and to Israel,” specifically clean of marital relations with a menstruating woman or any type of physical closeness to her. Keeping Shabbat with all its details, cleaning the forbidden sinews and fats from meat, avoiding seminal emission, even involuntary emission, not making use of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה holy names, for whosoever who makes use of the crown will be destroyed, not to disgrace a Torah scholar, for a person such as this is called a heretic (“Apikorus”), to desist from incriminating and slandering others, especially to non-Jews. Other severe prohibitions are swearing in the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, even about the truth, false testimony and any type of oath, and desisting from eating any forbidden food.
D) Fulfilling the positive <i>mitzvot</i> of Tzitzit, Tefillin, reciting the Shema twice daily, honoring the Shabbat in all its details, circumcision of male offspring, doing acts of lovingkindness, visiting the sick, welcoming guests into your home, bringing peace between people, praying the Amidah prayer with complete focus and joy, bringing merit to those who are unmeritorious, conducting one’s business affairs honestly, giving charity to the poor, giving charity in an unpretentious and hidden manner, and setting of times for the study of Torah day and night, for the study of Torah is commensurate to them all.
E) Fulfilling Torah customs; reciting the Shema before retiring to bed at night, rising at midnight to mourn for the exile of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>) and the destruction of the Holy Temple in Jerusalem and to be occupied in the study of Torah until dawn, the fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה should always be upon your face and keep you far from sin, know <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה in all your ways, your soul should always cleave to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He, without stopping for even a moment.

Shaar 6

Gate Six
<b>A short summary of everything that was mentioned in the previous gates, within which the order of conduct of a Chassid is briefly explained in all his deeds throughout the days of his life, so that he will not stumble</b>
Now my son, listen to my voice in all that I instruct you. Prepare yourself to greet your God, Israel. Every night before going to sleep remember that sleep is a foretaste of death and remind yourself of the great and true death.<sup class="footnote-marker">259</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 4b, 5a, 57b and elsewhere.</i> Contemplate all your deeds of that day. If any were bad, confess them before <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, as is the custom of all who are sentenced to death.
During the recital of Shema before going to sleep, accept the yoke of heaven upon yourself so that your soul will be uplifted to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He, with the word One-<i>Echad</i>-אחד. After this, put your soul into His hand, blessed is He, with the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">260</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 31:6</i> “I place my spirit into Your hands.” This is similar to true death, about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">261</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 12:7</i> “And the spirit returns to God etc.” However, since sleep is just a foretaste of true death, give your soul over to Him as a temporary deposit, with the understanding that in the morning it will be returned to you revitalized and refreshed. Then, with fear and trepidation, lay down on your bed, for now your spirit will ascend to give an accounting of all your deeds, words and thoughts during that day, before the Creator, blessed is He and blessed is His Name. Then quiet your heart and mind from thinking idle thoughts until you fall asleep in fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He.
When you wake up for the midnight prayers (<i>Tikkun</i> <i>Chatzot</i>) be as light as an eagle to rise quickly from your bed. Properly wash your hands to remove the spirit of impurity from your flesh. Bless and praise <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He, for although you are guilty of many sins, in His faithfulness He did not delay your spirit from returning to you. Be thankful that it was not real death, but that instead, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה returned your soul to a lifeless body, renewed and refreshed with new vigor and energy.
Moreover, do not be unappreciative of all this, but instead, agonize over the exile of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Indwelling Presence and the destruction of His Holy Sanctuary. For your sins and the sins of your forefathers caused all this, and as of yet, His Indwelling Presence (<i>Shechinah</i>) is still in her fallen state. Nevertheless, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה paid no heed to your evil deeds and though you went to bed tired and weary, He returned your soul renewed and invigorated. Moreover, through mourning for the exile of the <i>Shechinah</i> you will merit beholding the redemption of Zion, along with all those who mourn for her. After this, if you are able, occupy yourself with the study of the oral Torah until dawn. Through this you draw down influence upon the <i>Shechinah</i> and strengthen her from her great fall.
At dawn, run to the house of prayer to receive the <i>Shechinah</i> - the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, for she has already preceded you there to listen to your prayers that she be uplifted and returned to Zion, where she formally was. Moreover, even though you cannot accomplish this singlehandedly, nonetheless, you actually help in uplifting her to some degree. As recompense, she will listen to your prayer and fulfill your requests for goodness. Therefore, my son, when you pray, do so with joy and align your thoughts to <i>HaShem’s-</i>יהו"ה Supernal intent. When you pray, your intention should be for the <i>Shechinah</i> to be uplifted and to do a kindness to your Maker, rather than merely praying for your own needs, and then the prayers for your needs become like the request of a servant who has no source of livelihood other than from his master. 
If you truly call out to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, He too will be close to you, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">262</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:18</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה is close to all who call Him, to all who call Him in truth,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">263</sup><i class="footnote">Chronicles I 28:9</i> “For <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה seeks all hearts and He understands the inclination of all thoughts and knows all who take refuge in Him. If you seek Him, He will be found by you.”
This is particularly so when you confess your sins before Him after the <i>Amidah</i> prayer, or if you say the blessing, “Who listens to prayer” of the <i>Amidah</i> prayer with all your heart, with the resolve to never revert to sin. For <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה knows all hidden and revealed matters. He beholds the kidneys and the heart. Likewise, during the <i>Nefilat Apayim</i> prayer, when you reach the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 25:1</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, I give my soul over to You,” resolve with all your heart to sacrifice yourself unto death, if necessary, for the sake of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Torah and <i>mitzvot</i>. On condition that your mouth and heart are truly one, all your sins will be forgiven.
After concluding your prayers, go from strength to strength by establishing set times to study the Torah of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה for the sake of its Name (particularly right after the morning prayers). Do not change or postpone these set times under any circumstances. Afterwards, eat your meal of bread with salt and a measure of water, for,<sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 13:25</i> “a Tzaddik eats to satisfy his soul,” that is, just enough to maintain his health. This too, should be done for the sake of heaven, to have the strength to properly serve <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 3:6</i> “In all your ways, know Him.”<sup class="footnote-marker">267</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot, Ch. 3</i> Approach your table, which is compared to an altar, with awe, for you are eating at the table of the King.
Now, so that your table will be an altar that atones for your sins, eat little and thereby weaken the power of the external husk of the food that nourishes you, and while eating, occupy yourself in Torah by learning a Mishnah or a Psalm. Through this, your table will be declared to be an altar to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He,<sup class="footnote-marker">268</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 153b</i> as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">269</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 41:22</i> “This table is in the presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה.” This weakens your evil inclination, whereas your intellectual soul becomes strengthened and nourished by your Torah study.
After you finish your meal and have been physically and spiritually nourished through eating and studying, do not be unappreciative.
