Bless <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה for all the goodness He has sustained you with, by reciting the blessings after meals with great joy, like a person who has just received a precious gift,<sup class="footnote-marker">270</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 218</i> as we say in the blessing,<sup class="footnote-marker">271</sup><i class="footnote">In the grace after meals (Birkhat HaMazon)</i> “for the Torah that you taught us and for the consumption of food that you sustain us with.” In the merit of doing this, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה will open His treasury of goodness<sup class="footnote-marker">272</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 28:12 </i> to you and will sustain you always.
After this, see to either doing a new <i>mitzvah</i>, in order to perfect the 248 organs of your soul, or do an old <i>mitzvah</i> to add to your merit before the Holy One, blessed is He. After this, go to your occupation or business, and conduct them faithfully and honestly, without deceit or price gouging. Do not approach your business affairs with the intent of becoming wealthy, but rather, to meet your physical needs. Make your study of Torah essential and your business affairs non-essential,<sup class="footnote-marker">273</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:15; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Talmud Torah, 3:7</i> for as Torah tells us regarding the manna,<sup class="footnote-marker">274</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 16:18</i> “The one who gathered more had no leftovers and the one who gathered less had no lacking; each person gathered according to his eating needs.”
Also, never accept gifts, for whosoever despises receiving gifts will live,<sup class="footnote-marker">275</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 15:27</i> for it is <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה who impoverishes or gives wealth.<sup class="footnote-marker">276</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 2:7</i> It is He who gives you the strength to accomplish.<sup class="footnote-marker">277</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 8:18</i> Therefore, cast your needs upon <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה with all your heart and He will sustain you.<sup class="footnote-marker">278</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 55:23</i> May the fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He, be upon your face, so as not to commit any of the 365 Torah prohibitions.<sup class="footnote-marker">279</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yere’im 352</i> Take particular care not to fall into bad character traits, which are like sourdough<sup class="footnote-marker">280</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 17a</i> that causes physicality to rise, especially those bad character traits that are readily found and therefore trampled upon.<sup class="footnote-marker">281</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 18a; Rashi to Deuteronomy 7:12</i>
<b>Matters that should be avoided in the extreme</b>
Beware of every kind of anger, pedantry and arrogance, even in relation to the members of your household. If someone insults you do not answer him. Rather, when insulted, do not respond in kind, for about this it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">282</sup><i class="footnote">Judges 5:31</i> “Those who love Him are like the sun coming out in its full strength.” Pass over your feelings towards whoever sinned against you and do not be anguished over it, even in your heart, because, in actuality, it is for your good, in that whosoever passes over his feelings, all his intentional sins are likewise passed over,<sup class="footnote-marker">283</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i> and this certainly also applies to unintentional sins. On the contrary, it would be wise to seek out someone who causes you anguish, for by doing so you seek life.
Greet every person with joy, even if he hates you, for by doing so, he will be transformed into your friend and this will be to your merit. Let all your words be calm and speak in a low voice, lest you enter into the domain of anger. Rid your heart of sorrow and worry and thus remove negativity from yourself, for negativity is a trap that removes the Holy Spirit from being upon you. Moreover, flee from a position of power, for it shortens one’s life.
Distance yourself from idle chatter, falsehood, flattery, jesting and speaking badly of others (<i>Lashon</i> <i>HaRa</i>), for whoever engages in these will not greet the face of the <i>Shechinah</i> – the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה – in the coming world. Rather, take hold of humility, which brings one to receiving the Holy Spirit and be like a threshold that is stepped on by young and old. Block your ears from listening to gossip, the evil tongue and idle chatter, and make yourself like a deaf person who cannot hear.<sup class="footnote-marker">284</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 42:19; Psalms 38:14</i> Moreover, make yourself as if you are mute<sup class="footnote-marker">285</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 38:14</i> and do not speak except in matters of Torah, <i>mitzvot</i> and necessary business matters. Greet everyone with a smile and soft words. Do not boast about your good deeds to others, for by doing so you lose the reward and moreover, you will be punished for boasting.
Be very careful with the afternoon prayers, for Eliyahu the prophet was specifically answered in the afternoon prayers.<sup class="footnote-marker">286</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 6b</i> Moreover, it is a time of complete judgment, because at noon, the day begins to wane and the shadows of evening begin to form.<sup class="footnote-marker">287</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 95b; Zohar II 36b </i> Be even more careful with the evening prayers, when darkness already covers the earth and all the destructive forces awaken and are arrayed against the body and soul of man, when it ascends in sleep, to give an accounting before its Creator, blessed is He.
Also keep to the additional matters that I already have included in the fifth Gate. For the sake of brevity, I have not repeated them here.
We now will prepare a general remedy, comprising of three things that save a person from all maladies of the soul. This is because there are three things that cause a person to stray and damage his soul. 1) Physicality causes a person to forget goodness and brings him to sin. 2) He has it in his heart to seek pleasure in life as long as he can. 3) Even if he sets his heart to remember goodness, he could be beset with worry about providing for his physical needs throughout the seventy years of his physical life. This is actually worse than the two above-mentioned matters.
Therefore, my son, do the following and save yourself from these three transgressions of Israel: To combat the first problem, always think deeply whether you should do or speak even the smallest thing or whether you should desist from doing so, for regret is the produce of rushing into something, and once a word is said or a deed is done, there is no taking it back.
To combat the second problem, place the fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה before you. Let not the fear of the day of death pass from your eyes, when you will go down into the grave and become the food of worms and maggots and suffer decomposition and the judgment of purgatory, nor should you forget the great and awesome day of judgment for all mankind, which even Samuel the prophet, who is equated to both Moshe and Aharon, was fearful of.<sup class="footnote-marker">288</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 4b</i>
To combat the third problem, acquire the quality of true trust in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, for <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה sees all man’s ways and recompenses him accordingly. Moreover, man’s actions and schemes are ineffectual in this, for “the race is not won by the swift.”<sup class="footnote-marker">289</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 9:11</i> Rather, give your needs over to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, as we say,<sup class="footnote-marker">290</sup><i class="footnote">In the Rosh HaShanah liturgy</i> “Happy is the man who does not forget You, and a person who strengthens in You, for those who seek You will never falter and those who find shelter in You will never be shamed.”
Until this point, we have provided explanations on how a person should conduct himself to be a Tzaddik or a Chassid. From this point on, we will engage in matters of rebuke that bring one to submission to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, blessed is He, and the consequences of persisting on the wrong path, as well as the bountiful reward for greatly desiring <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Torah and <i>mitzvot</i>.

Part 2





Shaar 1

Part Two
Gate One
<b>Words of Rebuke</b>
Now, son of man, open your eyes from your blindness and realize that all the pleasures and goodness of this world are vanity and error.<sup class="footnote-marker">291</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 10:15</i> Why be prideful over others? If you are proud of your tall and upright stature, others too were created in the image of God, just like you. If you are proud of your family lineage, are we not all the children of one man and are not all Jews children of Avraham, Yitzchak and Yaakov? If you are proud of your wealth, are there not many empty-headed and reckless people who are wealthier than you? Moreover, it is <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה who impoverishes and enriches.<sup class="footnote-marker">292</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 2:7</i> Therefore, if you are wealthy, do not glorify in your wealth,<sup class="footnote-marker">293</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 9:22</i> for it could be wealth kept for its possessor to his detriment.
If you are proud of your authority and honor over others, are there not many despicable people who have power over others in this world, as proverbs states,<sup class="footnote-marker">294</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 30:21</i> “because of a slave who reigns.” Furthermore, wealth and honor are in <i>HaShem’s-</i>יהו"ה control<sup class="footnote-marker">295</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 3:16</i> and He brings the haughty down to the ground.<sup class="footnote-marker">296</sup><i class="footnote">Liturgy of the morning blessings of the Shema recital.</i> If you are proud of your intelligence, there were many people who were more intelligent than you, such as Doeg, Achitophel and Yeravam, who lost their lives, both in this world and the coming world. For it is in <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה power to distort the utterances of the trustworthy and take reason away from the elders.<sup class="footnote-marker">297</sup><i class="footnote">Job 12:20</i> Therefore, let not the wise glory in his wisdom,<sup class="footnote-marker">298</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 9:22</i> for how can you be haughty if from your very inception you were born of a putrid drop,<sup class="footnote-marker">299</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:1</i> and you entered and exited by way the birth canal.
Moreover, during your lifetime you are shameful and disgraceful, and in death, you are worms and maggots,<sup class="footnote-marker">300</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:1 ibid.</i> for from dust you came and to dust you shall return<sup class="footnote-marker">301</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 3:19</i> and will be as if you never were. How then can you be angered at others, but not at yourself, being that by your anger you destroy your very soul and serve idolatry, thus angering your Maker who will exact punishment from you.
How then can a person place importance on the vanities of this world when his end is to perish. “The spirit passes over him and he is gone, and his place no longer recognizes him,”<sup class="footnote-marker">302</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 103:16</i> “and whoever has seen him will say, ‘where is he?’”<sup class="footnote-marker">303</sup><i class="footnote">Job 20:7</i> Why then, will you be saddened at the loss of a world that is not yours, but are not saddened about the departure of your soul from your body with trembling, quaking, sudden fear and great darkness falling upon you?<sup class="footnote-marker">304</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 15:12</i>
Why do you lust for material wealth, in amassing gold and building great houses and storerooms, for in the end, you will be carried to the grave emptyhanded and all your wealth will be left in the hands of others? Why then do you labor so greatly to amass wealth, when in reality, it all depends on <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה Divine providence, even a Torah scroll in the sanctuary?<sup class="footnote-marker">305</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 134a</i> Why are you concerned with a world that is not yours, for in the blink of an eye, you will be transported to a different world? Then all your efforts will be as nothing, because all your energy was spent in acquiring worthless vanity and nothingness. Why do you reject the Torah of eternal life for the sake of amassing the possessions of transient life? For everything that God has decreed upon you, whether for poverty or for wealth, cannot be added to nor subtracted from, for it is <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה who impoverishes and enriches.<sup class="footnote-marker">306</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 2:7</i> You thus lose your eternal life, without having accomplished even half of what you lusted for, but tomorrow you will lay in the dust. Maggots will be beneath you and worms will cover you. Why then do you seek power and high position when the hope of man is maggots?
Moreover, one kingdom does not overlap another kingdom even by a hairsbreadth, for kingship is <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה.<sup class="footnote-marker">307</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 22:29, 145:13</i> It is in His power to strengthen and make great. It is He who lowers one person and elevates another. How then can you speak wickedly of your fellow, who is better than you, when there are many accusing angels who tell of your wickedness and point out your sins before He who spoke and the world was?
Why do you hate your enemy, when in reality you have no greater enemy than yourself, in that you bring evil upon yourself by oppressing and damaging your eternal soul and pleasuring your body, which is nothing but a clump of earth that is here today and gone tomorrow? Why do you love your true enemy, the evil inclination-<i>Yetzter HaRa</i> that is within you, though he seeks your downfall and desires to kill you? You are like a bird hurrying to the trap, unaware that it’s life will be lost as the arrow splits it liver!<sup class="footnote-marker">308</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 7:23</i>
Why do you flatter one such as you, born of woman, and are embarrassed from him, but are not embarrassed before the great and awesome King who is the judge over all, and whose glory fills the earth? The souls of all living creatures are in His hands and from His abode He supervises all who dwell on earth. Why do you sin in secrecy though all your deeds and words are recorded in the book? For <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה eyes scan all the ways of man on earth. He takes account of all your steps and will bring you to judgment over every hidden thing.<sup class="footnote-marker">309</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 12:14</i> Why would you waste your time on things that exist today but are gone tomorrow, for the span of your life is short. When will you prepare for your eternal abode if you are preoccupied by these things, for as known, whosoever does not toil on the eve of Shabbat will not eat on Shabbat.<sup class="footnote-marker">310</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud, Avodah Zara 3a</i>
Look and see how many people died in their youth and how many miscarriages and suckling infants passed away and were cut off from life, like a stalk whose produce is cut off. No man knows his appointed time, when he will die and his name will be lost from the world. If so, how can you forget the day of death, the judgment of purgatory and the great and awesome day of judgment of the coming future? Who can withhold it, to give you refuge from these? For nothing is as sure as death and no man is saved from the grave. In the end you will groan for the gates of repentance, but they will be locked before you and there will be no remedy for your afflictions and sins.
All this being so, how can your eyes avoid the reality of death when, in fact, it is coiled like a snake around your heel. Every night you lay upon your bed like a corpse, as a reminder of actual death. Death is tied like frontlets between your eyes and like deep slumber upon your eyelids. This knowledge protects you when you sleep, but when you wake up, you look away at all the vanities of the world, at wealth that is not yours, at pleasures that are not yours, at power over others that is not yours, and at a world that is not yours.

Shaar 2

Gate Two
<b>Words of rebuke gleaned from the words of our sages, of blessed memory</b>
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated<sup class="footnote-marker">311</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Vei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 21</i> that a person should always be in a state of fear of Heaven, privately as well as openly. Happy is he who sets all his words and all his ways for the sake of Heaven. Let your eyes and heart always be directed toward your Creator, so that you will be saved from every type of sin and transgression. Let the fear of He who formed you always be upon you, and let the awe of Him be constantly present in your heart and mind, and before your eyes, so that they are never removed from before your eyes for even a moment.
Let the day of death never depart from before your eyes, and the day of your burial and the day of great judgment. It should be for you as if you actually see it, and as if it actually is upon you, as though you are about to enter into judgment, so that thoughts of sin do not even come upon your heart. For, all your limbs shall testify about you, and against your will you will be forced to give an accounting before the King, King of kings, the Holy One, blessed is He.<sup class="footnote-marker">312</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 4:22</i>
Each and every day you should lament to yourself that you did not adequately give charity to Torah scholars or properly study Torah, for every day that has passed shall never be returned to you.
Our sages stated<sup class="footnote-marker">313</sup><i class="footnote">Reishit Chochmah, Shaar HaYirah, Ch. 12</i> that at the time of a person’s passing from this world, the angel of death asks him, “Did you engage in Torah study and acts of kindness? Did you crown your Maker over you every morning and evening? Did you crown your fellows over you as your superiors and with a pleasant spirit?” If he has these qualities, his soul will then depart from his body as with a kiss, but if not etc.
The second judgment is the judgment of the grave. The day of entering the grave is even more arduous than the judgments of purgatory.<sup class="footnote-marker">314</sup><i class="footnote">Mesechet Chibut HaKever 3; Reishit Chochmah ibid.</i> Even the perfectly righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i> who have never sinned are judged by it. What then shall a person do to be saved from the torments of the grave (<i>Chibut HaKever</i>)? He should engage in Torah study, love charity, rebuke, and acts of kindness, and he should welcome Torah scholars and guests into his home, and provide them with delight in his belongings, and he also should pray with devotion. He will then be saved from the torments of the grave and even the judgments of purgatory will not be visited upon him.
The third judgment is the judgment of purgatory. At the time of his judgment, the Holy One, blessed is He, asks him, “Did you engage in Torah study and acts of lovingkindness?” If he has these qualities, he then is exempted from the judgments of purgatory.<sup class="footnote-marker">315</sup><i class="footnote">Mesechet Chibut HaKever 4; Reishit Chochmah ibid.</i> Happy is the man who subjugates himself like an ox to a yoke and like a donkey to a burden,<sup class="footnote-marker">316</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 5b; Tanna d’Bei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 2</i> so that he sits and studies and reviews the words of Torah every day constantly, reading the words of the Torah, the Prophets and the Scriptures, and reviewing the laws and teachings. If he does so, increasing his engagement in Torah study and minimizing his engagement in the pursuit of wealth, the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) will immediately rest upon him.<sup class="footnote-marker">317</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Bei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 2 ibid.</i>
Eliyahu, who is remembered for good, stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">318</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Bei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 9</i> “As the heavens and earth are my witnesses, any man or woman, whether they are Gentile or Jew, even if they are a servant or a maid, the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) will dwell upon each person according to his actions!”<sup class="footnote-marker">319</sup><i class="footnote">Also see the very first Chassidic discourse (Maamar) of the Lubavitcher Rebbe, entitled “Bati LeGani – I have come to My garden,” translated in The Teachings of The Rebbe, 5711, Discourse 1.</i> Happy is he who places all these matters before his face at all times, meriting to perfect himself in these ways all the days of his life, and conducting himself according to these manners throughout his life and with all these deeds. If only he guards himself, keeping his limbs and body far from all sin and transgression, he will merit all the glory that is hidden for the righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i>, glory that is incalculable and beyond measure, such that no physical eye can behold it, and the physical ear is incapable of grasping the great glory that is apportioned to the righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i> and the pious <i>Chassidim</i>. It is about this that the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">320</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 64:3</i> “Such things have never been heard or noted, no eye has seen them God, but You, that which He will do for those who have awaited Him!”

Shaar 3

Gate Three
<b>The reward for fulfilling Torah and Mitzvot</b>
In order that you know the reason for the fulfillment of the <i>mitzvot</i>, as they are founded upon their roots in the manner that I revealed to you in Part One, I will quote what the sages stated in the Book of Repairs (Sefer HaTikkunim), in Tikkun 18,<sup class="footnote-marker">321</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar 32a</i> and in Tikkun 70,<sup class="footnote-marker">322</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar 130b and on. (This gate is a summary of the cited sections of the Tikkunei Zohar in the original Aramaic).</i> and will compile the explanations of their roots and organize them into a very brief summary. They stated as follows:
Every prophet and all human beings are bound to and ascend to the particular [spiritual] limb to which their soul is included and bound. There are those who stem from the head of the King, and there are those who stem from the hairs of the head, some are bound to the eyes, some to the ears, and some to the nose, the mouth, the neck and throat, and the hands. There are those who stem from the stature of the torso which is the body, some from the thighs, from the legs or feet, and some from the organ that is the sign of the covenant,<sup class="footnote-marker">323</sup><i class="footnote">The male reproductive organ</i> some from the brain and some from the heart. Each of these limbs possesses a corresponding known <i>Sefirah</i> of the ten <i>Sefirot</i>, and all these limbs and organs are what is known as the form of the body of the King (<i>Goofa d’Malka</i>). There also are those whose souls stem from the garments (<i>Levushin</i>) of the King.
All six-hundred and thirteen commandments of the Torah are tied to these limbs of the body of the King (<i>Goofa d’Malka</i>). There are <i>mitzvot</i> that are tied to the head of the King, and those that are tied to the eyes etc. For each of the <i>mitzvot</i> that dwell upon each particular limb, there is a known name, and within that name is the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, which is the soul of that limb. All the limbs are called the particular titles (<i>Kinuyim</i>) for the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, for it is He who is within each particular limb.  Each of those names and titles for each of the particular limbs only has dominion over its particular limb. However, the Holy One, blessed is He, whose Name is <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, His rule and dominion is over them all, just as the soul has dominion and rule over all of the particular limbs and organs. About this the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">324</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 6:3</i> “The whole earth is filled with His glory.”
Those commandments that a person fulfills without any ulterior motive of receiving reward,<sup class="footnote-marker">325</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:3</i> are tied to the form of the King in the world of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>. However, those commandments that a person fulfills for the ulterior motive of receiving reward, are tied to the form of he who is called a lad (<i>Na’ar</i>) above in Godliness.
Now, there are also hosts of angels that are bound to each and every limb of the form of the King. There are angels that are called “the eyes of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>,” those who are called “the ears of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>,” and those who are called “the hands of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>” etc. They all are bound to the body of the King (<i>Goofa d’Malka</i>) like the strands of hair that are attached to the head. That is, each strand is a single angel.
The 613 limbs and organs of man are thus all ordered according to the order of the whole of creation, and it is for this reason that man is called a “microcosm of the world” (<i>Olam Katan</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">326</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar 100a, 130b; Also see Sefer HaMashalim of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla (translated as The Book of Allegories 1-4), and elsewhere.</i> With every <i>mitzvah</i> that a person fulfills, he causes the coronation of the Holy One, blessed is He, over that limb or organ of his soul, according to what that particular <i>mitzvah</i> is. The same applies to each particular limb and organ of his soul, each of which are called flames (<i>Neirot-נרות</i>), as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">327</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 20:27</i> “The soul of man is the flame of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>נר יהו״ה</i>,” and it is with that limb that he performs that particular commandment, which likewise is called a flame (<i>Ner-נר</i>), as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">328</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:23</i> “The commandment (<i>mitzvah</i>) is a flame (<i>Ner</i>-<i>נר</i>).”
It is necessary for a person to eradicate all impure and vile thoughts and impurities from each of these limbs and organs. For, they stem from the extraneous husks (<i>Kelipot</i>) which dwell in man. He therefore must repair and prepare the place, to refine and cleanse it, thus making it is a fitting receptacle within which the flame of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> can dwell. For, when any limb or organ becomes blemished through the iniquities and transgressions that a person does, the Holy One blessed is He does not dwell in that limb. This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">329</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 21:18</i> “For any man in whom there is a blemish shall not approach.” Any person who causes blemish to a particular commandment, it is as if he has transgressed against the form and body of the King. A person must therefore burn those external husks (<i>Kelipot</i>) that dwell there in each of those limbs, and must eradicate them from within him. For, those extraneous husks are called sourdough (<i>Se’or</i>), leaven (<i>Chametz</i>), chaff (<i>Motz</i>), and straw (<i>Teven</i>), and he must eradicate them from those flames about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">330</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:23</i> “The commandment (<i>mitzvah</i>) is a flame (<i>Ner</i>-<i>נר</i>),” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">331</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 20:27</i> “The soul of man is the flame of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>נר יהו״ה</i>, Who searches all the chambers of one’s innards.” By doing so, the Holy One, blessed is He, dwells there, meaning, the Name <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, and His titles, which are called His limbs, along with His myriads of camps and troops, which are the angels that are tied to that particular limb, and which guard that particular limb from all evil forces and extraneous husks of <i>Kelipah</i> that were residing there.
Different commandments are tied to different limbs. The commandments of love and fear of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, are dependent upon the brain and the heart.<sup class="footnote-marker">332</sup><i class="footnote">See Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah 2:2</i> All commandments that relate to travel are dependent upon the feet, such as going to the house of prayer, to a circumcision, to perform the <i>mitzvah</i> of burying the dead, and any other travel associated with fulfilling a <i>mitzvah</i>. Similarly, there are commandments that one fulfills by standing upon his feet, such as standing during the <i>Amidah</i> (standing) prayer, which is tied to his two thighs and legs.
The commandment of circumcision (<i>Brit Milah</i>) is bound to the Tzaddik, who is the rainbow and sign of the covenant. The eighteen blessings of the <i>Amidah</i> prayer are tied to the eighteen vertebrae of the spine with which one bows and prostrates, and are bound to the Tzaddik who is called the eighteen worlds and statures of the body that prostrate to the Divine Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, the <i>Shechinah</i>, during prayer.<sup class="footnote-marker">333</sup><i class="footnote">For a lengthier explanation of this, see Kuntres Inyan Tefilah of Rabbi DovBer of Lubavitch, translated as Praying With Passion.</i> That is, they are bound to the Name <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, so that the four corresponding prostrations of the <i>Amidah</i> prayer are bound to the center column. The Tefillin of the hand are bound to the left hand.
All of the commandments that relate to action are bound to the hands, such as giving charity, tying the Tefillin, which utilizes the right hand to tie it onto the left, and acts of righteousness (<i>Tzedakah</i>) to the Holy One, blessed is He. The term for charity and righteousness is <i>Tzedakah</i>-<i>צדקה</i>. The <i>Tzadi</i>-<i>צ-</i>90 of <i>Tzedakah</i>-<i>צדקה</i> refers to the ninety times that a person responds “amen” daily. The <i>Dalet</i>-<i>ד</i>-4 refers to the four sanctifications (<i>Kedusha</i>) that one recites daily. The <i>Kof</i>-<i>ק-</i>100 refers to the 100 blessings that one recites daily. The <i>Hey</i>-<i>ה</i>-5 refers to the five books of the Torah that one should study every day. About this charity and righteousness (<i>Tzedakah</i>-<i>צדקה</i>) Torah states,<sup class="footnote-marker">334</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 15:11</i> “You shall surely open your hand,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">335</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 15:10</i> “You shall surely give,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">336</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 15:14</i> “You shall surely furnish him,” which hints at the ten types of gifts etc.
The Tzitzit are worn on the shoulders. The delight of Shabbat is through eating and drinking, and similarly, the sacrificial offerings (<i>Korbanot</i>) are consumed through the eating and drinking of the Holy One, blessed is He, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">337</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 28:2</i> “My offering, My food.” The prayers that were established corresponding to the sacrificial offerings,<sup class="footnote-marker">338</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 26b</i> and over which one makes a blessing to the Holy One, blessed is He, for all that he eats and drinks, should be consumed after one concludes his prayers and not before, and they all are bound to the neck.
The commandment to study and teach Torah, as well as the recitation of the prayers are all related to the voice and speech, through which one calls out to the Holy One, blessed is He. The same is true of the <i>Shema</i>, which is to be recited twice daily, as well as all the songs, praises, and hymns of thanks to <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, all of which are tied to the mouth. The blowing of the <i>Shofar</i> is tied to the lungs which blow the air and spirit through the mouth, and it is that air and spirit which activates the voice. Likewise, the rendering of all judgments is tied to speech, and also are tied to the eyes, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">339</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 6b</i> “A judge can only render judgment based upon that which his eyes see.”
The sacrificial offerings, which are called<sup class="footnote-marker">340</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 1:9 and elsewhere</i> “a pleasing aroma to <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>,” as well as the aromatic spices over which one makes the Havdalah, are tied to the nose. The recitation of the <i>Shema</i>, the commandment to hear the <i>Shofar</i>, and all other <i>mitzvot</i> about which it states that they must be heard by one’s ears to be fulfilled, are all tied to the ears. The Tefillin are also tied upon the head, and all of the <i>mitzvot</i> are thus intertwined with one another.
In the book of Zohar on Parshat Naso, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">341</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 124a</i> “Even when a person only fulfills a single <i>mitzvah</i> with love and fear of the Holy One, blessed is He, on account of this <i>mitzvah</i> the ten <i>Sefirot</i> dwell upon him. Whoever fulfills even a single <i>mitzvah</i> as fitting, it is as if he has fulfilled all 248 positive <i>mitzvot</i> of the Torah. This is because there is not a single <i>mitzvah</i> that is not intertwined with and includes all two-hundred and forty-eight positive <i>mitzvot</i> within it.”
The reward a person receives for crowning the Holy One, blessed is He, over each of his limbs, is that it is considered as if he crowned the Holy One, blessed is He, over the entire world, for man is called a microcosm of the world. Permission was not granted to reveal the reasons for the commandments-<i>mitzvot</i>, in order that a person should not come to serve <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, for the ulterior motive of receiving reward.<sup class="footnote-marker">342</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:3</i>  Nevertheless, come and see how meritorious is the soul that is rooted in the form of her Master, and fulfills all His commandments. When such a soul ascends, all the hosts of angels ascend with her. For they are all tied to and dependent upon those commandments, fixtures, and camps of the body of the King (<i>Goofa d’Malka</i>). Thus, they all ascend with her and descend with her, and this soul is called the ladder (<i>Sulam</i>) about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">343</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 28:12</i> “There was a ladder set on the ground and its top reached the heavens, and the angels of God were ascending and descending upon it.” When that soul ascends, a voice comes down and proclaims in all the firmaments and to all the hosts and camps that are tied to that soul, “Grant honor to the form of the King.”
Regarding the <i>mitzvah</i> of the covenant of circumcision (<i>Brit Milah</i>), just as he removes all the husks and membranes from that organ, thus fixing it to be an abode for the <i>Shechinah –</i> Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He – so likewise does his soul ascend above to the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה. All extraneous husks are removed from it and all angels of destruction are prevented from approaching him.
Similarly, just as he toils in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of the commandments-<i>mitzvot</i>, which are likened to the light of a candle, this is likewise the case when he goes to that world. About this the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">344</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 13:21</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה went before them by day in a pillar of cloud to lead them on the way, and by night in a pillar of fire to give them light.” The word “them” in the plural, refers to the <i>Neshamah</i>, <i>Ru’ach</i> and <i>Nefesh</i> levels of one’s soul, which are guided by the pillar of cloud and the pillar of fire to lead them on the way and give them light.
Likewise, just as he honored the Shabbat, by resting and delighting in it in honor of the Holy One, blessed is He, so likewise he is granted a place to rest above, and he rests there from all that he toiled in this world.
Whoever unifies the Holy One, blessed is He, with His Indwelling Presence – the <i>Shechinah</i> – the Holy One, blessed is He, likewise unites him with his spouse in that world. Just as man brings the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, close to himself, so likewise, he is brought close to his spouse. Similarly, whoever makes his place of dwelling into a Holy Temple, the Holy One, blessed is He, makes a dwelling place for him in the coming world, which is the Holy of Holies, and this is where he will dwell.
Whoever makes a <i>Sukkah</i> (סוכה) for the Holy One, blessed is He, the Holy One, blessed is He, shelters him in His shade in that world, and when he departs from this world, the Holy One, blessed is He, shelters and protects him from all angels of destruction and from all accusers.
Whoever recites the seven blessings of the <i>Shema</i> recital, sanctifying <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, when he recites “Holy, Holy, Holy is <i>HaShem</i> <i>Tzva’ot</i>-יהו״ה צבאו״ת,” and whoever unifies Him in the <i>Shema</i> recital, he will be blessed and sanctified with ten canopies of Holy matrimony (<i>Kiddushin</i>) in the Garden of Eden, and will be unified with his bride.
When a man wraps himself in the <i>mitzvah</i> of the Tallit, dons Tefillin and calls to the Holy One, blessed is He, in the <i>Shema</i> recital, he affixes a throne for the Holy One, blessed is He, upon which He sits. So likewise, the Holy One, blessed is He, affixes a throne and crown for him in the coming world, granting him the crown of kingship (<i>Keter Malchut</i>), and crowns him as king over all of the angels and ministers there. Just as he brings satisfaction to his Maker with songs, praises, and gratitude, so likewise when his soul ascends above, all the angels that carry the Supernal Chariot (<i>Merkavah</i>) and all the camps of the Chayot, Ophanim and Seraphim angels spread their wings to receive his soul with great delight, rejoicing and song.
In conclusion, it is beyond the capacity of the mouth to express the full extent of his eternal reward in that world, for generation after generation. Happy is he who causes the Holy One, blessed is He, to dwell in all of his limbs and organs. For, even if a person is missing only one limb, in that it is vacant of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו"ה, in that He does not dwell upon it, because of that one limb, he will be required to return to this world and reincarnate until he has perfected all of his limbs and has the full form (<i>Tzelem</i>) of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה. For, even if he only lacks one, he is not in the form of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה.
In conclusion, commensurate to a person’s toil in fulfilling the <i>mitzvot</i> of the Holy One, blessed is He, for the sake of unifying the Holy One, blessed is He, with the <i>Shechinah</i> – His Indwelling Presence – so likewise, the Holy One, blessed is He, will reciprocate measure for measure with him and his spouse in the coming world.

Shaar 4

Gate Four
<b>Regarding the punishments for bad character traits, and the reward for the acquisition of good character traits</b>
<b>Pride</b> is the root of many sins, whether they are between man and <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, the Ever Present One, blessed is He, or whether they are between man and his fellow. In regard to man and his fellow, this is because his arrogance will bring him to harm his fellow, in disdaining him and speak badly of him, amongst many other negative matters. Or whether between man and <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">345</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 8:14</i> “and your heart will become haughty and you will forget <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God.” That is, because of conceit he forgets <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה his God, greatly damaging his relationship with <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, the Ever Present One, blessed is He. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">346</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 5a</i> “Whoever is haughty is called an abomination, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">347</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 16:5</i> ‘Every haughty person is an abomination to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.’” They also stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">348</sup><i class="footnote">Sotah 5a ibid.</i> “Whoever is arrogant should be excommunicated,” and, “it is fitting to hew him down as like an <i>Asherah</i> tree that has been designated for idolatry,” and, “his dust will not stir at the time of the resurrection of the dead,” and, “the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, the <i>Shechinah</i>, wails for him.” Moreover, they stated that a haughty person is equal to an idolater and to one who denies the fundamental principle of existence, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. Moreover, it is as if he transgressed every kind of forbidden relationship, and as if he built a personal altar to idolatry within himself. They further stated that even if, like our forefather Avraham, he attributes the possession of the entire heavens and earth to the Holy One, blessed is He, a haughty person will not be cleansed of the judgements of purgatory (Gehinnom). In the end he will be diminished from his haughty position and will depart from the world before his time.
Even about Yeravam, our Sages taught<sup class="footnote-marker">349</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 101a-b</i> that all the Torah scholars of the generation were like the grass of the field next to him and there were no imperfections his Torah teachings. Moreover, he could expound upon Torah from one-hundred and fifty angles. Nonetheless, he was punished with excision from both this world and the coming world, only because of his arrogance. Our Sages, of blessed memory, stated<sup class="footnote-marker">350</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 43b</i> that it is as if a haughty person pushes away the feet of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, thus causing Him to withdraw from the world, as the Holy One, blessed is He, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">351</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 5a ibid.</i> “He and I cannot dwell together in the world.” 
Such a person rebels against the Kingdom of Heaven by wrapping himself in the <i>Tallit</i> that belongs only to the King, King of kings, the Holy One, blessed is He, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">352</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 93:1</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is King, He is clothed in pride.” After all, what does man have to be proud of? His very existence is from a putrid drop and he was formed in menstrual blood. His lifetime is one of filth and stench and upon his death he is covered with worms and maggots, until his body decays and becomes a pile of dust and his soul descends to hell.
In contrast, there is no greater quality than humility and a sense of lowliness. We learn this<sup class="footnote-marker">353</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Reishit Chochmah, Gate of Humility, Ch. 7</i> from our teacher Moshe, peace be upon him, the father of all the prophets in Torah, <i>mitzvot</i> and fear of sin. Even so, Torah only praised him for his humility, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">354</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 12:3</i> “The man Moshe was exceedingly humble.” Go and learn the quality of humility from the Holy One, blessed is He, who set aside the loftiest heavens to dwell with the despondent and the lowly of spirit, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">355</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 57:15</i> “I abide with exaltedness and in holiness, but I am with the despondent and the lowly of spirit.” Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">356</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 34:19</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is close to the broken hearted and He saves those who are crushed in spirit.” It likewise states,<sup class="footnote-marker">357</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 15:1</i> “Who may sojourn in Your tent? One who is lowly and contemptible in his own eyes.”
Now, although it is true that about fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">358</sup><i class="footnote">Job 28:28</i> “The fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, that is wisdom,” and similarly,<sup class="footnote-marker">359</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 33:6</i> “Fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, that is His treasure,” nevertheless, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">360</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Yerushalmi, Shabbat 1:3; Midrash Tanchuma BeHa’alotcha</i> “What wisdom proclaimed to be the crown of its head, humility made into a heel (<i>Eikev</i>-עקב) for its sandal, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">361</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 22:4 – This verse is usually translated, “The result of humility is fear of HaShem-יהו"ה.”</i> ‘The heel (<i>Eikev</i>-עקב) of humility is fear of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.’”
A person whose opinion of himself is that he is lowly, is as if he has offered all the sacrificial offerings, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">362</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 51:19</i> “The sacrifices that God desires are a broken spirit.” Moreover, his prayer is not despised or rejected, for,<sup class="footnote-marker">363</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 5a</i> “the prayers of a person are heard only if he casts his heart like flesh, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">364</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 66:23</i> ‘It shall be that at every New Moon and on every Shabbat, all flesh shall come and prostrate themselves before Me.’” It similarly is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">365</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 66:2</i> “It is to this that I look, to the poor and broken-spirited.”
Whoever is humble causes the <i>Shechinah</i> – the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה – to dwell upon man on earth, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">366</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 20:18</i> “Moshe approached the thick cloud where God was.” What brought him to this? His humility, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">367</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 12:3</i> “The man Moshe was exceedingly humble.”<sup class="footnote-marker">368</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Reishit Chochmah, Gate of Humility, Ch. 3</i>
It is taught,<sup class="footnote-marker">369</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 20b </i> “Rabbi Pinchas ben Ya’ir would say: “The study of Torah study leads to caution. Caution leads to zeal. Zeal leads to cleanliness from sin. Cleanliness from sin leads to abstinence from indulgence. Abstinence from indulgence leads to purity. Purity leads to separation from worldliness. Separation from worldliness leads to humility etc.”  Moreover, they concluded, “Humility is greatest of all, since it leads to the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>), as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">370</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 61:1</i> ‘The spirit of My Lord <i>HaShem/Elohi”m</i>-אדנ״י יהו״ה is upon me, because <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה has anointed me to bring tidings to the humble.’”
It is related,<sup class="footnote-marker">371</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 88b</i> “They sent a message from there:<sup class="footnote-marker">372</sup><i class="footnote">From the Sanhedrin in Eretz Yisroel</i> Who is destined for the coming world (<i>Olam HaBa</i>)? One who is humble and kneels down, bowing when he enters and bowing when he exits, and reviews the words of Torah constantly without giving credit to himself.”<sup class="footnote-marker">373</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Mishnah Avot 2:8</i> About such a person it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">374</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Megillah 15b; Sanhedrin 101b</i> “In the future, the Holy One, blessed is He, will be a crown on the head of every single righteous man, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">375</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 28:5</i> ‘On that day, <i>HaShem of Hosts-HaShem</i> <i>Tzva’ot</i>-יהו״ה צבאו״ת will be a crown of delight and a diadem of glory.’ One might think this extends to everyone who is righteous. The verse therefore continues, ‘for the remnant of his people,’ meaning, for whoever sees himself as a remnant.”
In Zohar Parshat Shelach it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">376</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 168b</i> “The head of the academy began and said: Happy is he who makes himself small in this world. How great will he be in the coming world! One who is small in his own eyes is great, and one who is great in his own eyes is small!” It similarly states in Zohar Terumah,<sup class="footnote-marker">377</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 166a-b</i> “Why is he called Yechezkel the son of Buzi (בוזי)?<sup class="footnote-marker">378</sup><i class="footnote">The term “Boz-בוז” means “scorn” as in the verse (Song of Songs 8:7), “He would be scorned to the extreme-Boz Yavozu Lo-בוז יבוזו לו.” The Zohar thus negates the implication that the prophet Yechezkel was from a scornful family.</i> Because [for the sake of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה] he was willing to disgrace himself (<i>Mevazeh</i>-מבזה) in relation to those greater than himself and on account of this, he is called, “Son of man-<i>Ben Adam</i>-בן אדם,” a term indicating his perfection over all others of his generation. He thus is also called “exalted-<i>Ram</i>-רם,” as it states [about Elihu],<sup class="footnote-marker">379</sup><i class="footnote">Job 32:2</i> “The son of Barachel, the Buzi (הבוזי) from the house of Ram (רם),” indicating his greatness over everyone because of his great humility.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">380</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Taanit 7a</i> “Why are the words of Torah compared to water? To teach us that just as water comes from a high place and only descends to a lower place, so too, Torah only dwells upon one who is lowly of spirit.” Happy is the man who does not become agitated and whose spirit is very lowly and humble, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">381</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 51:19</i> “The sacrifices that God desires are a broken spirit.” Happy is the man who is long-patient and bears everything for the will of his Creator, and who makes himself like a remnant, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">382</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:18</i> “Who is a God like You, pardoning iniquity and overlooking transgression for the remnant of His heritage,” meaning, for whoever sees himself as a remnant. Happy is the man who makes himself like the dust that is trampled by everyone, who is like the lower stoop that is stepped on by all, and like the lowest peg upon which all depend.

<b>Anger</b> is a branch of pride and is equal to it. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">383</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Nedarim 22a</i> “Whoever is angry, all kinds of punishments of purgatory (Gehinnom) rule over him.” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">384</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 105b</i> “A person who rends his garments in anger, or breaks his vessels in anger, or scatters his money in his anger, should be regarded like an idolator in your eyes, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">385</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 81:10</i> ‘You shall not have an alien god within you.’”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">386</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Nedarim 22b</i> “Whoever is angry, indicates that he has no thought of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו״ה Indwelling Presence (the <i>Shechinah</i>) and he forgets his Torah learning and increases in folly. Moreover, it is known that his sins are more numerous than his merits, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">387</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 29:22</i> ‘A man of wrath is full of iniquity.’” Our sages, of blessed memory, similarly stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">388</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 66b</i> “Anyone who becomes angry; if he is a scholar, his wisdom departs from him, as we learn from Moshe and Elisha.” Likewise, Eliyahu who is remembered for good, told Rabbi Yehudah,<sup class="footnote-marker">389</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 29b</i> “Do not get angry and you will not sin.”
Similarly, Zohar states in Parshat Tetzaveh,<sup class="footnote-marker">390</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 182a-b</i> “An angry person uproots his holy soul and replaces it with the opposite of holiness (<i>Sitra Achara</i>). Such a person rebels against his Maker and it is forbidden to come close and attach oneself to him. About him the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">391</sup><i class="footnote">Job 18:4</i> ‘You who rips your soul apart in your anger,’ and he causes an alien god to dwell within him. Such a person is considered as if he built a personal altar to idolatry within himself, and therefore, whoever adheres to him, it is considered as if he has attached himself to actual idolatry, since idolatry dwells within this person. It is forbidden to look at the face of a person who is angry and about this the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">392</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 19:4</i> ‘Do not turn to gods that are nothingness,’ and,<sup class="footnote-marker">393</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 34:17</i> ‘You shall not make molten gods for yourselves.’”
This sin is worse than all others, for all other sins and contaminations, except for this, are refinable and reparable. It is the worst because through it, he contaminates his body, both from within and without, and his soul becomes entirely contaminated. Even when such a person completely repents and uproots this alien contamination from himself forever, and then comes to purify himself and become holy, may it only be that he should merit to draw forth his holy soul in himself and become holy again. For, no matter how much he toils in good deeds, he can never return his soul to its original perfection and holiness.<sup class="footnote-marker">394</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 182b – That is, he cannot fully undo the damage that he wrought in his state of anger. Nevertheless, as will be stated at the end of Section 2, Shaar 8, he still can and must repent in full Teshuvah while he is still in this world and able to do so.</i>

<b>Pedantry </b>is a branch of arrogance and anger. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">395</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 110b</i> “Whoever is intolerant, they are intolerant with him.” Such a person is not forgiven for his sins, as they taught,<sup class="footnote-marker">396</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a (also see Rashi)</i> “It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">397</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:18</i> ‘He pardons iniquity and overlooks transgression.’ For whom does He pardon iniquity and overlook transgression? For a person who overlooks his reckonings with others, for the slights and injustices that they perpetrated against him.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">398</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 44b</i> “One should plead for mercy every day, and that he should have no enemies.” It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">399</sup><i class="footnote">Lamentations 3:29-30</i> “Let him put his mouth to the dust… Let him offer his cheek to he who smites him, let him be filled with disgrace.” Happy is he who hears his disgrace and does not respond.<sup class="footnote-marker">400</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Mitzvot Gadol, Prohibitive Commandment 12</i> Isaiah the Prophet thus stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">401</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 50:6</i> “I submitted my body to those who smite and my cheeks to those who pluck; I did not hide my face from humiliation and spit.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, thus stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">402</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i> “Whoever overlooks his reckonings with others for slights and injustices that were perpetrated against him, is himself forgiven for all his sins, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">403</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:18</i> ‘He pardons iniquity and overlooks transgression.’”
In Chupat Eliyahu<sup class="footnote-marker">404</sup><i class="footnote">Chupat Eliyahu, Shaar 3 (end of Reishit Chochmah) citing Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 113b</i> it states, “There are three that the Holy One, blessed is He, loves: One who does not get angry; one who does not get drunk; and one who is forgiving.” Rabbi Akiva asked Rabbi Nechunya the Great,<sup class="footnote-marker">405</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Megillah 28a</i> “In the merit of what virtue were you blessed with longevity?” He replied, “In all my days I never accepted gifts, nor was I inflexible and intolerant by exacting retribution against those who wronged me.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">406</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a ibid.</i> “Rav Huna, the son of Rav Yehoshua, became sick etc. Upon his recovery they asked him, ‘What did you see when you were hovering between life and death?’ He replied, ‘I was indeed close to death, but the Holy One, blessed is He, said: Since he does not insist on his rights, do not be exacting with him, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">407</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:18</i> ‘He pardons iniquity and overlooks transgression.’’” Our sages, of blessed memory, related<sup class="footnote-marker">408</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 152a</i> that there were diggers who were digging on Rav Nachman’s land and came upon the grave of Rav Achai bar Yoshiya, who was fully preserved, and he rebuked them. When Rav Nachman came and asked him how it was that he was preserved, he answered that it was because in all his days he did not stand on his rights against those who trespassed against him, and he never was begrudging or envious of his fellows, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">409</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 14:30</i> “Envy causes the rotting of bones.”
Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, related,<sup class="footnote-marker">410</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Taanit 25b</i> “There was an incident in which Rabbi Eliezer descended before the ark to serve as the prayer leader, but he was not answered. Rabbi Akiva descended before the ark after him, and was answered. The sages whispered amongst themselves about this, and a Supernal voice (<i>Bat Kol</i>) emerged and said, ‘It is not because this one is greater than that one, but because this one is tolerant and forgiving and that one is intolerant and unforgiving.’”
The sages, of blessed memory, also said,<sup class="footnote-marker">411</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chullin 89a (See Rashi)</i> “The world is only sustained in the merit of those who muzzle (<i>Bolem</i>-בולם) their mouths in a time of quarrel, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">412</sup><i class="footnote">Job 26:7</i> ‘He hangs the earth upon nothingness (<i>Blimah</i>-בלימה).’ Rabbi Avahu said, this refers to a person who makes himself as if he is nothingness.” The Rabbis taught,<sup class="footnote-marker">413</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 23a</i> “Regarding those who are insulted but do not insult, who hear themselves shamed but do not respond, the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">414</sup><i class="footnote">Judges 5:31</i> ‘Those who love Him are like the sun as it goes forth in its might.’”
Father Eliyahu, who is remembered for good, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">415</sup><i class="footnote">Tractate Kallah Rabbati Ch. 5</i> “The knowledge of Torah is revealed only to one who is not intolerant, and I too will not be revealed except to one who is not intolerant.”
<b>Depression</b> obstructs one’s service of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, and the fulfillment of His <i>mitzvot</i>. It obstructs one’s involvement in Torah study and having proper devotional intent in prayer and negates his good and positive thoughts to serve <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. It is the gateway through which the evil inclination entices and turns a person away from serving <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, even if he is a righteous <i>Tzaddik</i>, by making it appear to him, that because of his suffering, his service of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is ineffectual.
Moreover, the evil inclination will even come under the guise of piety and tell him, “How can it even enter your mind that you, who are nothing but dust, worms and maggots, can come close and be sanctified in the holiness of the King of the world! Does not the verse state,<sup class="footnote-marker">416</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 24:7</i> ‘For a fool wisdom is unattainable?’” Moreover, the evil inclination says, “Even if you attain righteousness, does it not say,<sup class="footnote-marker">417</sup><i class="footnote">Job 35:7</i> ‘If you are righteous, what have you given Him?’” In addition, depression causes the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) to depart from him.
The opposite is true when one serves <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, with joy, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">418</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 100:2</i> “Serve <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה with joy.” For joy increases one’s desire and love of adhering to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">419</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 28:47</i> “Because you did not serve <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God with joy and gladness of heart etc.” For, a person who serves <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, with melancholy, is likened to a servant who serves his master with a sullen and annoyed face.
It is likewise written,<sup class="footnote-marker">420</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 10:22 – The root Etzev-עצב of this verse is explained to mean “suffering” or “burdensome toil” (see Rashi), however, the simple meaning of the root Etzev-עצב is “sadness” or “melancholy,” as in the verse (Isaiah 54:6), “For like a wife who is forlorn and melancholy (Atzoovah-עצובה), HaShem-יהו״ה has called you. Can one cast off the wife of his Youth? Said your God.” (See Radak to Isaiah 54:6 ibid.)</i> “The blessing of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is what enriches, and sadness (<i>Etzev</i>-עצב) does not increase it.” For, sadness is drawn from the contamination of <i>Sama’el</i><sup class="footnote-marker">421</sup><i class="footnote">    This is the angelic name of Satan-the Accuser. </i> and the snake, who infected Adam and Chavah with it, as it states about Adam,<sup class="footnote-marker">422</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 3:17</i> “With sadness (<i>Eetzavon</i>-<b>עצב</b>ון) you shall eat of it all the days of your life,” and about Chava it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">423</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 3:16</i> “I will greatly increase your sadness (<i>Eetzavon</i>-<b>עצב</b>ון)… with sadness (<i>b’Etzev-</i>ב<b>עצב</b>) you shall bear children.”<sup class="footnote-marker">424</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the prior note, the root Etzev-עצב can mean “suffering” or “sadness.” In context to the subject being explained here, it means “sadness.” </i>
On account of this, the Holy One, blessed is He, and His Indwelling Presence, the <i>Shechinah</i>, withdraw from him. Proof of this is our forefather Yaakov, the choicest of the forefathers,<sup class="footnote-marker">425</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Rabba 76:1 and elsewhere.</i> from whom the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) departed for a period of twenty-two years when Yosef was separated from him and he assumed that he had been devoured by a wild animal. However, when he rejoiced over the tidings that Yosef was alive, the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">426</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 45:27</i> “The spirit of Yaakov was revived,” that is, the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) returned and rested upon him.<sup class="footnote-marker">427</sup><i class="footnote">Avot d’Rabbi Natan 30:4; Midrash Tanchuma, Veyeishev 2:7; Rashi to Genesis 45:7 ibid., and elsewhere.</i>
Similarly, our sages,<sup class="footnote-marker">428</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 117a; Zohar I 217b</i> of blessed memory, taught that the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, (the <i>Shechinah</i>) and the spirit of Prophecy, do not dwell in a place of sadness. We thus find that it says about Elisha and the students of the prophets,<sup class="footnote-marker">429</sup><i class="footnote">Kings II 3:15</i> “As the musician played, the spirit of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה came upon him,” and it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">430</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 10:5</i> “When you arrive at the city, you will encounter a group of prophets coming down from the high place, and leading them will be players of lyre, drum, flute and harp, and they will be prophesying.”
Even when serving <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, in the performance of any <i>mitzvah</i> or in prayer, one must be in an ultimate state of joy. This can be seen from Abaye,<sup class="footnote-marker">431</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 30b</i> who was sitting before his teacher Rabbah and was excessively joyful, and when questioned about his joy, he said, “I now am donned in <i>Tefillin</i>.” It is similarly related<sup class="footnote-marker">432</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 9b</i> that, “Rav Bruna was a great man who rejoiced in the <i>mitzvot</i>. Once, through juxtaposing the blessing of redemption (<i>Ge’ulah</i>) to the Amidah prayer, a smile did not depart from his mouth for that entire day.”
<b>Hatred</b> brings a person to sin against his fellow man, by inflicting all types of evil upon him. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">433</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 2:11</i> “Hating the creatures removes a person from the world,” for by doing so, it is as if he harbors hatred of their Creator, the Holy One, blessed is He, who created him, for are we not all children to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה our God?<sup class="footnote-marker">434</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 14:1</i> Moreover, by hating another Jew, it is as if he also hates Avraham, Yitzchak and Yaakov, from whom this person came forth. All souls are bound to the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, and each has an extremely lofty purpose, namely that through them <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, will be glorified.<sup class="footnote-marker">435</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 49:3</i> This being so, how can anyone hate his fellow?
Our sages, of blessed memory, related<sup class="footnote-marker">436</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 9b</i> that during the period of the second Holy Temple, there were many righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i> and Torah Scholars. Nonetheless, the Holy Temple was destroyed only because of the sin of baseless hatred. They likewise said that the exile was lengthened and its end was concealed solely due to baseless hatred. Furthermore, in regard to all other sins, a person is only in a state of transgression when he actively violates them, whereas baseless hatred is a constant transgression that one carries in his heart. Therefore, he is in violation of the negative <i>mitzvah</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">437</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 19:17</i> “You shall not hate your brother in your heart” and negates the positive <i>mitzvah</i> of,<sup class="footnote-marker">438</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 19:18</i> “You shall love your fellow as yourself,” at every moment.
Furthermore, about the <i>mitzvah</i> of loving one’s fellow Jew, they stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">439</sup><i class="footnote">Rashi to Leviticus 19:18, citing Sifra; Torat Kohanim, and elsewhere.</i> “This is a great principle that includes the entire Torah in it,” for everything depends on it. Our teacher Moshe only merited attaining all of his wondrous and exalted levels because of his great love of Israel and because he was pained by their suffering, as our sages, of blessed memory,<sup class="footnote-marker">440</sup><i class="footnote">See Rashi to Exodus 2:11, citing Midrash Shemot Rabba 1:27</i> said about the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">441</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 2:11</i> “He saw their burdens,” and about the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">442</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 32:32</i> “Now, if You would but forgive their sin – but if not, erase me now from Your book that You have written.” On account of this, he was equated to the entire Jewish people, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">443</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 63:11; Also see Rashi to Exodus 18:1 citing Mechilta.</i> “They remembered the days of old, of Moshe, His people.”
<b>Envy</b> brings a person to hatred and is actually even worse than hatred, since by being envious, he rebels against the Holy One, blessed is He, by saying to himself, “Why has the Holy One, blessed is He, bestowed more goodness to my fellow than to me?” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">444</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 4:21</i> “Envy, lust, and [the desire for] honor, remove a person from the world.”
Study and you will see that all the ancients were punished solely on account of their envy. Cain, who spoke with <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, mouth to mouth, was excised from the world along with his descendants, because he was envious of his brother Abel’s twin sister.<sup class="footnote-marker">445</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Bereishit Rabba 22:1; Pirkei d’Rabbi Eliezer, Ch. 21</i>  As a result of his jealousy he came to transgress all his sins. Similarly, the ten tribes of Israel were exiled to Egypt because Joseph’s brothers envied him.<sup class="footnote-marker">446</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 37:11; Also see Tanchuma Veyeishev 18 and elsewhere.</i> Ultimately, they were further punished with the incident the ten martyrs.<sup class="footnote-marker">447</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Eileh Ezkera and elsewhere.</i> Yeravam, before whom all the Torah scholars of the generation were like grass of the field,<sup class="footnote-marker">448</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 101a-b</i> was excised from the world solely because he envied the kingdom of the House of David.
Even Shaul, the chosen one of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, who as taught by our sages, of blessed memory, was as pure as a one-year-old child who has never tasted sin<sup class="footnote-marker">449</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 22b</i> and whose ancestry and kingship were free of flaw,<sup class="footnote-marker">450</sup><i class="footnote">See Yoma 22b ibid.</i> was excised from his kingship and killed along with his three sons, for having caused the people of Nov, the city of the Priests, to be killed, for having caused the exile of the Jewish people amongst the Philistines, and for having caused the destruction of the Tabernacle (<i>Mishkan</i>) at Shiloh, all of which were brought about because he envied David regarding the matter of Goliath.<sup class="footnote-marker">451</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 18:7 and on.</i> This caused the Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) to withdraw from him, which was replaced by a spirit of distortion (<i>Ru’ach Eeveem</i>)<sup class="footnote-marker">452</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 18:12; 16:14-15 and elsewhere; Isaiah 19:14</i> that rested upon him.
Moshiach, the son of David, will not come until the spirit of envy is removed, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">453</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 11:13</i> “The jealousy of Ephraim shall cease and the oppressors of Yehudah shall be cut off; Ephraim shall not be jealous of Yehudah and Yehudah will not harass Ephraim.” Moreover, even the Supernal angels fell from their holiness as the result of envy, as written in Pirkei d’Rabbi Eliezer,<sup class="footnote-marker">454</sup><i class="footnote">Pirkei d’Rabbi Eliezer, Ch. 13-14</i> that the angel <i>Sama’el</i> was greater than all the <i>Seraphim</i> angels, in that they only had six wings, whereas he had twelve wings. He nonetheless was uprooted from the side of holiness because he was envious of man. The same is said of the <i>Nefillim</i> angels, <i>Aza</i> and <i>Aza’el</i>, who were excised from the world because they were jealous of man.<sup class="footnote-marker">455</sup><i class="footnote">Pesikta Rabbati 34:1; Yoma 67b and Rashi there; Zohar I 37a.</i>
The bones of whoever possesses envy shall rot.<sup class="footnote-marker">456</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 14:30; Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 152b</i> It therefore is appropriate for a person to be happy with his lot,<sup class="footnote-marker">457</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 4:1</i> even if it is small. For, he is certainly no better than Hillel the Elder, Rabbi Chaninah ben Dosa, Rabbi Yehuda bar Ila’i, Rabbi Elazar ben Pedat, and others like them.<sup class="footnote-marker">458</sup><i class="footnote">All of whom were materially poor. (See Yoma 35b; Brachot 17b; Nedarim 49b; Taanit 25a, and elsewhere.)</i>
<b>Greed </b>is the father of all impurity. It brings to hatred and envy, as well as theft, false oaths and even murder. This prohibition is the last of the Ten Commandments and is equal to them all, since<sup class="footnote-marker">459</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 4:8</i> “his eye is never sated with wealth,” like the eye of the snake, about whom it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">460</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 65:25</i> “The food of the snake shall be dust.” Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">461</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 28:22</i> “One who is overeager for wealth has an evil eye, he does not know that want may befall him.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">462</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 4:21</i> “Lust removes a person from the world,” since it causes his mind to be preoccupied and distracted, thus uprooting him from studying <i>HaShem’s-</i>יהו"ה Torah and fulfilling His <i>mitzvot</i>. Moreover, he denies <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Divine Providence, in that he does not believe that everything comes about according to <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו״ה Supernal will and supervision, blessed is He. As our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">463</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 48b</i> “Whoever has bread in his basket and says to himself, ‘What will I eat tomorrow,’ has little faith. About such a person the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">464</sup><i class="footnote">Zachariah 4:10</i> ‘For who wastes the day? Small things.’ That is, what is it that causes the reward of the righteous to be wasted from the coming future? It is their small-mindedness and their smallness of faith in the Holy One, blessed is He.”
In contrast, there is no greater quality than trust in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">465</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 2:12</i> “Happy are all who trust in Him.” A person who has this quality is faithful that there is a God in the world, who is all-capable and supervises over everything. It thus is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">466</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 17:7</i> “Blessed is the man who trusts in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה will be his security.” Such a person is certain that he will not lack sustenance, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">467</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 55:23</i> “Cast your burden upon <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה and He will sustain you.” However, this applies on condition that his trust in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is truly sincere, with all his heart and without doubt. This is evident by the fact that if he truly trusts in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, he will occupy himself in studying His Torah and fulfilling His <i>mitzvot</i> with all his heart and without any misgivings.
<b>Lust</b> for pleasure is worse than all the negative traits mentioned above. For, if a person is gluttonous, he will come to fall to greed, theft, false oaths, hatred of the creatures and envy. Such a person is like Esav, who said,<sup class="footnote-marker">468</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 25:30</i> “Please pour some of that red red stuff into me.” About such a person it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">469</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 23:2 (See Rashi)</i> “If you care for your soul, it would be better for you to put a knife to your throat.” For out of gluttony he will eventually come to eat the meat of an animal that died without being slaughtered (<i>Neveilah</i>) or that has been slaughtered improperly (<i>Treifah</i>) and all other kinds of forbidden foods. Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">470</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 6:7</i> “All man’s toil is for his mouth,” and it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">471</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 13:25</i> “The stomach of the wicked will always be lacking.”
It likewise is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">472</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:15</i> “Yeshurun became fat and kicked. You became fat, you became thick, you became corpulent. He deserted God, his Maker and scorned the Rock of his salvation.” That is, this negative trait brings a person to deny <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">473</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 30:9</i> “Lest I become sated and deny, saying, ‘Who is <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה?’”
Furthermore, in regard to all other sins, a minor is not punished, however, in the case of the rebellious son, if he steals and eats a <i>tartimer</i> of meat and a half <i>log</i> of wine, he is stoned to death.<sup class="footnote-marker">474</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 70a; Rashi to Deuteronomy 21:18</i> Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">475</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Taanit 11a</i> “The wicked are accustomed to eat meat and drink wine, saying,<sup class="footnote-marker">476</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 56:12</i> ‘Come, I will fetch wine and we will fill ourselves with strong drink; and tomorrow will be like today etc.’” However, about this it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">477</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 22:14 – The prior verse states, “Yet behold! There is joy and gladness, slaying of cattle and slaughtering of sheep, eating meat and drinking wine, [saying,] ‘Eat and drink, for tomorrow we die.’</i> “Until the day of your death you will not be atoned of this sin.” Eliyahu, who is remembered for good, said to Rabbi Yehudah,<sup class="footnote-marker">478</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 29b</i> “Do not get drunk and you will not sin.”
