In contrast, a person who suffices with what is necessary for him is called a righteous <i>Tzaddik</i>, as scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">479</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 13:25</i> “A righteous person eats to satisfy his soul.” Similarly, King David said,<sup class="footnote-marker">480</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 119:71</i> “It is good for me that I was afflicted, so that I might learn Your statutes.” We likewise find that our forefather Yaakov only requested the following,<sup class="footnote-marker">481</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 28:20</i> “Give me bread to eat and clothes to wear.” It is likewise written,<sup class="footnote-marker">482</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 49:14</i> “Yissachar is a strong-boned donkey… he bent his shoulder to bear.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">483</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 6:4</i> “Such is the way of [the life] of Torah: You shall eat bread with salt and drink rationed water; you shall sleep on the ground and your life will be one of privation, and you shall labor in Torah. If you do this,<sup class="footnote-marker">484</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 128:2</i> ‘You shall be happy and it shall be good for you.’ That is, ‘You shall be happy’ in this world, ‘and it shall be good for you’ in the coming world.” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">485</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 63a</i> “The words of Torah are only sustained in one who kills himself over them.” They also said,<sup class="footnote-marker">486</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 2:</i> “Whoever increases his flesh, increases his maggots.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">487</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Taanit 11a-b</i> “A person should always consider himself as if holiness dwells in his bowels, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">488</sup><i class="footnote">Hosea 11:9</i> ‘Holiness is in your innards.’” Our teacher, Moshe, peace be upon him, only merited receiving the Torah after having fasted for forty days and forty nights.<sup class="footnote-marker">489</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 34:28</i> Similarly, Eliyahu the Prophet, who is remembered for good, only merited ascending the heights after he fasted for forty days and forty nights.<sup class="footnote-marker">490</sup><i class="footnote">Kings I 19:8</i> Likewise, Rabbi Elazar, Rabbi Akiva, and Rabbi Yishmael only merited all the wondrous wisdom and prophecy they attained when they ascended to the Pardes, after having fasted for many days and through all kinds of self-flagellation and abstention.<sup class="footnote-marker">491</sup><i class="footnote">Heichalot Rabbati and Heichalot Zutrati</i>  Similarly, King Solomon, about whom it states that,<sup class="footnote-marker">492</sup><i class="footnote">Kings I 5:11</i> “He was wiser than all men,” only merited to such wisdom after fasting for forty days and forty nights, as our Sages explained about the large letter <i>Mem</i>-מ<sup class="footnote-marker">493</sup><i class="footnote">The numerical value of the letter mem-מ is forty.</i> of the opening word of Proverbs-<i>Mishlei</i>-משלי.<sup class="footnote-marker">494</sup><i class="footnote">Yalkut Shimoni Mishlei, Remez 929</i>
It states in Zohar<sup class="footnote-marker">495</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 11a-b (See Ramak and the other commentaries.)</i> that when Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai came out of the cave, Rabbi Pinchas ben Ya’ir saw that his body was completely covered with blisters. He cried and said, “Woe is me, that I have seen you in such agony!” Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai answered him, “Great is your merit that you have seen me in such agony, for had you not seen me like this, I would not have merited to all that I merited.”
In Zohar Terumah it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">496</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 141a</i> “The spirit of impurity has no dominion over the bodies of the righteous <i>Tzaddikim</i> who, in this world, were not drawn after the pleasures and lusts of that extraneous husk (<i>Kelipah</i>). For, they have not pleasured themselves in this world at all, except for fulfilling the <i>mitzvah</i> of pleasure on Shabbat and Biblical Festivals. The spirit of impurity thus has no dominion or hold on them at all, since they have not derived any pleasure whatsoever from that which is the opposite Holiness (<i>Sitra Achara</i>). However, about a person who did derive pleasure from the opposite the Holiness (<i>Sitra Achara</i>) during the mundane days of the week, the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">497</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 2:3</i> ‘I will smear dung upon your faces, the dung of your festive offerings, and you shall be carried out to its heap.’”
It was taught in the School of Eliyahu,<sup class="footnote-marker">498</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Vei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 26; Also see Ketubot 104a, Tosefot entitled “Lo Neheneiti – I did not derive any pleasure from even my pinky.” </i> “If a person has not yet merited to plead for mercy from <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה that Torah should be in his innards, he should at least plead for mercy that excess food and drink should not enter his innards.”

<b>Power and honor</b> are extremely problematic, as they bring a person to haughtiness, which is worse than all the above-mentioned negative qualities. As a result of it, he becomes a leader who casts excessive fear on the community, in a manner that is not for the sake of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה. As our sages, of blessed memory said, in the end he will be uprooted from the world and his children will be completely unsuccessful after him.<sup class="footnote-marker">499</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i>
We find this about the great sage, Yeravam, that because he sought power, both he and his descendants were uprooted from this world, nor does he have a portion in the coming world. Similarly, when Shaul, the chosen one of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, began his reign, he was as pure as a one-year-old child who has never tasted sin.<sup class="footnote-marker">500</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 22b</i> Moreover, as the verse attests, when they sought to crown him as king,<sup class="footnote-marker">501</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 10:22</i> “He hid amongst the baggage,” in that he fled from power. Nevertheless, he was ultimately caught in its net and pursued it, as he said to the Prophet Shmuel,<sup class="footnote-marker">502</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 15:30</i> “Please honor me in the presence of the elders of my people.” In the end he lost the kingdom and he was killed along with three of his sons, as mentioned before in the section on envy.
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">503</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 4:21</i> “Envy, lust, and [the desire for] honor, remove a person from the world.” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">504</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 86b; Pesachim 87b; Avot d’Rabbi Natan Ch. 39</i> “Authority shortens the life of those who possess it and buries them.” This is because it causes one’s heart to be haughty with his Maker, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">505</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 17:20</i> “So that his heart should not become exalted above his brethren and so that he will not depart from the commandment, neither to the right nor to the left, so that his years will be prolonged over his kingdom, he and his sons in the midst of Israel.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">506</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 86b ibid.; Sanhedrin 7b</i> “When Rava would go out to judge, he would say, ‘I willingly go out to die etc.’” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">507</sup><i class="footnote">See Midrash Shemot Rabba 27:9, and elsewhere</i> “The verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">508</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:1</i> ‘My son, if you have been a guarantor for your fellow etc.’ Rav Huna explained that this refers to a person who was appointed to a position of authority over the masses. However, the next verse continues,<sup class="footnote-marker">509</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:2</i> ‘You have been trapped by the words of your mouth, snared by the words of your mouth. Do this, therefore, my child, and be rescued; for you have come into your fellow’s hand. Go humble yourself etc.’” However, if he does not, about him the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">510</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:32</i> “One who commits adultery with a married woman lacks an understanding heart, he who destroys his own soul will do this,” and they have no mercy upon him in purgatory (Gehinnom).
The Holy One, blessed is He, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">511</sup><i class="footnote">See Midrash Bamidbar Rabba 22:1; Tanchuma Matot 1:1</i> “I am holy, I am pious, I am upright etc. If you possess all these qualities, you can accept a position of power and authority, but if not, do not accept it.” King David, peace be upon him, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">512</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 131:1</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, my heart was not proud and my eyes were not haughty, nor did I pursue matters too great and too wondrous for me. I swear that I stilled and silenced my soul, like a suckling child at his mother’s side, my soul is like a suckling child.”
Therefore, flee from power and authority to the opposite extreme, as I explained at length when discussing the quality of pride. For, Zohar states,<sup class="footnote-marker">513</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 168a</i> “One who makes himself small in this world is meritorious.” Is there anyone greater than Moshe, the teacher of all Israel, who for seven days refused the authority placed upon him by the Holy One, blessed is He, and did not desire it, saying,<sup class="footnote-marker">514</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 4:13</i> “Please, my Lord, send through whomever You will send!” About him the verse attests,<sup class="footnote-marker">515</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 4:14</i> “The wrath of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה burned against Moshe,” to the point that he was adversely affected by it, as our sages, of blessed memory, explained.<sup class="footnote-marker">516</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Zevachim 102a; Also see Rashi to Exodus 4:14 ibid.</i> He subsequently assumed the responsibility, but in the end was punished because of the Jewish people at the waters of strife,<sup class="footnote-marker">517</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 3:26 (see Rashi); Psalms 106:32</i> and all of his merits did not suffice to help him.
For, whoever exerts power and authority over the congregation, even if it is for the sake of Heaven, like Moshe, will ultimately be punished. For, he is responsible for all their deeds, as our sages, of blessed memory, stated<sup class="footnote-marker">518</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Dvarim Rabba 1:10</i> in explanation of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">519</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 1:13</i> “I will place them upon your heads.” How much more so does this certainly apply to orphans such as ourselves, for whom there would be no hope of salvation, God forbid.
<b>Boastfulness </b>is a quality about which our sages, of blessed memory, related about the woman who was punished in purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>) because she told her friend, “Today I fasted etc.” That is, when a person boasts of his righteousness, not only does he not receive reward, but on the contrary, he is judged with the punishments of purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>). For, by boasting, he reveals his true intentions and that his actions are not at all for the sake of Heaven. He is counted amongst the seven categories of the pseudo-righteous (<i>Parushim</i>) who erode the world, such as those who practice self-flagellation and blood-letting etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">520</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Sotah 22b</i>
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">521</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Vei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 21; Also see Mishnah Avot 2:12</i> “A person should always be in a state of fear of Heaven, even in private, and all his ways should be for the sake of Heaven.” If a person is able, he should conduct himself in all his deeds and ways for the sake of Heaven, without revealing any of it to the creatures. His reward will be doubled and quadrupled, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">522</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 25:2</i> “It is the honor of God to conceal a matter.”

Shaar 5

Gate Five
<b>Forbidden Traits</b>
<b>Evil speech</b> is a quality about which our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">523</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Arachin 16b; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot 7:3</i> “There are three transgressions that bring retribution against the one who perpetrates them in this world and disinherit him from a share in the coming world. These are idolatry, forbidden relations, and murder, but evil speech outweighs them all.” Our sages, of blessed memory, also stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">524</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Arachin 15b</i> “Whoever speaks with an evil tongue denies the fundamental principle of the existence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">525</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 12:5</i> ‘Those who said, ‘Because of our tongues we shall prevail, our lips are with us, who is master over us?’’”
<b>Gossip</b> kills three people and is equal to murder, and on account of it, one is barred from entry into the Garden of Eden. This is as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">526</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 15:1</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, who may sojourn in Your tent? Who may dwell on Your Holy Mountain? One who walks in perfect innocence and does what is right, and who speaks the truth from his heart; who has no gossip on his tongue etc.” We see that Doeg the Edomite was one of the mighty shepherds of Israel and the head of the Sanhedrin.<sup class="footnote-marker">527</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 106b</i>  However, because of his gossip he was excised from the coming world, was killed having lived only half his days, and caused the people of Nov, the city of the Priests, to be killed, as well as the death of Shaul and his household.
<b>Causing embarrassment, calling one’s fellow by a negative nickname and glorying in the downfall one’s fellow</b> cause a person to descend to purgatory and never ascend, having no share in the coming world. These are included in the commandment,<sup class="footnote-marker">528</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 20:13</i> “You shall not murder.” This is as our sages, of blessed memory, taught,<sup class="footnote-marker">529</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Metziya 58b</i> “Whoever humiliates another in public, it is as though he is spilling his blood. Over what <i>mitzvah</i> are they particularly vigilant in the West?<sup class="footnote-marker">530</sup><i class="footnote">The land of Israel</i> In refraining from causing the color to leave a person’s face, so that his face becomes pale.”
<b>Levity</b> is one of the four classes of traits that prevent a person from receiving the countenance of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He – the <i>Shechinah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">531</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 42a</i> Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">532</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 18b</i> “Whoever acts with levity falls into purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>).” Likewise, our sages, of blessed memory, stated<sup class="footnote-marker">533</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:2</i> that even if a person sits idly and not engaging in Torah study, it is considered as if he is sitting with the frivolous who have contempt for Torah, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">534</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 1:1</i> “Praiseworthy is the man who did not walk in the counsel of the wicked and did not stand in the path of the sinful and did not sit in the gathering of the frivolous.” The very next verse continues and states,<sup class="footnote-marker">535</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 1:2</i> “But his desire is in the Torah of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, and in His Torah he meditates day and night.” It continues,<sup class="footnote-marker">536</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 1:3-4</i> “He shall be like a tree planted alongside brooks of water, that yields its fruit in its season and whose leaf never withers; and everything that he does will succeed. Not so the wicked; Rather they are like the chaff that the wind drives away etc.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">537</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 6</i> “Every day, a Heavenly voice (<i>Bat Kol</i>) goes forth from Mount Chorev and proclaims, ‘Woe to the creatures for their contempt of Torah.’ For, whosoever does not occupy himself in the study of Torah is called censured-<i>Nazuf</i>, meaning excommunicated from Heaven. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">538</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 99b; Yalkut Shimoni Remez 749</i> “The following verse applies to such a person,<sup class="footnote-marker">539</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 15:31</i> ‘For he had contempt the word of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה and violated His commandment, that soul shall surely be cut off – his sin is upon him.’ Rabbi Nechemiah says: This refers to anyone who is able to engage in Torah study but fails to do so.” Similarly,<sup class="footnote-marker">540</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Batra 79a</i> “Rav said: “Whoever excuses himself from studying the words of Torah, a fire consumes him.” Likewise, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">541</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 12b; Ketubot 111b; Brachot 63a and elsewhere.</i> “Whoever weakens or stops his study of words of Torah to engage in idle chatter, will be fed the hot coals of a Juniper tree, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">542</sup><i class="footnote">Job 30:3</i> ‘They pluck saltwort and the leaves of wormwood and the roots of the Juniper tree is their bread.’” Our sages, of blessed memory, likewise stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">543</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:4</i> “One who turns his heart to idle matters is mortally guilty,” as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">544</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 4:9</i> “Only beware for yourself and greatly beware for your soul, lest you forget the words<sup class="footnote-marker">545</sup><i class="footnote">The word “Dvarim-דברים” is generally translated as “things” but also means “words” and in the above verse refers to the words of Torah and the Ten Commandments (which are called (Exodus 34:28) “Aseret HaDvarim-עשרת הדברים”), as stated in the continuing verse (Deuteronomy 4:10), “The day that you stood before HaShem-יהו״ה, your God, at Chorev.”</i> that your eyes have beheld and lest you remove them from your heart all the days of your life etc.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">546</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 7a</i> “The beginning of a person’s judgment is that he is judged only concerning the study of Torah, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">547</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 17:14</i> ‘Exemption from waters is the beginning of judgment.’”<sup class="footnote-marker">548</sup><i class="footnote">The term “release-Poter-פוטר” here means that he exempts himself from the waters, which refers to Torah study. The term “Madon-מדון” which means “strife,” is also of the root “judgement-Din-דין” as the Talmud here indicates. Thus, the verse is understood to mean, “Excusing oneself from the waters of Torah study is the beginning of judgment.” (See Rashi to Talmud Bavli, Kiddushin 40b.)</i> Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">549</sup><i class="footnote">Joshua 1:8</i> “This Book of the Torah shall not leave from your mouth; you shall contemplate it day and night, so that you may guard yourself to do according to all that is written in it; for then your way will be successful, and then you will be wise.” About each moment, hour or day that a person is idle from studying the words of Torah, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">550</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 1:15 (See Rashi)</i> “Crookedness that cannot be straightened, lacking that is incalculable.”
On the other hand, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">551</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Pe’ah 1:1</i> “These are the things, the fruits of which a person enjoys in this world, while the principle remains for the coming world; honoring one’s father and mother, doing deeds of kindness, early attendance in the house of study morning and evening, welcoming guests, visiting the sick, dowering a bride, escorting the dead, concentration in prayer, bringing peace between man and his fellow and between husband and wife. But the study of Torah is equal to them all.” Moreover, whoever is engaged in Torah study is exempt from all the commandments, since it equals all the commandments.<sup class="footnote-marker">552</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sukkah 25a-26b; Brachot 11a, 16a; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Ishut (Laws of Marriage) 15:2, and elsewhere.</i>
It was taught in the school of Eliyahu, who is remembered for good,<sup class="footnote-marker">553</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Bei Eliyahu Zuta, Ch. 1; Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 5b</i> “Happy is the man who subjugates himself to Torah study, like an ox to a yoke and like a donkey to a burden, sitting and studying and reviewing Torah every day constantly. The Holy Spirit (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) will immediately rest upon him.” If this is the case, that when a person sits idly he is punished to such a great degree, then how much greater is the punishment of a person who actually behaves with levity and disdain toward Torah.
<b>Idle chatter </b>leads to very great sins. For, even when he merely sits idly it is considered as though he sits with the frivolous who have contempt for Torah, and he is punished with very great punishments, as we mentioned before regarding the matter of levity and mockery. This being so, how much more is this true of one who actually engages in empty chatter. Moreover, this brings him to come to speak badly of others, to gossip, slander and mock others.
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">554</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 19b</i> “One who engages in idle chatter violates a positive commandment, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">555</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:7</i> ‘You shall speak of them,’ referring to words of Torah, rather than other matters.” It was said about Rabbi Yochanan ben Zachai,<sup class="footnote-marker">556</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sukkah 28a</i> that in all his days he never engaged in idle conversation. Our sages, of blessed memory, likewise coined this adage,<sup class="footnote-marker">557</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Megillah 18a</i> “If a word is worth one <i>sela</i>, silence is worth two.” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">558</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:17</i> “In all my days I grew up among the sages and I found nothing better for a person than silence.” It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">559</sup><i class="footnote">Lamentations 3:28</i> “Let one sit in solitude and be silent,” and it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">560</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 18:21</i> “Death and life are in the hands of the tongue.” Our sages, of blessed memory, also said,<sup class="footnote-marker">561</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:13</i> “The guardrail of wisdom is silence.” King Solomon said,<sup class="footnote-marker">562</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 5:1</i> “Be not rash with your mouth, and let not your heart be hasty in uttering a word before God; for God is in heaven and you are on earth, so let your words be few.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">563</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chullin 89a</i> “The verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">564</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 58:2</i> ‘Is there truly (<i>HaUmnam</i>-ה<b>אמנ</b>ם) silence (<i>Eilem</i>-אלם) when you should be speaking righteousness?’ That is, in what skill (<i>Umanut</i>-<b>אמנ</b>ות) should a person toil in this world? He should toil in making himself as if he is mute (<i>Eelem</i>-אלם).” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">565</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 23a</i> “When the Master would read the following verse, he would cry. The verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">566</sup><i class="footnote">Amos 4:13</i> ‘For behold, He Who forms the mountains and creates the wind, and declares to man what is his speech.’ This even includes the lighthearted and frivolous speech between a man and his wife before engaging in relations. Even if they are completely insignificant, they nevertheless written into a person’s ledger and read before him at the time of his death.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">567</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Sotah 9:15; Also see Tanchuma Vayeitze 6; Tzava’at HaRivash, translated as The Way of The Baal Shem Tov, Ch. 49.</i> “One’s silence leads to humility,” and humility the chief quality that leads to fear of Heaven.<sup class="footnote-marker">568</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 20b</i> Thus, when engaging in the study of Torah, he should be silent and glue his lips together, like two millstones that sit upon each other. This is because all the righteousness and meritoriousness a person accrues are insufficient from saving him from what comes out of his lips. Happy is he who makes himself as if mute and like a deaf person, like a cripple and one who is blind! Why is it imperative to take such great care? So that he should not come to sin and obligate himself and his limbs, thus condemning himself to purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>). Similarly, King David said,<sup class="footnote-marker">569</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 38:14</i> “I am like a deaf man, I do not hear, like a mute who does not open his mouth.”
In Zohar it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">570</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 59a</i> “There is not a single breath that does not possess a voice and create a spirit. All the words that a person speaks which are not for the sake of serving the Holy One, blessed is He, create a spirit that carries and travels around in the world and when the soul leaves him upon death, that spirit is hurled at him in the torments of the grave, like a stone flung from a slingshot (<i>Kaf HaKela</i>). This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">571</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 25:29</i> ‘may He hurl away the soul of your enemies as one shoots a stone from a slingshot (<i>Kaf HaKela</i>).’” It also states in Zohar,<sup class="footnote-marker">572</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 183b</i> “From the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">573</sup><i class="footnote">Esther 5:1</i> ‘And Esther donned royal garments,’ we learn that any person who guards his mouth and tongue, merits to don the garment of the spirit of holiness and Divine Inspiration (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>).’”<sup class="footnote-marker">574</sup><i class="footnote">Just as Esther guarded her mouth (Esther 2:20) “and did not reveal her kindred or her people, as Mordechai had instructed her.”</i>

<b>One who gazes at women,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">575</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 92a; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah 4:4</i> even if he literally is equal in stature to Moshe, he will not be cleansed of the judgments of purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>). In the end he will come to sin with forbidden relations. He rouses the lusts of his evil inclination within himself, and will ultimately come to wasteful seminal emissions, the gravity of which will be explained in the sixth gate.
<b>One who derives benefit from the honor of the Torah</b> removes his life from the world and is liable of the death penalty. The incident with Rabbi Tarfon proves this.<sup class="footnote-marker">576</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Nedarim 62a</i> Namely, “A certain man found Rabbi Tarfon eating figs when most of the knives had already been set aside.<sup class="footnote-marker">577</sup><i class="footnote">That is, Rabbi Tarfon assumed that the figs were abandoned. (Rashi to Nedarim 62a ibid.)</i> He placed Rabbi Tarfon in a sack, lifted him up and carried him to throw him into the river. Rabbi Tarfon cried out and said, ‘Woe to Tarfon, for this man is killing him.’ When the man heard that it was Rabbi Tarfon, he left him and ran away. Rabbi Abahu said in the name of Rabbi Chananiyah ben Gamliel: All the days of that righteous man he was distressed over this matter, saying, ‘Woe is me, for I made use of the crown of Torah.’” As our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">578</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 4</i> “Do not make them into a crown for self-exaltation, nor a spade with which to dig… Whoever derives worldly benefit from the words of Torah, removes his life from the world.” In the end, such a person inherits purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>).
<b>Falsehood.</b> A person who speaks falsehood denies the God of Israel, giving credence to another god, called falsehood. A person such as this is in the category of those who shall not greet the countenance of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, the <i>Shechinah</i>. This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">579</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 101:7</i> “One who tells lies shall not be established before My eyes.” A person such as this is not considered to be included amongst the Jewish people, about whom it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">580</sup><i class="footnote">Zephaniah 3:13</i> “The remnant of Israel will not commit corruption, they will not speak falsehood, and a deceitful tongue will not be found in their mouth,” and the lifespan of such a person will be shortened.
In contrast, one who speaks truthfully lengthens his lifespan, as stated in Tractate Sanhedrin<sup class="footnote-marker">581</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 97a</i> about Rav Tavyomee that, “Even if they were to give him the entire world, his words would not deviate from the truth. Rava said: “Once, I happened to come to a certain place called Truth, the inhabitants of which never deviated from truth in their words, and no one ever died prematurely there. I married a woman there and she bore me two sons.” One day his wife was sitting and washing her hair and her neighbor came and knocked on the door. He thought, ‘It is improper to say that she is bathing,’ and he instead said, ‘She is not here.’ Because of this, his two sons died. The people of the place came and asked him, “What is the meaning of this?” He answered, explaining the nature of the incident. They said, “Please leave our place and do not provoke premature death upon these people.”
It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">582</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 9:4-8</i> “Each man lies to his fellow and they do not speak truth; they train their tongue to speak falsehood, striving to be iniquitous. Your dwelling is amid deceit; because of their deceit they refuse to know Me – the word of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>. Therefore, thus said <i>HaShem Tzva’ot</i>-<i>יהו״ה צבאו״ת</i>, I shall smelt them and I shall test them – for what [else] can I do for the daughter of My people? Their tongue is like a drawn arrow, speaking deceit; with his mouth a person speaks peace with his fellow, but within himself, he lays his ambush. Shall I not punish them for these things? – the word of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>. From a nation such as this, shall My soul not exact vengeance?”
The spies and the generation of the desert were only punished because of false testimony. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">583</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 92a (See Rashi)</i> “Whoever speaks deceitfully, it is as though he worships idolatry.” It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">584</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 6:16-19</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> hates these six, but the seventh is the abomination of His soul. Haughty eyes, a false tongue and hands that spill innocent blood. A heart that plots iniquitous thoughts, feet that run to do evil, a false witness who spouts lies, and one who stirs up strife among brothers.” The verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">585</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 9:4-8</i> “They do not speak truth… Shall I not punish them for these things?” It also is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">586</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 34:13</i> “Who is the man who desires life, who loves days of seeing good? Guard your tongue from speaking evil, and your lips from speaking deceit.”
Gechazi was only punished because he lied in the name of Elisha.<sup class="footnote-marker">587</sup><i class="footnote">Kings II 5:20-27; Midrash Tanchuma, Metzora 1:1</i> Amnon deceived Tamar, which led to him being killed.<sup class="footnote-marker">588</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel II 13:1-29</i> The spirit of Navot was sent out from before the Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, because he spoke deceitfully,<sup class="footnote-marker">589</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 102b; Zohar I 192b (Kings I 21:1-13)</i> as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">590</sup><i class="footnote">Kings 1 22:20-22</i> “And <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> said, ‘Who will lure Achav to go up [to war] that he may fall in Ramoth-Gilead?’ This one said, ‘Like this’ and this one said, ‘Like this!’ Then a spirit came forward and stood before <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> and said, ‘I shall lure him!’ And <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> said, ‘How?’ [The spirit] replied, ‘I will go out and be a spirit of falsehood in the mouths of all his prophets.’ He said, ‘You will lure him and you will succeed. Go out (<i>Tzei</i>-<i>צא</i>) and do so!’” What is the meaning of the term “Go out-<i>Tzei</i>-<i>צא</i>?” It means, “Get out of My presence!”<sup class="footnote-marker">591</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 102b ibid.; Zohar I 192b ibid. – That is, he was a liar in the first instance, and was thus expelled from the presence of HaShem-יהו״ה, blessed is He.</i>
Rav Huna said,<sup class="footnote-marker">592</sup><i class="footnote">Reishit Chochmah, Shaar HaKedushah, Ch. 12</i> “The Jewish people were only exiled from their land because they transgressed the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">593</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 23:7</i> ‘Distance yourself from a false word.’” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">594</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 14a</i> “Jerusalem was not destroyed until trustworthy men ceased to exist in it, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">595</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 5:1</i> ‘Walk about in the streets of Jerusalem, see now and know, and seek in its plazas; if you will find a man, if there is one who dispenses justice and seeks truth, then I will forgive her.’”
It states in Zohar,<sup class="footnote-marker">596</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 63, 95a</i> “About a time in which the Jewish people speak falsely about the Torah of Truth, the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">597</sup><i class="footnote">Daniel 8:12</i> ‘Truth was hurled to the ground.’ It is about such a time of exile that the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">598</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 59:15</i> ‘Truth became lacking,’ and falsehood reigns in the world. What is falsehood? That is <i>Sama’el</i>. This is what caused the destruction of both the first and second Holy Temples.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">599</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:18</i> “The world stands on three things: On Justice, Truth and Peace.” It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">600</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 15:1-2</i> “Who may sojourn in Your tent? One who speaks the truth in his heart.” That is, even when it comes to matters that he only thought in his heart, he must bring forth into action and actualize them truthfully, in accordance what our sages,<sup class="footnote-marker">601</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Batra 88a; Makkot 24a, and Rashi there, citing She’eltot d’Rav Acha (She’ilta 36) – The incident with Rav Safra is that he had placed an object for sale. A man came before him to purchase it when he was in the middle of reciting the Shema. The man named his price, but Rav Safra did not respond because he was in the middle of the Shema. The man thought that Rav Safra was not interested in selling it at that price, so he raised his purchase price. When Rav Safra concluded the Shema, he told the man that he would accept the original price, for that is the price that he was originally satisfied with. It is about him that the verse states (Psalms 15:2), “One who speaks the truth in his heart” is applied.</i> of blessed memory, taught regarding the incident with Rav Safra. It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">602</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 2:6</i> “The Torah of Truth was in his mouth, and injustice was not found on his lips… for he is an angel of <i>HaShem Tzva’ot</i>-יהו״ה צבאו״ת.”
<b>The flatterer </b>is amongst the four classes of people who shall not greet the countenance of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He (the <i>Shechinah</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">603</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 42a</i> This is because he denigrates the honor of the Ever Present One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, when he cajoles and flatters the wicked. This is as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">604</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 24:24</i> “One who tells a wicked person, ‘You are righteous,’ – the peoples shall curse him, the nations shall despise him.” Even if he flatters and cajoles a person who is not wicked, it nevertheless is as if he fears man and places his trust in man, as it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">605</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 17:5</i> “Accursed is the man who puts his trust in people.” Regarding such a person the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">606</sup><i class="footnote">Job 13:16; See Talmud Bavli, Sotah 42a ibid.</i> “The flatterer shall not come before Him.”
This accords with what our sages, of blessed memory, stated<sup class="footnote-marker">607</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 19a-19b</i> about the incident with King Yanai, that because the sages of the court of the Sanhedrin flattered and yielded to him in a minor way by not forcing him to stand during judgment, the angel Gavriel came and struck them to the ground and they died.<sup class="footnote-marker">608</sup><i class="footnote">A slave of King Yanai killed someone. The court sent word to him and he sent them the slave. They sent word back to him that he himself must come in person, as per the verse (Exodus 21:29), “He should be testified against, with his owner.” Yannai came and sat down. Shimon ben Shetach said to him: Yannai the King, stand on your feet and witnesses will testify against you. It is not before us that you will be standing, but it is before He who spoke and the world was, as it states (Deuteronomy 19:17), “Then both people, between whom the controversy is, shall stand.” Yannai answered: “I will not stand if you alone say this, but only according to what your colleagues say.” Shimon ben Shetach turned to his right, but the other judges lowered their faces to the ground and said nothing out of fear. He turned to his left, and they too forced their faces to the ground and said nothing out of fear. Shimon ben Shetach said to them: You are masters of thought! May the Master of thoughts come and punish you. Immediately, Gavriel came and struck those judges to the ground and they died. (Sanhedrin 19a-19b ibid.)</i> Similarly, when they flattered King Agrippa, who was righteous, the enemies of the Jewish people<sup class="footnote-marker">609</sup><i class="footnote">This is a euphemism for the Jewish people.</i> were sentenced to destruction.<sup class="footnote-marker">610</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 41a-b – King Agrippa rose and read from the Torah while standing, and the sages praised him for it (though a king can read while sitting). When he came to the verse (Deuteronomy 17:15), “You may not appoint a foreigner over you,” tears flowed from his eyes (since it excluded him from Kingship, being that he was a descendent of Herod). The assembled said to him: Fear not, Agrippa, for you are our brother. It was taught in the name of Rabbi Natan that in that moment, they were sentenced to destruction for having flattered Agrippa.</i>
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">611</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 113b</i> “The Holy One, blessed is He, hates three types of people: One who says one thing with his mouth but thinks another in his heart etc.” Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">612</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 41b</i> “Any person who has flattery in him falls into purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>), as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">613</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 5:20</i> ‘Woe to those who call evil good and good evil,’ the continuation of which states,<sup class="footnote-marker">614</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 5:24</i> ‘Therefore, as the tongue of fire devours straw, and as chaff is consumed by the flame, so will their root become rot and their flower will be blown away like dust etc.’”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">615</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 42a</i> “Any congregation in which there is flattery is as repulsive as a menstruating woman, as is stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">616</sup><i class="footnote">Job 15:34</i> ‘A flattering congregation will be forlorn.’” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">617</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 72b</i> “Any Torah scholar whose inside is not like his outside is not a Torah scholar and is called a loathsome abomination.” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">618</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 41b</i> “Any person who has flattery in him brings wrath to the world, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">619</sup><i class="footnote">Job 36:13</i> ‘Those with flattery in their hearts bring about wrath.’ Moreover, his prayers are despised and are not heard.” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">620</sup><i class="footnote">Sotah 41b ibid.</i> “Any person who has flattery in him, even fetuses in their mothers’ wombs curse him.” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated about the sin of flattery, that it will cause a person to fall into the hands of his enemies,<sup class="footnote-marker">621</sup><i class="footnote">Sotah 41b ibid.; Reishit Chochmah, Shaar HaKedushah 12:32</i> as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">622</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 10:6 </i> “I shall send them against a flattering people.”
Flattery and hypocrisy are just as bad as idolatry, forbidden relations, adultery and murder. From where do we learn that it is equal to idolatry? From the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">623</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 32:6</i> “For the vile person speaks villainy and his heart plans iniquity, to act with hypocrisy and to speak falsehood about <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.” From where do we learn that it is equal to forbidden relations and adultery? From the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">624</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 3:1</i> “If a man divorces his wife and she goes from him and is with another man, can he return to her again? Would that not surely bring the profound guilt of hypocrisy upon the land?” From where do we know that it is equal to murder? From the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">625</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 106:38</i> “They spilled innocent blood… and the land was polluted by the blood of hypocrisy.”
It is on account of the sin of flattery and hypocrisy that the rains are withheld.<sup class="footnote-marker">626</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Taanit 7b</i> On account of the sin of flattery and hypocrisy, one is judged in purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>) eternally, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">627</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 33:14</i> “Sinners were afraid in Zion; trembling seized hypocrites, [saying], ‘Which of us can live with the consuming fire? Which of us can live with the never-dying blaze?’” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated<sup class="footnote-marker">628</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanedrin 101b</i> that the only reason Yeravam merited kingship was because he did not flatteringly yield to Solomon.
<b>Fraud </b>has two great evils. The first is that it is similar to the matter of falsehood and hypocrisy, and the second is that it is like theft and deception. In doing so, he denigrates the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, and thinks to himself that the Holy One, blessed is He, does not see his deception, God forbid. It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">629</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 25:17</i> “Each of you shall not defraud his fellow, and you shall fear your God, for I am <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God,” and it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">630</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 19:35</i> “You shall not commit a perversion of justice, in measures of length, weight, or volume. You shall have correct scales, correct weights, correct dry measures, and correct liquid measures – I am <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God.” At the beginning of one’s judgement after passing from this world, he is asked, “Did you conduct your business faithfully?”<sup class="footnote-marker">631</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 31a – That is, with honesty and integrity.</i>
One who defrauds is amongst the four classes of people who do not receive the countenance of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He (the <i>Shechinah</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">632</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 42a; Sanhedrin 103a</i> This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">633</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 101:7</i> “In the midst of My house shall not dwell a practitioner of deceit; one who tells lies shall not be established before My eyes.” As stated before, in the section on falsehood,<sup class="footnote-marker">634</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 14a</i> “Jerusalem was not destroyed until trustworthy men ceased to exist in it.” In contrast, regarding one who conducts himself faithfully, with honesty and integrity, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">635</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 15:1</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, who may sojourn in Your tent? Who may dwell on Your holy mountain? One who walks in perfect innocence, who does what is right and speaks the truth from his heart.” 
Similarly, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">636</sup><i class="footnote">See Rashi and the other commentators to Proverbs 28:20; Shemot Rabba 51:1; Zohar I 199b; Reishit Chochmah, Masa uMatan b’Emunah Ch. 2; Also see Mechilta d’Rabbi Yishmael 15:26; Ramban to Exodus 15:26; Sefer Chassidim 1062, and elsewhere.</i> “The verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">637</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 28:20</i> ‘A man of integrity will increase blessings,’ refers to one who conducts his business in good faith. Such a person’s possessions will be increased, and the Holy One, blessed is He, will arrange his financial sustenance.” Moreover, such a person is called a righteous <i>Tzaddik</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">638</sup><i class="footnote">Reishit Chochmah, Masa uMatan b’Emunah, Ch. 2 ibid.</i> as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">639</sup><i class="footnote">Habakkuk 2:4</i> “The righteous (<i>Tzaddik</i>) shall live by his faith.” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">640</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Makkot 24a</i> “There are six-hundred and thirteen commandments, but Chabakkuk came and established them upon one, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">641</sup><i class="footnote">Habakkuk 2:4 ibid.</i> ‘The righteous (<i>Tzaddik</i>) shall live by his faith.’”

Shaar 6

Gate Six
<b>The punishments for transgressing the negative commandments</b>
<b>Causing a desecration of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He</b>, is worse than all sins.<sup class="footnote-marker">642</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 22:32; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah, Ch. 5</i> Our sages, of blessed memory, stated in regard to the matter of the four categories of atonement,<sup class="footnote-marker">643</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 86a</i> “One who has caused a desecration of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, his repentance has no power to suspend punishment, nor does Yom Kippur atone for his sin, nor does suffering have the power to absolve him. Rather, it is only by his death that he will be cleansed, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">644</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 22:14</i> ‘This sin will never be atoned for you until you die.’”
<b>Relations with a menstruating woman</b>, is punished with excision (<i>Karet</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">645</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 18:19; Leviticus 20:18; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Issurei Biyah, Ch. 1, Ch. 4</i> Aside for that, it states in Zohar,<sup class="footnote-marker">646</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 3a-b</i> “There are three types of people who push the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He (the <i>Shechinah</i>) from the world. When such people cry out in prayer, their voices are not heard. These are them: One who has relations with a menstruating woman, for there is no greater impurity in the world than the impurity of relations with a menstruating woman.”

<b>Shabbat</b> is known to be equal to all of the <i>mitzvot</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">647</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Shemot Rabba 25:12</i> Even the wicked are granted respite on Shabbat and the fires of purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>) are dimmed for them. However, when it comes to those who transgress Shabbat, their fires are not dimmed even on Shabbat.<sup class="footnote-marker">648</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 24, 69b</i> Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">649</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 118b; Also see Shemot Rabba 25:12 ibid.</i> “If only the Jewish people would keep two [consecutive] Shabbats in accordance with the <i>Halachah</i>-Torah law, they would be immediately redeemed.” Our sages, of blessed memory, also stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">650</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 118b ibid.; Also see Tzava’at HaRivash translated as The Way of The Baal Shem Tov, Section 18.</i> “Anyone who observes Shabbat in accordance with its laws, even if he is an idolater like the generation of Enosh, he is forgiven, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">651</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 52:6</i> ‘Praiseworthy is the man (<i>Enosh</i>-אנוש) who does this and the person who grasps it tightly, who guards the Shabbat against desecration (<i>Meichalelo</i>-מחללו).’ Do not read it ‘against desecration (<i>Meichalelo</i>-מחללו),’ but rather, ‘he is forgiven (<i>Machul Lo</i>-מחול לו).’” It likewise is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">652</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 58:13</i> “If you restrain your foot because it is the Shabbat, refrain from accomplishing your own desires on My holy day; If you proclaim the Shabbat ‘a delight,’ and the holy [day] of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה ‘honored,’ and you honor it by not engaging in your own affairs, from seeking your own needs or discussing the forbidden – then you will delight in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, and I will mount you astride the heights of the world; I will provide you the heritage of your forefather Yaakov, for the mouth of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה has spoken.”
<b>The consumption of forbidden fats and blood</b> are known to be amongst the transgressions that are punished with excision (<i>Karet</i>),<sup class="footnote-marker">653</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 7:25-27; Mishneh Torah, Ma’achalot Asurot, Ch. 6-7.</i> and cause the soul to become detestable.
<b>With regard to one who makes use of the Holy Names,</b> our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">654</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 1:13; 4:5</i> “One who makes use of the Crown, shall perish,” in that either he or his offspring will become apostates, or he and his offspring will die, or he and his offspring shall become impoverished.<sup class="footnote-marker">655</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Avot d’Rabbi Natan, Ch. 12; Sefer Mitzvot Gadol, Positive Commandment 12 and the citations there.</i>
<b>One who treats a Torah scholar with contempt, and one who is an informer,</b> are amongst those that have no portion in the coming world, and who shall not rise in the resurrection of the dead.<sup class="footnote-marker">656</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 99b; Shulchan Aruch, Choshen Mishpat 388:10</i>
<b>Wasteful seminal emissions </b>are worse than spilling the blood of others,<sup class="footnote-marker">657</sup><i class="footnote">Since in this case he is spilling the blood of his own offspring (Zohar I 219b). </i> for in doing so, he is spilling not only their blood, but the blood of all their future generations without end.<sup class="footnote-marker">658</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Niddah 13a; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Issurei Biyah 21:18; Shulachan Aruch, Even HaEzer, Siman 23</i> In Zohar to Parshat Vayechi it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">659</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 219b ibid.</i> “One is able to repent for all transgressions except for this.” Moreover, when it comes to all other transgressions, a minor is exempt from punishment, except for this. For, Er and Onan were minors who were only about seven years old,<sup class="footnote-marker">660</sup><i class="footnote">Seder HaDorot, Year 2217</i> and yet they died at the hands of Heaven on account of this sin,<sup class="footnote-marker">661</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 38:7-10; Yevamot 34b; Midrash Bereishit Rabba 85:5; Tractate Kallah 4:6</i> even though they were not yet commanded regarding the <i>mitzvot</i>. The same is likewise true of the generation of the flood, about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">662</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 6:12 – The words “For all flesh destroyed its ways upon the earth” refers to their wasteful seminal emissions (Zohar I 62a).</i> “For all flesh destroyed its ways upon the earth.” Because of this sin, all creatures were blotted out, everything from man to beast, birds of the sky and insects,<sup class="footnote-marker">663</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 7:23</i> and even the first three handsbreadths of the earth were destroyed<sup class="footnote-marker">664</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Bereishit Rabba 31:7</i> – something that had not occurred from the beginning of creation until that point, and which shall not occur again.<sup class="footnote-marker">665</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 8:21</i> Moreover, this took place even though they were commanded only a mere seven <i>mitzvot</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">666</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 56a; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Melachim u’Milchamot 8:11</i>
<b>The consumption of forbidden foods</b> is known to cause the soul to become abominable, as is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">667</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 11:43</i> “Do not make your souls abominable by means of any teeming thing; do not contaminate yourselves through them, lest you become contaminated through them.” One who stays away from the consumption of forbidden foods is called holy (<i>Kadosh</i>-קדוש), as written in the continuing verses,<sup class="footnote-marker">668</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 11:44-45</i> “You are to sanctify yourselves and you shall be holy, for I am Holy; and you shall not contaminate yourselves through any teeming thing that creeps on the earth. For I am <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה Who elevates you from the land of Egypt to be a God unto you; you shall be holy, for I am Holy.” You have already been informed to know that it is holiness (<i>Kedushah</i>) that brings to the Holy spirit of Divine Inspiration (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>).
<b>Regarding oaths</b> that are taken in vain or in falsehood, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">669</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shevuot 39a</i> “When the Holy One, blessed is He, said at Sinai,<sup class="footnote-marker">670</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 20:7</i> ‘You shall not bear the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God, in vain,’ the entire world trembled.” This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">671</sup><i class="footnote">Job 9:6</i> “Who shakes the earth from its place, and its pillars tremble,” and the waters of the abyss wish to ascend and flood the entire world etc. Our sages,<sup class="footnote-marker">672</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shevuot 39a ibid.</i> of blessed memory, stated about this sin, “In regard to all other transgressions in Torah, it states that it is possible to be cleansed (<i>v’Nakeh</i>-ונקה), whereas here, it is stated that he ‘will not be cleansed (<i>Lo Yenakeh</i>-לא ינקה).’ Moreover, for all other transgressions in Torah, punishment is exacted only from the transgressor, whereas here, punishment is exacted from him and from his family, and from the entire world,”<sup class="footnote-marker">673</sup><i class="footnote">See also Rif to Shevuot 18a-b; Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim 87:20 </i> even if it is in truth. Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">674</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Gittin 57a; Midrash Bamidbar Rabba 22:1</i> “King Yannai had six-hundred thousand towns on the King’s Mountain, and they were all destroyed because of oaths that were taken in truth, even though they fulfilled them.”
Our sages, of blessed memory, stated about Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi,<sup class="footnote-marker">675</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Ketubot 77b – When Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi was on the verge of dying, they said to the angel of death, “Go and do his bidding.” When the angel of death appeared to him, he said, “Show me my place in the Garden of Eden.” The angel of death responded, “Very well.” Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi said to him, “Give me your knife, lest you frighten me on the way,” and he gave it to him. When he arrived there, he lifted Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi so he could see his place, and he jumped and fell into that place. The angel of death grabbed onto him by the corner of his cloak. Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi said to him, “I swear that I will not come with you.” The Holy One, blessed is He, said to the angel of death, “If he ever requested dissolution of an oath, then he must return with you, but if not, then he need not return.” The angel of death said to Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi, “At least give me back my knife,” but he did not give it to him. A Supernal voice came forth and said to him, “Give it to him, as it is necessary to the created beings.”</i> that “The Holy One, blessed is He, told the angel of death, see if in all his days he requested dissolution of an oath, and if he has, then you may take him out of the Garden of Eden, but if not, then leave him. They checked and found that not only did he never ask for dissolution of an oath, but in all his days, he never took an oath.”

Shaar 7

Gate Seven
<b>The fulfillment of the positive commandments, and good practices</b>
<b>Tzitzit: </b>You already are aware that the <i>mitzvah</i> of Tzitzit (ציצית) is equal to all the <i>mitzvot</i> of the Torah.<sup class="footnote-marker">676</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Nedarim 25a</i> The word Tzitzit (ציצית) has the numerical value of 600, and together with the 8 threads and 5 knots, equals 613.<sup class="footnote-marker">677</sup><i class="footnote">Rashi to Numbers 15:39 and elsewhere.</i> Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">678</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 15:39</i> “You will see it and remember all of the commandments of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה,” thus teaching us that Torah equates the Tzitzit to all the <i>mitzvot</i>.
<b>Tefillin:</b> Whoever does not fulfill this <i>mitzvah</i> is called “A skull that has not donned Tefillin,” and will not rise in the resurrection of the dead.<sup class="footnote-marker">679</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i> However, all destructive forces and the nations of the world are in fear of one who dons them, and about him the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">680</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 28:10</i> “Then all the peoples of the earth will see that the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is proclaimed over you, and they will fear you,” as Rabbi Eliezer says,<sup class="footnote-marker">681</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 6a, 56a, and elsewhere.</i> “This verse refers to the Tefillin of the head.” Regarding the coming future it states about such people,<sup class="footnote-marker">682</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 17a</i> “In the coming world the righteous sit with their crowns upon their heads, delighting in the radiance of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>).”
<b>The <i>Shema</i> recital:</b> You already are aware that this is the <i>mitzvah</i> of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו״ה unity, blessed is He, which is the root of all of the commandments.<sup class="footnote-marker">683</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah, Ch. 1</i> The <i>Shema</i> recital consists of 248 words, for through its recital, the 248 limbs and organs of one’s soul undergo repair.<sup class="footnote-marker">684</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar Chadash Ruth 95a; Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim 61:3</i> Our sages, of blessed memory, also stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">685</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Tehillim 1:15; Also see Talmud Bavli, Menachot 99b</i> “Whoever recites the <i>Shema</i> twice every day, it is as if he fulfills the entire Torah, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">686</sup><i class="footnote">Joshua 1:8 (See Rashi)</i> “You shall contemplate it day and night.”
<b>Prayer:</b> Our sages, of blessed memory, said about prayer,<sup class="footnote-marker">687</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 6b</i> “These are matters that ascend to the loftiest heights of the world, and yet people treat them as unimportant and insignificant.” You already are aware that prayer is greater than all the sacrificial offerings,<sup class="footnote-marker">688</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Tanchuma, Vayera 1:6</i> as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">689</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 1:11</i> “Why do I need your numerous sacrifices?” The continuation is, “Even if you were to increase your prayers etc.,” indicating that prayer is greater than them all. Just as the sacrificial offerings bring atonement, so likewise, prayer brings atonement for a person’s transgressions.<sup class="footnote-marker">690</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Brachot 26b</i> In Zohar to Parshat Vayakhel it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">691</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 201a-b</i> “Serving the Creator in prayer is greater and more precious than all other forms of service, including all the sacrificial offerings.”
<b>Bringing merit to the guilty:</b> Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">692</sup><i class="footnote">Tanna d’Bei Eliyahu Rabba, Ch. 8</i> “Elkana merited having his son Shmuel – who was equal to Moshe and Aharon<sup class="footnote-marker">693</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 31b</i> – because he would go up [to the Tabernacle at Shiloh] for every Festival, and would bring multitudes of people with him, thus bringing merit upon them.” His son Shmuel followed this practice, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">694</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 7:16-17</i> “He would travel year after year, circling to Beth-El, Gilgal and Mitzpah, and judging Israel in all these places. He then would return to Ramah, for his home was there, and there he would judge Israel. And there he built an altar to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.” Similarly, our forefather Avraham, peace be upon him, only merited all his exalted levels on account of what is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">695</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 12:5</i> “The souls that they made in Choran.” Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">696</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 18:18-19</i> “Avraham shall surely be a great and mighty nation and all the nations of the world will be blessed in him. For I know him, that he will command his children and his household after him, to keep the way of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, doing charity and justice etc.” Moreover, the leaders of every generation are either rewarded or punished only in regard to this matter.
The Zohar at the beginning of Parshat Terumah, greatly lauds the praise of this <i>mitzvah</i>, stating,<sup class="footnote-marker">697</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 128b</i> “The righteous and meritorious must chase after the guilty and acquire them at full price, to remove the contamination of their sins from them, thus restraining and humbling the opposite of holiness (<i>Sitra Achara</i>). He must toil to repair the soul of the guilty, and this will be considered as if he created them. This brings praise to the glory of the Holy One, blessed is He, over and above all other praises and causes Him to be elevated more than anything else. Regarding this the verse states about Aharon,<sup class="footnote-marker">698</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 2:6</i> ‘He returned many from iniquity,’ and it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">699</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 2:5</i> ‘My covenant was with him, life and peace; I gave these to him for the sake of the fear with which he feared Me, for he was in awe of My Name.’ Such a person is caused to be uplifted in three elevations, which other’s do not attain by virtue of the other <i>mitzvot</i>. About such a person the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">700</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 2:5 ibid.</i> ‘My covenant was with him, life and peace,’ and he merits to see his children and children of his children. He is meritorious both in this world and the coming world. No accusing forces can judge him in this world, and he enters into the twelve portals of the firmament in the coming world, and none can restrain his hand. About him the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">701</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 112:2-4</i> “His offspring will be mighty in the land, a generation of the upright who shall be blessed. Wealth and riches are in his house and his righteousness endures forever. Even in darkness, light shines for the upright.’ The Holy One, blessed is He, blesses the form of such a righteous person with all seven blessings that He blessed Avraham with, when he did this and rectified the wicked of his generation. Such a person enters into the seven hidden worlds, which no one, except for those who do this and repair the souls of the guilty, merit. If only people would know the beneficence of such deeds and the merit they bring to the righteous-<i>Tzaddikim</i> for bringing merit to the guilty, they would pursue this as one pursues life itself.”

<b>Doing one’s business in good faith</b> has already been discussed before regarding the matter of fraud.<sup class="footnote-marker">702</sup><i class="footnote">In the fifth gate of this section.</i> Review that section in depth. As has already been explained, know that upon death, at the beginning of one’s judgement he is asked,<sup class="footnote-marker">703</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 31a – That is, with honesty and integrity.</i> “Did you conduct your business faithfully?” 
<b>Charity</b> is explained by the prophet Yishayahu,<sup class="footnote-marker">704</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 58:7-9</i> “Surely, you should break your bread for the hungry and bring the moaning poor to your home; when you see a naked person, clothe him; and do not hide yourself from your kin. Then your light will burst out like the dawn and your healing will speedily sprout; your righteous deed will precede you and the glory of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה will gather you in. Then you will call and <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה will answer; you will cry out and He will respond, ‘Here I am!’” Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">705</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 15:10</i> “You shall surely give him, and let your heart not feel bad when you give him, for because of this matter, <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> your God, will bless you in all your deeds and in your every undertaking.” Similarly, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">706</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 21:14</i> “An anonymous gift will cover over anger,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">707</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 10:2</i> “Charity rescues from death.” Likewise, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">708</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 111:3; 112:3</i> “His charity endures forever.” That is, there is no sin that can extinguish it, as with the other <i>mitzvot</i>, and it brings life to a person, as in the incident of Binyamin the righteous, mentioned by our sages, of blessed memory.<sup class="footnote-marker">709</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Batra 11a – It was said about Binyamin the righteous, who was appointed over the charity fund: Once, a woman came before him during the years of drought and said to him, “My master, sustain me.” He said to her, “I swear by the Temple service that there is nothing left in the charity fund.” She said to him, “My master, if you do not sustain me, a woman and her seven sons will die.” He arose and sustained her with his own funds. A while later he fell deathly ill. The ministering angels said to the Holy One, blessed is He, “Have You not said that anyone who saves a single life in Israel, is regarded as if he has saved the entire world? Should Binyamin the righteous, who saved a woman and her seven sons, die after only having lived a few years?” They immediately tore up his death sentence, and it was taught that twenty-two years were added to his lifespan.</i>
<b>Honoring the Shabbat:</b> As you know, Shabbat is equal to the entire Torah,<sup class="footnote-marker">710</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Shemot Rabba 25:12</i> as explained at the beginning of this gate. Review that section in depth. It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">711</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 58:13</i> “If you restrain your foot because it is Shabbat, refrain from accomplishing your own desires on My holy day; If you proclaim the Shabbat ‘a delight,’ and the holy [day] of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה ‘honored,’ and you honor it by not engaging in your own affairs, from seeking your own needs or discussing the forbidden – then you will delight in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, and I will mount you astride the heights of the world; I will provide you the heritage of your forefather Yaakov, for the mouth of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה has spoken.” You are familiar with the well-known story of Yosef who cherishes Shabbat (<i>Yosef Mokir Shabbat</i>),<sup class="footnote-marker">712</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 119a – The Talmud related a story of Yosef who cherishes Shabbat: There was a gentile on his property was extremely plentiful. The astrologers told him that all of his property would be consumed by Yosef who cherishes Shabbat. He went and sold all his property, bought a precious pearl, and placed it in his hat. When he was crossing a river in a ferry, the wind blew off his hat and cast it into the water, and a fish swallowed it. The fish was caught and brought to shore right before Shabbat eve. The fishermen said, “Who buys fish at a time like this?” The people said, “Go bring it to Yosef who cherishes Shabbat, as he regularly purchases delicacies for Shabbat.” They brought it to him and he purchased it, and when he opened the fish, he found the pearl inside. He later sold it for thirteen vessels filled with golden dinars. An elderly man encountered him and said, “One who lends to Shabbat, Shabbat repays him.”</i> who on account of honoring Shabbat, merited inheriting the great wealth of his gentile neighbor. Similarly, there is the story<sup class="footnote-marker">713</sup><i class="footnote">Shabbat 119a ibid.</i> of Rabbi Chiya bar Abba, who was the guest of a certain man in Laodicea who would eat his Shabbat meals on a table made of gold, affixed with sixteen chains of silver. This table was so heavy that sixteen people were needed to carry it, and it was laden with bowls, cups, pitchers and flasks, and every kind of food, delicacy and fragrant spice created in the six days of creation. When Rabbi Chiya bar Abba asked him what he had done to merit all of this, he responded, “I was a slaughterer, and from the choicest parts of the finest animals I would say, ‘This will be for Shabbat!’” Our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">714</sup><i class="footnote">Shabbat 119a ibid.</i> “By what virtue do the wealthy who live outside of the Land of Israel merit their wealth? Because they honor and delight in the Shabbat!”
<b>Circumcising one’s son:</b> If you understood our explanation of the greatness of bringing merit to the guilty and the limitless reward brought about by such deeds, then how much more so is this the case regarding bringing one’s own son under the wings of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>), in that one’s responsibility toward his family, takes precedence over others.
<b>Acts of loving-kindness, visiting the sick, bringing peace, and welcoming guests,</b> are amongst the <i>mitzvot</i> that a person eats of their fruits in this world, while the principal remains for him in the coming world.<sup class="footnote-marker">715</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Pe’ah 1:1</i> About anyone who engages in Torah study and acts of lovingkindness, the Holy One, blessed is He, says,<sup class="footnote-marker">716</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 8a</i> “I ascribe him credit as if he redeemed Me and My children from among the nations of the world.” This is the character trait of Avraham, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">717</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:20</i> “Give truth to Yaakov, kindness to Avraham.” It is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">718</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 21:21</i> “One who pursues charity and kindness will find life, righteousness and honor.”
It is taught<sup class="footnote-marker">719</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 18a (See Rashi)</i> that Rabba bar Nachmeinee and Abaye both came from the house of Eli.<sup class="footnote-marker">720</sup><i class="footnote">The House of Eli was subject to a curse that its members would die young and would not be atoned for through sacrificial offerings (Samuel I 3:11-14). The Talmud discusses other means by which members of the House of Eli were able to bring about atonement and prolonged their lives, such as through the study of Torah and acts of lovingkindness.</i> Rabba bar Nachmeinee who engaged almost exclusively in Torah, lived for forty years, whereas his student, Abaye, lived twenty years longer because he engaged both in Torah study and acts of lovingkindness. Acts of goodness and kindness save a person from the judgments of purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>) as well as the judgments of the torments of the grave (<i>Chibut HaKever</i>), as mentioned before in the second gate.
<b>Set times for Torah study:</b> In the fifth gate, we already explained the sin of frivolity, and as well known, the study of Torah is equal to all the <i>mitzvot</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">721</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Pe’ah 1:1</i> Additionally, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">722</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 7a</i> “The beginning of a person’s judgment is only that he judged concerning the study of Torah, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">723</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 17:14</i> ‘The exemption from waters is the beginning of judgment.’”<sup class="footnote-marker">724</sup><i class="footnote">The term “release-Poter-פוטר” here means that he exempts himself from the waters, which refers to Torah study. The term “Madon-מדון” which means “strife,” is also of the root “judgement-Din-דין” as the Talmud here indicates. Thus, the verse is understood to mean, “Excusing oneself from Torah study is the beginning of judgment.” (See Rashi to Talmud Bavli, Kiddushin 40b.)</i>
<b>Good Practices:</b>
<b>Reciting the <i>Shema</i> upon retiring to sleep:</b> Know what our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">725</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 212a-b</i> “One who recites the <i>Shema</i> upon his bed kills myriads of destructive forces found at night, particularly when his soul ascends above. This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">726</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 149:5-6</i> ‘Let the pious (<i>Chassidim</i>) exalt in glory, let them sing joyously upon their beds. The praises of exaltation of God are in their throats, and a double-edged sword is in their hand.’”
