<b>Arising after midnight:</b><sup class="footnote-marker">727</sup><i class="footnote">To pray the Tikkun Chatzot prayer and to study Torah.</i> Firstly, by engaging in this practice he is counted among those who mourn for Zion and Jerusalem, about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">728</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 66:10</i> “Be glad in Jerusalem and rejoice in her, all you who love her, exult with her in jubilation, all you who mourn for her.” For, it is at that hour that the Holy One, blessed is He, also mourns and roars like a lion.<sup class="footnote-marker">729</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 3a</i> Moreover, in regard to one’s study of Torah at that hour, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">730</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Shemot Rabba 47:5; Vayikra Rabba 19:1</i> “The exaltation in the Torah is only at night.” Additionally, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">731</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Avoda Zarah 3b; Midrash Mishlei 31:3; Tanna d’Bei Eliyahu Zuta, Pirke Derech Eretz 2</i> “Whoever occupies himself with Torah study at night, the Holy One, blessed is He, extends a thread of kindness upon him by day.” Our sages, of blessed memory, also stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">732</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Tamid 32b</i> “Anyone who occupies himself with Torah study at night, the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה (the <i>Shechinah</i>), is opposite him. The verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">733</sup><i class="footnote">Lamentations 2:19 – In reference to Torah study (Shemot Rabba 47:5).</i> “Arise! Exalt in the night, at the beginning of the watches!” King David, peace be upon him, only merited to live in this world and in the coming world on account of this practice,<sup class="footnote-marker">734</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 3b-4a and elsewhere.</i> as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">735</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 119:62</i> “At midnight I arise to thank You for Your righteous ordinances.” The book of Zohar is filled with explanations praising this <i>mitzvah</i> to no end, and the Holy Spirit of Divine Inspiration (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) dwells upon such a person, as mentioned there in Parshat Shemot.<sup class="footnote-marker">736</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 18b</i>

Shaar 8

Gate Eight
The Gate of Repentance Which divides into three sections:
Section One: The Positive Commandments
The gravest of the positive commandments are the <i>mitzvah</i> of offering the Paschal Lamb (<i>Korban Pesach</i>) and the <i>mitzvah</i> of circumcision. The nullification of either of these two commandments results in excision (<i>Karet</i>). Even more severe is the nullification of positive commandments that are punished with excision (<i>Karet</i>) and also violate a negative commandment, such as the <i>mitzvah</i> to fast and desist from all prohibited forms of labor on Yom Kippur (The Day of Atonement). Higher than this is the <i>mitzvah</i> of resting from all prohibited forms of labor on Shabbat, as nullifying this <i>mitzvah</i> is both a negative prohibition and is punishable by stoning (<i>Skilah</i>). Higher than this is the <i>mitzvah</i> to procreate, that is, to be fruitful and multiply. For even if a person is full of Torah and <i>mitzvot</i>, like King Chizkiyahu,<sup class="footnote-marker">737</sup><i class="footnote">See Kings II 18:5 – The Torah attests about King Chizkiyahu, “He trusted in HaShem-יהו״ה, the God of Israel; after him there was not anyone like him among all the kings of Yehudah, nor among those who preceded him.”</i> he will die in this world and not live in the coming world, because he abstained from procreating.<sup class="footnote-marker">738</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Brachot 10a – Notwithstanding his greatness, he was told (by HaShem-יהו"ה through His prophet Yishayahu) that because he did not bear children (since he saw with the Holy Spirit (Ru’ach HaKodesh) that his children would not be virtuous), (Isaiah 38:1), “You shall die and shall not live,” meaning, “You will die in this world and will not live in the coming world.” He indeed repented and rectified this, and thus fifteen years were added to his life.</i> This is also the case in regard to the <i>positive</i> <i>mitzvah</i> of donning Tefillin. That is, a skull that has never donned Tefillin shall not rise in the time of the resurrection and is called a rebellious Jew who sins with his body.<sup class="footnote-marker">739</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i> Greater than all these is a person who abrogates the covenant of the circumcision<sup class="footnote-marker">740</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 85b; Shevuot 13a; Sanhedrin 99a; Avot d’Rabbi Natan, Ch. 26, and elsewhere.</i> in order to cause anger.
It is a positive commandment to know that there is a God, and one who denies this primary foundation has no share in the coming world.<sup class="footnote-marker">741</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Yesodei HaTorah (Foundations of the Torah), 1:1-6</i>
There are also <i>mitzvot</i> that one eats of the fruit in this world, while the principal remains for the coming world.<sup class="footnote-marker">742</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Pe’ah 1:1; Also see Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 127a and elsewhere.</i> These include honoring one’s father and mother, acts of kindness for the poor and the rich, both through physical action and with one’s money, bringing joy to a bride and groom, visiting the sick, burying the dead and comforting mourners, clothing the naked, welcoming guests, praying with concentration and devotional intent, bringing peace between one person and another and certainly between himself and his fellow, as well as judging one’s fellow favorably. The study of Torah is equal to them all. Included in this category is rising early to the house of prayer, and raising one’s sons by guiding them to study Torah.
Section Two: Regarding the punishments for forbidden character traits, and punishments for transgressing the negative commandments
There are two character traits that are the gravest of all. The first is anger, which is equal to idolatry,<sup class="footnote-marker">743</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot De’ot 2:3; Zohar I 27b; Zohar II 182b; Zohar III 179b, 234b; Tikkunim 89b; Zohar Chadash Noach</i> about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">744</sup><i class="footnote">Job 18:4</i> “You who tears his soul apart in his anger,” causing his soul to be uprooted and to depart, and to be replaced with another evil soul.
The second is arrogance and haughtiness which is higher and worse than anger. It is equal to idolatry, and he is compared to an <i>Ashera</i> tree, <sup class="footnote-marker">745</sup><i class="footnote">This was a grove used for the ancient idolatry of tree worship.</i> and is like one who stands in denial of the fundamental truth of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה existence, and it is as if he violated every one of the forbidden sexual relations, and his dust will not stir at the time of the resurrection of the dead.<sup class="footnote-marker">746</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sotah 5a</i> Nevertheless, when it comes to the punishment for the negative commandments, these are prohibitions for which one does not receive lashes, similar to a prohibitive commandment that has no action and that is transformable through a positive commandment.<sup class="footnote-marker">747</sup><i class="footnote">An example of this is the negative commandment (Deuteronomy 2:6), “Do not take the mother [bird] together with the young.” If he violates this and takes the mother with the young, it is repairable by (Deuteronomy 22:7), “You shall surely send the mother,” which is a positive commandment. One is thus not administered lashes by the violation of the prohibition when he is still able to fulfill the positive commandment. (See Me’iri to Talmud Bavli, Makkot 13a and elsewhere.)</i>
These two categories, as well as the nullification of all positive commandments except for those severe ones that we previously mentioned, are called minor transgressions (<i>Aveirot Kalot</i>). All of the severe positive commandments that we mentioned before, and all of the negative commandments except for these two categories that we mentioned, are called severe transgressions, in which there are many levels. They are all the sins for which one is liable for excision (<i>Karet</i>) and death by the hands of Heaven or death administered by the court.
However, when it comes to the transgression of the commandment,<sup class="footnote-marker">748</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 20:7</i> “You shall not bear the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God, in vain,” even though it is not punishable by excision (<i>Karet</i>), in a different respect it is more severe than all other commandments. This is because retribution is exacted on him as well as his family and the entire world, even including those who are not in a position to admonish him.
About the matter of desecrating the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, our sages, of blessed memory, stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">749</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 87a - “His repentance does not have the power to suspend his judgment, nor does the day of Yom Kippur have the power to atone for his sin, nor does suffering alone have the power to absolve him. Rather, all these suspend punishment and death absolves him, as is written (Isaiah 22:14), ‘And HaShem Tzva’ot-יהו״ה צבאו״ת revealed Himself to my ears: This sin will never be atoned for you until you die.’”</i> “To what extent does the desecration of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה go? Rav said: For me, it would be if I would take meat from a butcher and not pay him immediately. Rabbi Yochanan said: For me, it would be if I would walk four cubits without the Torah and without wearing Tefillin due to bodily weakness, for those who would see me would not know that it is due to my weakness. They would learn from my behavior, causing a nullification of Torah study and the fulfillment of the <i>mitzvah</i> of Tefillin.<sup class="footnote-marker">750</sup><i class="footnote">See Rashi to Yoma 87a ibid.</i> Rabbi Yanai said: Anything that causes one’s friends to become embarrassed because of his reputation, this is a desecration of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה. Abaye said: It is as taught about the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">751</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:5</i> ‘And you shall love <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה your God,’ that the Name of Heaven should become beloved by your hand. This means that a person should read Torah, study Mishnah, serve and study from Torah scholars, conduct his business transactions faithfully and be pleasant with people. However, if he does all the above, except not conduct his business dealings in good faith, and does not speak pleasantly with others, the Name of Heaven is desecrated by his hand.”
In regard to all of the above, if he died without repenting, he is judged in purgatory (<i>Gehinnom</i>). However, in the end, he rises and ascends from there, is reparable and has a portion in the resurrection of the dead and in the coming world.<sup class="footnote-marker">752</sup><i class="footnote">Tosefta Sanhedrin 13</i>
Higher and worse than this, are those who are called rebellious Jews who sin with their bodies (<i>Poshei Yisroel b’Gufam</i>), such as a skull that has never donned Tefillin because he is too lazy to don them, even though he can.<sup class="footnote-marker">753</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i> For, if his intention was to cause anger, then he is said to be in the category of the atheist (<i>Min</i>), or at the very least an apostate (<i>Mumar</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">754</sup><i class="footnote">For the distinctions as to these classifications, see Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah (Repentance), Ch. 3, and elsewhere.</i> If such a person dies without repentance, he is judged in purgatory (<i>Gehinom</i>) for twelve months, after which his body is destroyed and his soul is burned and becomes ashes under the souls of the feet of the righteous in the coming world.<sup class="footnote-marker">755</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a ibid.</i>
Higher and worse than this are those who have no portion whatsoever in the coming world. Even when purgatory (<i>Gehinom</i>) itself ceases, their punishment does not cease.<sup class="footnote-marker">756</sup><i class="footnote">Rosh HaShanah 17a ibid., and elsewhere.</i> This applies even if they possess Torah and good deeds, but died without repenting, like Doeg the Edomite, the mighty of the shepherds.<sup class="footnote-marker">757</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 21:8</i> This category includes the atheists (<i>Minim</i>), and students who alter the words of Torah to fit their atheism.<sup class="footnote-marker">758</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:11; Yoma 85b, and Rashi there.</i> The same applies to one a person who is an apostate (<i>Mumar</i>) with only the single transgression of idolatry, even though he acknowledges the truth of all the <i>mitzvot</i> and is known to fulfill them all constantly.
The category of apostates (<i>Minim</i>) also includes the following:<sup class="footnote-marker">759</sup><i class="footnote">See Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah, Ch. 3 ibid.; Mishnah Sanhedrin 10:1; Tamud Bavli, Sanhedrin 90a; Talmud Yerushalmi, Pe’ah 1:1; and elsewhere.</i> This category includes even a person who is only an apostate in regard to a single commandment and transgresses only that one commandment as an act of rebellion; or even if he only does so to satisfy his lust; and similarly, one who casts off the yoke of Heaven, meaning that he denies the fundamental truth of <i>HaShem’s</i>-יהו"ה existence and states that there is no God; and likewise, one who says that the Torah is indeed from Heaven, but “I cannot stand it,” meaning “I do not fulfill it;” or alternatively, one who says that the Torah is not from Heaven, even if he only is referring to a single verse, or a single grammatical aspect, such as missing letters or additional letters, or denies even one exegetical matter, such as a single <i>Kal VaChomer</i> or a single <i>Gzeira Shava</i> transmitted by our sages; Some also include those who deny the Oral Torah or matters that are established by the Sages;<sup class="footnote-marker">760</sup><i class="footnote">Like Chanukah and Purim</i> This category also includes one who says that the resurrection of the dead is not from the Torah, meaning that it is not hinted at in the Torah, even though he believes both in the Torah and the resurrection of the dead; Also, one who interprets Torah falsely, such as Menasheh, who would expound the Torah scornfully and falsely, saying things like “There was no reason for Moshe to write the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">761</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 36:2</i> ‘And Lotan’s sister was Timna,’” and the like;<sup class="footnote-marker">762</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:11; Sanhedrin 99b; Yoma 85b, and Rashi there.</i> Also, one who publicly violates the commandments of the Torah high-handedly, like Yehoyakim;<sup class="footnote-marker">763</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 103b; Mishneh Torah, Teshuvah, Ch. 3 ibid.</i> One who abrogates the covenant of circumcision (<i>Brit Milah</i>), meaning that as an act of rebellion, he does not circumcise himself, or alternately, he stretches his foreskin to look uncircumcised; One who himself sins and also causes others to sin such as Yeravam, which even includes transgressing minor prohibitions;<sup class="footnote-marker">764</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 107b</i> Also, infidels (<i>Apikorsim</i>), that is, those who treat a Torah scholar with contempt, to their faces;<sup class="footnote-marker">765</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 99b</i> and also one who sits before his master and says, “this thing is forbidden,” or “this thing is permissible,” in the form of a statement, rather than in the form of a question; Also one who ridicules his master when he expounds something that seems to be an exaggeration, and he does not believe his words; Also one who treats Torah scholars with contempt, even not to their face, such as those who say “Those Rabbis…” in a degrading manner, or similarly, those who say, “With what have the Rabbis benefited us? They read the Torah for their own benefit, and study the Mishnah for their own benefit etc.,”<sup class="footnote-marker">766</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 99b ibid.</i> or like those who say, “With what have the Rabbis benefited us? Never have they permitted a raven for us, nor have they prohibited a dove for us.”<sup class="footnote-marker">767</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 100a – That is, they say, “Of what benefit is their Torah study, if they merely tell us matters explicitly stated in Torah.” (Rashi)</i> Also included is one who addresses his master by name, and does not respectfully address him as “my master and teacher;” Likewise, one who disgraces his fellow before a Torah scholar; and those who betray others to the Gentile authorities, whether they turned a Jew into the hands of the Gentile authorities to be beaten, or whether they only betrayed him monetarily to the Gentile authorities; Likewise, a communal leader who imposes excess fear upon the community out of pride, rather than for the sake of the Name of <i>HaShem-יהו"ה</i>;<sup class="footnote-marker">768</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 17a</i> One who disgraces the Festivals, in that he intentionally performs labor during <i>Chol HaMo’ed</i> as a show of disgrace and that he does not believe that it is forbidden, rather than for personal benefit;<sup class="footnote-marker">769</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:11</i> One who publicly embarrasses his fellow in his presence; One who derives honor from the shame of his friend, and it seems to me, that this too is if it is his presence; One who reads extraneous literature, such as the book of Ben Sira and the books of Ben La’anah, which are nonsensical books that draw a person’s heart and cause him to neglect his Torah study;<sup class="footnote-marker">770</sup><i class="footnote">The indication by the commentaries is that these are books that were written by apostates in the style of Torah, and other books of that nature, which may lead the reader to think that they are Torah, yet they are not Torah, and are completely contrary to Torah.</i> The same applies to books of apostacy, such as those of the priests and ministers of the nations; However, books such as that written by Homer<sup class="footnote-marker">771</sup><i class="footnote">The indication by the commentaries is that this refers to literature that is like that of the Greek writer and poet Homer, which are either clearly known fiction or the natural scientific wisdoms of the nations, and are considered mundane, like one who reads a letter, and are thus not in this same category of grave transgression as the false and misleading literature mentioned before. They therefore are not cause for loss of the coming world, as with the prior category. Even so, as the Talmud there concludes citing King Solomon (Eccl. 12:12), “Beyond these my son, be warned,” – “They are given to develop reason, but not for toiling in.”</i> and other similar books, are considered to be mundane, and are as if he is merely reading a correspondence, as stated in the Jerusalem Talmud;<sup class="footnote-marker">772</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Yerushalmi, Sanhedrin 10:1</i> One who whispers incantations over an injury, or even if he recites a verse over it and spits,<sup class="footnote-marker">773</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Sanhedrin 10:1; Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 90a</i> irrespective of whether it is the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">774</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 15:26</i> “I will not bring any of the diseases upon you,” or whether it has any other mention of illness, healing, or the Name of Heaven, but even if it is a verse such as,<sup class="footnote-marker">775</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 1:1</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> called to Moshe etc.”;<sup class="footnote-marker">776</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Avodah Zarah 11:12; Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh De’ah 179:8</i> One who pronounces the Name <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> according to its letters outside the Temple,<sup class="footnote-marker">777</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 101b</i> which the Jerusalem Talmud<sup class="footnote-marker">778</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Yerushalmi, Sanhedrin 10:1 – His title Lord-Adona”y-אדנ״י</i> explains means that he does not mention Him by His title, in accordance to the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">779</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 3:15</i> “This is My Name forever, and this is My remembrance from generation to generation.” However, in our Talmud<sup class="footnote-marker">780</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Avodah Zarah 18a</i> we learn that this is specifically if he does so publicly; One who disgraces the word of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, meaning that he recalls words of Torah in a filthy place;<sup class="footnote-marker">781</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Yerushalmi, Sanhedrin 10:1 and elsewhere.</i> Likewise, one who reads the written Torah, but pays no heed to the words of the Mishnah, which explain the written Torah; Similarly, one who studies Torah but does not teach it, the exception being the secrets of the Torah, about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">782</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 27:26</i> “The lambs (<i>Kvasim</i>-<i><b>כבש</b>ים</i>) shall be for your clothing,” meaning,<sup class="footnote-marker">783</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 13a</i> “Matters that are the secrets of the world (<i>Kivshono shel Olam</i>-<i><b>כבש</b>ונו של עולם</i>) should be hidden under your clothing.” It is only fitting to teach them to the pious (<i>Chassidim</i>) of the generation, who are worthy of being taught; Similarly, one who is capable of engaging in Torah study but does not engage in it, and instead engages in business and other worldly matters; One who gossips (<i>Rechilut</i>), meaning that he takes the words of one friend and brings them to another, and this applies even if they are not words that cause any shame or ill repute, and even if they are true, like what occurred with Doeg the Edomite and David;<sup class="footnote-marker">784</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 22:9-10; Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 106b</i> One who speaks evil speech (<i>Lashon Hara</i>), in that he speaks of his fellow’s shamefulness, even if it is true; The slanderer (<i>Motzi Shem Ra</i>) who relates false matters about his fellow to disgrace his name; Anyone who violates these three, that is, the gossiper, one who speaks evil speech and the slanderer, it is considered as if they have denied the primary foundation of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה existence, and these are so severe that they are equal to the three cardinal sins of the Torah, these being idolatry, forbidden relations, and murder; One who lends to his fellow Jew with interest and did not return the interest to him will not rise upon the resurrection of the dead;<sup class="footnote-marker">785</sup><i class="footnote">See Baal HaTurim to Leviticus 25:36</i> One who transgresses the Shabbat is judged in purgatory (<i>Gehinom</i>) for all generations;<sup class="footnote-marker">786</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 24, 69b</i> One who intentionally does not bear children and dies childless is excised from this world and will not have life in the coming world.<sup class="footnote-marker">787</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 10a</i>
There are three categories of people who descend to purgatory and never ascend: One who has relations with a married woman; One who calls his fellow by a derogatory nickname, and this applies even if he has become accustomed to being called by that name instead of his real name and does not become embarrassed by it, but the perpetrator intends to insult him; One who speaks evil speech (<i>Lashon Hara</i>), which is equal to all three, in which case he too has no share in the coming world.
Greater than all sins, is the transgression of wasteful seminal emissions,<sup class="footnote-marker">788</sup><i class="footnote">See Part II, Gate Six</i> in that he spills the blood of his own offspring for all generations until the end of the world. Even though all other sins are reparable through repentance, there is no repentance for this sin, as mentioned in Zohar to Parshat Vayechi.<sup class="footnote-marker">789</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 219b ibid.</i> However, there are those who have a version that states that repentance can be effective if he truly repents strongly and constantly.
Sins between man and his fellow are minor in comparison to transgressions between man and <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, the Ever Present One, blessed is He. However, from a different angle, they are worse, since they have no repair except by appeasing the fellow who he sinned against and that his fellow forgives him, and by making restitution, either through words or financially.
Section Three: Repentance for sins between man and the Creator
There is not a single sin that stands in the way of repentance, even the sin of denying the primary foundation of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה existence, and even if he only repented at the moment of death.
There are four categories of atonement.<sup class="footnote-marker">790</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 86a; Talmud Yerushalmi Yoma 8:7; Sanhedrin 10:1; Tosefta Yoma 4:9 and elsewhere.</i> If a person transgressed a minor positive commandment and repented, he does not move from there until he is forgiven.<sup class="footnote-marker">791</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shevuot 12b – That is, he is immediately forgiven upon his repentance.</i> If he transgressed a minor prohibitive commandment, repentance as well as Yom Kippur affect atonement for him.<sup class="footnote-marker">792</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 85b and on; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah (Repentance) Ch. 1 and on.</i> If he transgressed grave sins, be they positive commandments or prohibitions, such as those for which one is punished by excision (<i>Karet</i>) or is liable for the death penalty at the hands of Heaven, or whether he is liable for the death penalty at the hands of the court, with the exception being a desecration of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, repentance, Yom Kippur, as well as suffering, affect his atonement. If he caused a desecration of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, or if he violated the gravest of commandments, such as rebellious Jews who sin with their bodies (<i>Poshei Yisroel b’Gufam</i>), and all who descend to purgatory (<i>Gehinom</i>) and do not ascend, as well as all those who will not rise upon the resurrection of the dead and all those who have no portion in the coming world, as previously discussed at length in the two preceding sections - repentance, Yom Kippur, suffering, and death, affect his atonement.
The sufferings that affect atonement include every manner and type of suffering. To what extent is something considered suffering? To the point that even if he accidently puts his garment on backward and must take it off to put it on correctly, or if he reached into his pocket to take out two coins and only one coin came up and he must put his hand into his pocket a second time, this is considered suffering.<sup class="footnote-marker">793</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Arachin 16b</i>
Repentance (<i>Teshuvah</i>) means that the opportunity to commit the same sin that he transgressed presented itself to him, but he does not transgress it a second or third time. For example, he has the opportunity to transgress with the same woman, at around the same time period, and in the same place, and the like, but he does not do so.<sup class="footnote-marker">794</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 86b; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah 2:1</i> If he repents out of love of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, or even if only out of fear of punishment, then the sin is entirely uprooted from him, as if it never was. However, if he repents because suffering came upon him, the sin is not completely healed, and he is called a “<i>Baal Moom</i>” – a blemished person.
Repentance (<i>Teshuvah</i>) requires repentance with words.<sup class="footnote-marker">795</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 5:6-7; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah 1:1</i> The primary words of confession are thus,<sup class="footnote-marker">796</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Yoma 3:8; Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Teshuvah 1:1</i> “Please, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, I have sinned, I have done wrong, I have rebelled against You… but we and our fathers have sinned.” The words of the confessional presented in our Talmud<sup class="footnote-marker">797</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 87b</i> as well as the Jerusalem Talmud<sup class="footnote-marker">798</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Yerushalmi, Yoma 8:7</i> is as follows, although I shall both summarize and add some words:
“Master of the universe, I have sinned, I have done wrong, I have rebelled against You, and have done evil in Your eyes, and I was in a state of mind of wickedness, and I went in errant ways. I hereby regret my sins. If only it could be that I had not done them, but I shall no longer act and no longer do as I previously did. May it be desirable before You, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה my God, and the God of my fathers, that you atone me of all my rebellious deeds, and pardon me of all my transgressions, and forgive me for all my sins, that I sinned, transgressed, and rebelled before you, from the day that I was created in the world until this day, whether I did so in this incarnation or in any other incarnation, whether I transgressed prohibitions of the Torah or Rabbinic prohibitions, including their enactments, safe-guards, or customs, for You are He who desires repentance. May the expressions of my mouth and the thoughts of my heart find favor before You, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, my Rock and Redeemer.”

Part 3





Shaar 1

Part Three
<b>The conduct of attaining the Holy Spirit of Divine Inspiration (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>)</b><br>1. The existence of the worlds.<br>2. The existence of man.<br>3. The hindrances to prophecy.<br>4. The conditions to prophecy.<br>5. The nature of prophecy and its substance.<br>6. The levels of prophecy.<br>7. The conduct of the Holy Spirit of Divine Inspiration (<i>Ru’ach HaKodesh</i>) in our times.<br>8. A short introduction to the manner of its attainment.
Part Three
Gate One <b>The Existence of the Worlds</b>
This matter shall be explained with the utmost brevity, solely to the extent necessary to understand the matter of prophecy.<sup class="footnote-marker">799</sup><i class="footnote">The expansive details of the chaining down of the worlds (Seder Hishtalshelut) is the subject of Etz Chayim of the Arizal written by Rabbi Chayim Vital, and is explained in a manner of grasp and comprehension by Rabbi DovBer of Lubavitch in Shaar HaYichud, translated as The Gate of Unity.</i> Now, the Supernal Emanator, blessed is He, who emanated all the worlds, is called the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), blessed is He. He has no image whatsoever, neither in the form of a name, nor in the form of a letter, nor even in the thorns of the letters.<sup class="footnote-marker">800</sup><i class="footnote">See at length in Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 1, The Gate of Intrinsic Being (Shaar HaHavayah);</i> We thus are incapable and therefore barred from all thought of Him.
He emanated five worlds, one world being the soul for the next, and the next world being the soul for the next. These are: Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i>, as mentioned in Sefer Tikkunim,<sup class="footnote-marker">801</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 19 (42a), and Tikkun 70 (120a), and elsewhere.</i> which in the nomenclature of the Ge’onim is called, “Exceedingly Brilliant-<i>Tzachtzechoot</i>.” The second is the world of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>. The third is the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i>. The fourth is the world of Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>. The fifth is the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>. These five worlds are considered as One Being-<i>Havayah</i> <i>Achat</i>-הוי״ה אחת. For, the thorn of the letter <i>Yod</i>-יו״ד (י) is Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i>, the <i>Yod</i>-יו״ד (י) itself is the world of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>, the first <i>Hey</i>-ה״א (ה) is the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, the <i>Vav</i>-וא״ו (ו) is the world of Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, and the final <i>Hey</i>-ה״א (ה) is the world of <i>Action</i>.
Now, because Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i> is so concealed from us, to the point that it does not even have the form of a letter, but only the thorn of the <i>Yod</i>-יו״ד (י) – whereas the Unlimited One Himself, blessed is He, does not even have the simple image or form of the thorn of a letter<sup class="footnote-marker">802</sup><i class="footnote">See Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 1, The Gate of Intrinsic Being (Shaar HaHavayah).</i> – we therefore generally only discuss the four worlds of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>, Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, and Action-<i>Asiyah</i>. This is because they are complete letters, and together, the four are called, The Name of Being-שם הוי״ה.
These four further subdivide into nine levels, these being wisdom-<i>Chochmah</i>, understanding-<i>Binah</i>, the six directions of beauty-<i>Tiferet</i> and kingship-<i>Malchut</i>. For, these four are called the four Supernal foundations, which are the four worlds of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>, Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, and Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, and they divide into nine <i>Sefirot</i>. However, the thorn of the <i>Yod</i>-<i>יו״ד</i> (<i>י</i>), which is Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i>, is the fifth world, which is higher than them all and includes them all. It alone is the root of all four foundations, which are the four worlds of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>, Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, and Action-<i>Asiyah</i>. We thus find that there are never more than four foundations, and the general principle that arises, is that the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), blessed is He, is not included in any calculation whatsoever.<sup class="footnote-marker">803</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaar HaYichud of Rabbi DovBer of Lubavitch, translated as The Gate of Unity, Ch. 10-11.</i>
Subsequently, the worlds were initially included as one complete Name of Being-<i>Shem Havayah</i>-<i>שם הוי״ה</i>. Afterwards, they were divided into four foundations, except for their root, which is Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i> and is the thorn of the letter <i>Yod</i>-<i>יו״ד</i> (<i>י</i>) which is the tenth <i>Sefirah</i> that is higher than them all, and is therefore called the crown-<i>Keter</i>. Afterwards, the four foundations were divided into nine <i>Sefirot</i>, as mentioned.
Now, it all includes two categories; the Emanator and all the Emanated. About this, it states in Pirkei d’Rabbi Eliezer,<sup class="footnote-marker">804</sup><i class="footnote">Pirkei d’Rabbi Eliezer, Ch. 3</i> “Before the creation of the world” – the intention being to this world – “He and His Name were One.” The Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), blessed is He, is referred to here as, “He-<i>Hoo</i>-<i>הוא</i>,” and the emanated are included in, “His Name-<i>Shmo</i>-<i>שמו</i>,” which is One Being-<i>Havayah Achat</i>-הוי״ה אחת, and all of it is One, because<sup class="footnote-marker">805</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer Yetzirah 1:7</i> “the flame was concealed within the coal.”<sup class="footnote-marker">806</sup><i class="footnote">Note from the Chida: I have seen an explanation written as to why, in truth, the Unlimited One (Ein Sof) is called by the title “He-Hoo-הוא,” whereas the emanated are called, “His Name-Shmo-שמו,” all of which has already been discussed at length by the commentaries, of blessed memory. What is important for you to know is that all things below in the worlds, meaning, all that is actualized, formed and created, have a refined and concealed root above in the Essential Self of the Singular Preexistent Intrinsic Being of the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He.<br>Now, it is known that the nature of a thing that is hewn from another, is that within itself, it always possesses the power of that which it was hewn from. For example, within the branch of a tree is the power of the root, and necessarily, in the same manner, within the root of the tree is the power of the branch. If this was not the case, it would be impossible for the branch to come from the root. This being so, the ten Sefirot of the world of Emanation-Atzilut [which are the branch] necessarily possess a very hidden and concealed root in the Essential Self of the Singular Preexistent Intrinsic and Essential Being of the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He. However, in Him, they actually are not recognizably differentiated, God forbid to think so. In other words, it is impossible for us to differentiate and say that, “this is the crown-Keter” or “this is wisdom-Chochmah” etc., but it rather is like a Heyulie, similar to what we say below, in the world of Action-Asiyah, that the Heyulie is the root of the four elemental foundations.<br>Now, the words of the Ari”zal are well known, namely, that “when it arose in His simple will to create the worlds, the Unlimited One, blessed is He, estimated within Himself, in the aspect and level of His Kingship-Malchut, as in the verse (Psalms 145:13), “Your Kingship (Malchutcha) is the kingship (Malchut) of all the worlds.” (By way of analogy, this is called the aspect of Kingship within Kingship-Malchut sh’bMalchut of the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), even though this is not truly the case. For, in reality, we are incapable, and therefore barred from ascribing any form whatsoever to the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He, neither any image nor any Sefirah whatsoever, God forbid to think so. Rather, it only is in order to satisfy the ear that we speak in such terms, as the author writes in Etz Chayim, Drush ABY”A, Ch. 1.) All the lower worlds that are emanated from the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He, receive from Him, similar to the fact that biologically, the female receives from the male, so to speak. It is for this reason that the verse, “Your Kingship is the Kingship of all worlds,” begins by specifying, “Your Kingship-Malchutcha-מלכותך,” in the masculine, indicating that relative to the construct of the worlds, He is the giver, and it is only in relation to the other Sefirot that are above her, that she is called by the title kingship-Malchut-מלכות. This then, is the meaning of the continuation of the verse, “is the Kingship-Malchut-מלכות of all the worlds,” meaning that all worlds are emanated into her.<br>Now, it is known that the male is called by the term “He-Hoo-הוא,” and this term “He-Hoo-הוא” includes all ten Sefirot from below to above, as follows: The Hey-ה of the word “He-Hoo-<b>ה</b>וא” hints at the feminine aspect, which is included in the Sefirah of foundation-Yesod, and is the mystery of the corona-Atarah-עטרה. The Vav-ו-6 of the word “He-Hoo-ה<b>ו</b>א” hints at the six directions of the Sefirah of beauty-Tiferet. The Aleph-א of the term “He-Hoo-הו<b>א</b>” hints at the crown-Keter, wisdom-Chochmah, and understanding-Binah. For, as known, the first three Sefirot are considered as one, like the form of the letter Aleph-א. That is, the Yod-י above is wisdom-Chochmah, the Yod-י below is understanding-Binah, and the Vav-ו in between is the mystery of knowledge-Da’at, which mediates between wisdom-Chochmah and understanding-Binah, and as known, knowledge-Da’at is at times entitled the crown-Keter, in that it is the middle line that is called (Ex. 26:28) “The center bar that goes from end to end,” from above to below, as known.<br>We should also point out an additional reason that the Aleph-א hints at the first three Sefirot. Namely, as known, the title of the first three Sefirot is the name Ya”H-י״ה. That is, the thorn of the Yod-י is the crown-Keter, the Yod-י itself is wisdom-Chochmah, and the Hey-ה is understanding-Binah. When the Name Ya”H-י״ה is spelled out according to the name of Ma”H-מ״ה-45 [the Name HaShem-יהו״ה spelled with Aleph’s-א], that is, Yod Hey-יו״ד ה״א, it has the numerical value of כ״ו-26, which is the same numerical value as the Aleph-א, which has a Yod-י-10 above, a Yod-י-10 below, and Vav-ו-6 in between, in a way of complete Oneness-א. Thus, the first three Sefirot are called the Aleph-א of the word “He-Hoo-הו״א.” Also, as known, Malchut, which is the feminine aspect, is called, “His Name-Shem-שם.” This then, is what our sages, of blessed memory, meant when they said, “Before the creation of the world there was He-Hoo-הו״א,” meaning all the aforementioned aspects as they are in the Essential Self of the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He, “and His Name-Shmo-שמו,” meaning the aspect of Kingship-Malchut of the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), which includes all the emanated, who are the recipients of the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He, and are feminine, in that they are recipients relative to He who is above. All of it is included in the mystery of His Oneness (Echad-אחד), meaning that they are in a state of absolute unity, “like a flame that is bound to the coal.”<br>It may thus also be said that this is the meaning of the verse (Psalms 33:9), “He-Hoo-הוא spoke and it came to be, He-Hoo-הוא commanded and it stood firm.” This is to be understood as mentioned above, that the term “He-Hoo-הוא” refers to the Unlimited One (Ein Sof), blessed is He, according to the order of the levels of the roots in ascending order from below to above. This is likewise the meaning of the verse (Psalms 132:13), “For HaShem-יהו״ה has chosen Zion, Desiring it (Eevah-או״ה) as His habitation.” That is, the letters of the word, “Desiring it-Eevah-או״ה” are the same letters as the levels of the aforementioned roots, but in descending order, from Above to below. That is, the Aleph-א is the crown-Keter, wisdom-Chochmah, and understanding-Binah, the Vav-ו is the six directions of Beauty-Tiferet, and the Hey-ה is kingship-Malchut. The distinction between these two orders, is the distinction between the direct, forward light (Ohr Yashar) and the rebounding, returning light (Ohr Chozer), however, it all is an absolute Unity and Oneness. This should suffice for the understanding.</i>
Now, it was explained that all the worlds are included in the Name of Being-<i>Shem Havayah</i>-שם הוי״ה, which is divided into four foundations and ten <i>Sefirot</i>. In the same manner, this is likewise the case with each of the worlds, in the same manner, that each of them also divides into particulars. That is, the world of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>, which is the letter <i>Yod</i>-יו״ד (י) and is called wisdom-<i>Chochmah</i>, divides into each of the aforementioned aspects. It too possesses one complete Name of Being-<i>Havayah Achat</i>-הוי״ה אחת that is divided into four foundations and ten complete <i>Sefirot</i>, literally in the same manner that we mentioned in regard to the worlds in general. The same is likewise so of each of the five aforementioned worlds. The same is likewise the case that each further divides into its further particulars to the utmost specificity, until we find that even in this lowly world, even the most minor creation contains the totality of the four letters of Being-<i>Havayah</i>-הוי״ה and all the ten <i>Sefirot</i> within itself<i>.</i> All this is to show that everything is created by the power of the Emanator, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, and aside for Him, nothing exists.<sup class="footnote-marker">807</sup><i class="footnote">This is explained at length in Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One.</i>
Another introductory matter that you must know, is that all these aspects and levels, from the exalted level of Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i>, until the depths of the abyss of this lowly world, are all one above the other, and one within the other. For, the one that is higher manifests within the one that is below it, like the soul to the body. However, it is not all of the upper aspect that manifests within the lower aspect. Rather, it only is a specific aspect, which is the lowest level of the upper level, that manifests within each lower level, and the same is true in succession, until this lowest of all worlds. That is, such is the case with all the worlds, whether we are discussing the worlds in general, or whether we are discussing each particular aspect of them, including even in this world – in every particular detail in them, it is in this manner. That is, there is one that is higher than another, and one that is inner to the other, to the point that they all are like garments for one another, and ultimately, they all are garments of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, who is the Soul of all souls.
However, in each of these five worlds, there is a separation in the spreading forth of their lights and the extent of their spreading forth, so that there should be a distinction between them. Similarly, there is another separation in the particulars of the four foundations of each world, as well as in the particulars of the particulars, but this is not the place for the explanation of this matter.
What we find is that in the manner of the spreading forth of lights and illuminations from Above to below, there is no <i>Sefirah</i> that does not include all ten <i>Sefirot</i> within it, and each particular <i>Sefirah</i> further subdivides into thousands and tens of thousands of <i>Sefirot</i>. The same is likewise so of the spreading forth of the lights from inner to outer. It also is in this manner. For, the innermost of the <i>Sefirot</i> is called the crown-<i>Keter</i>, and the outer <i>Sefirah</i> that is upon it, is wisdom-<i>Chochmah</i>, and the outer <i>Sefirah</i> that is upon it, is understanding-<i>Binah</i>, and the outer <i>Sefirah</i> that is upon it, are the six directions of beauty-<i>Tiferet</i>, and the outermost of them all, is kingship-<i>Malchut</i>. The same is likewise so with each particular aspect, that it divides in this manner into thousands and tens of thousands of particular details.
However, because we have already provided the complete explanations of this matter,<sup class="footnote-marker">808</sup><i class="footnote">In the book Etz Chayim</i> as it is in all the worlds – except for the matter of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> – we will therefore only explain this subject in great brevity here, to the extent that it is necessary to understand the desired subject that we seek in this book.
Now, there are seven firmaments. The uppermost is called <i>Aravot</i>, because it includes the first three <i>Sefirot</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> within it. These are the Sphere of the Intellect (<i>Galgal HaSechel</i>), the Surrounding Sphere (<i>Galgal HaMakif</i>), and the Sphere of the Constellations (<i>Galgal HaMazalot</i>). The five spheres of Saturn (<i>Shabtai</i>), Jupiter (<i>Tzeddek</i>), Mars (<i>Ma’adim</i>), the Sun (<i>Chamah</i>), and Venus (<i>Nogah</i>), are the <i>Sefirot</i> of kindness-<i>Chessed</i>, Judgment-<i>Gevurah</i>, beauty-<i>Tiferet</i>, conquest-<i>Netzach</i> and majesty-<i>Hod</i>. The sixth sphere is foundation-<i>Yesod</i>, and includes both Mercury (<i>Kochav</i>) and the Moon (<i>Levanah</i>). 
The last firmament, which is called <i>Veelon</i>, has nothing of her own with which to serve,<sup class="footnote-marker">809</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 12b; Etz Chayim, Shaar 38, Ch. 3 (See also Ohev Yisroel, Vayechi 4); Also see Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 2, Section entitled, “The seven letters בג״ד כפר״ת correspond to the seven firmaments-Raki’im-רקיעים.”</i> and is the <i>Sefirah</i> of kingship-<i>Malchut</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>. Nevertheless, it too is divided into the ten <i>Sefirot</i> that are within it, which are as follows: The firmament <i>Veelon</i> is the crown-<i>Keter</i> within it. The four elemental foundations of fire (<i>Aish</i>), air (<i>Ru’ach</i>), water (<i>Mayim</i>), and earth (<i>Affar</i>) of this lowly world, are the aspects of wisdom-<i>Chochmah</i>, understanding-<i>Binah</i>, the six-directions of beauty-<i>Tiferet</i>, and kingship-<i>Malchut</i>. We thus find that kingship of kingship – <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> – that is within the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> is the foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>), which is the receptacle and substance-matter of this entire world. It is in this foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>) that all of its offspring are included, as it includes within it all four fundamental elements that were mentioned, as per the explanation of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">810</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 3:20</i> “All originate from the earth (<i>Affar</i>).”
We have thus explained the matter from Above to below, as well as from the inner to the outer. For, the elemental foundation of earth (<i>Affar</i>) contains ten <i>Sefirot</i>. Their crown-<i>Keter</i> is the innermost, and is called the aspect of the <i>Yechidah</i> essence of the foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>). External to it is wisdom-<i>Chochmah</i>, which is the aspect of the <i>Chayah</i> of the earth (<i>Affar</i>). External to that is the aspect of understanding-<i>Binah</i>, which is the aspect of the <i>Neshamah</i> of the earth (<i>Affar</i>). External to that is the aspect of the six-directions of beauty-<i>Tiferet</i>, which is the <i>Ru’ach</i> of the earth (<i>Affar</i>). External to that is kingship-<i>Malchut</i>, which is the <i>Nefesh</i> of the foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>). This external aspect of kingship-<i>Malchut</i> itself divides into ten <i>Sefirot</i> that are within it, and their kingship-<i>Malchut</i> is the foundational element of the gross physical earth (<i>Affar</i>) itself, which contains no spirituality at all, but only gross substance, which is called inanimate (<i>Domem</i>), whereas that which is inner to it, is called the soul-<i>Nefesh</i> of the inanimate (<i>Domem</i>).
The same applies to the foundational element of water (<i>Mayim</i>). For, the aspect of kingship-<i>Malchut</i> is the most external of its aspects, which is called water that brings forth growth and vegetation, and it thus is called the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>), and all the aspects that are inner to it, are called the soul-<i>Nefesh</i> of the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>). The same is so of the elemental foundations of air (<i>Ru’ach</i>) and fire (<i>Aish</i>), which are the animate (<i>Chay</i>) and speaking beings (<i>Medaber</i>), respectively. Together, the four are as follows: The inanimate (<i>Domem</i>) is the <i>Nefesh</i>; the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>) is the <i>Ru’ach</i>; the animate (<i>Chay</i>) is the <i>Neshamah</i>; the speaking being (<i>Medaber</i>) is the <i>Chayah</i>; and <i>Veelon</i> is the <i>Yechidah</i>. As already explained, each of these aspects includes them all.
These aspects are referred to by the philosophers as “powers.” For example, they stated that the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>) possesses the power to sustain, the power to draw sustenance, the power to absorb and the power to expel. Similarly, they stated about the soul of the animate living being (<i>Chay</i>) that it possesses the power of motion, the power of movement and the sensatory powers, and that it possesses the power of consciousness, the power of imagination and the power of imagery etc. The same principle applies to them all.
What arises from all this, is that even though kingship-<i>Malchut</i> is the most external of all the levels of whatever aspect it may be, nevertheless, it is the body of that aspect. However, it is not a body of actual coarse and gross physical substance. Rather, that is only the case with the final most external aspect of kingship-<i>Malchut</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, from above to below and from inner to outer. Only that level, which is the foundational element of completely gross material earth (<i>Affar</i>), is the coarsest and most gross body in all the world.

Shaar 2

Gate Two
<b>The Existence of Man</b>
In this section we shall explain wondrous mysteries, teachings that were never openly revealed by the ancients,<sup class="footnote-marker">811</sup><i class="footnote">A play on Deuteronomy 32:17 (see Rashi there)</i> and were they not necessary in order to explain the matter of prophecy, I would never have explained them. I therefore shall write them with the utmost brevity, and may they be as,<sup class="footnote-marker">812</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 27:26</i> “lambs (<i>Kvasim</i>-<i><b>כבש</b>ים</i>) for your clothing,” meaning that,<sup class="footnote-marker">813</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 13a</i> “Matters that are the secrets of the world (<i>Kivshono shel Olam</i>-<i><b>כבש</b>ונו של עולם</i>) should remain hidden under your clothing.”
I shall ask several deep questions as follows:
1. Why was it necessary for man to be created in this world, with a soul and a body?
2. Why, was man bestowed two additional forms when he was formed, these being the good inclination (<i>Yetzer Tov</i>) and the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer Hara</i>) that are within him?
3. Since both are equally balanced within him, what is it that gives man the strength to choose and tip the scales to one or the other? Moreover, if he indeed has the ability to tip the scales to one or other, why then were they created altogether?
4. We must explain the matter of these two inclinations and what they are.
5. We must know whether the soul of man is greater than the angelic beings or not. If we say that man is greater than the angels, then why did the angels not also descend into this physical world to manifest in a soul and a body? On the other hand, we cannot say that angels are greater than man. For, in all the teachings of our sages, of blessed memory, we find the opposite to be true. For example, along with many other teachings, they stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">814</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Bereishit Rabba 78:1</i> “Who is greater, the guard or the guarded?” Moreover, even Scripturally, the verses themselves indicate the opposite to be true, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">815</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:18</i> “You weakened<i>-תשי</i> the Rock who bore you,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">816</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 68:35</i> “Give strength to God, whose pride is over Israel,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">817</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 14:1</i> “You are children to <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> your God,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">818</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 49:3</i> “You are My servant Israel, in whom I take pride.” Moreover, the angels do not recite “Holy, Holy, Holy,” until the Jewish people below recite it first.<sup class="footnote-marker">819</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chullin 91b; Midrash Shemot Rabba 23:7</i> We find no such things whatsoever stated about the angels.
6. Even if we submit that man is greater than the angels, it nevertheless remains entirely questionable to call them “His children,” or to say that they weaken (<i>מתישים</i>) or strengthen Him, or that He takes pride in them, for a person could possibly fall into heresy from this.
7. In regard to the matter of prophecy, how is it applicable that the King, King of kings, the Holy One, blessed is He, would speak to lowly man, even through the agency of an angel, especially since man is manifest in the grossest and coarsest substance in all the worlds?
Now, in the preceding gate we explained the matter of the existence of the worlds and how they all are One Being-<i>Havayah Achat</i>-<i>הוי״ה אחת</i> that includes them all, and that they are divided into five worlds. We explained that these are called the <i>Yechidah</i>, <i>Chayah</i>, <i>Neshamah</i>, <i>Ru’ach</i>, and <i>Nefesh</i>. We also explained that this physical world is the body and substance to them all. That is, each of the worlds are in the form of man, and each possesses substance and form, and each are divided into five spiritual levels, as explained. You also know that when the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> is spelled out with the letter <i>Aleph</i>-<i>א</i> [<i>יו"ד ה"א וא"ו ה"א</i>] it has the same numerical value as “man-<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם-</i>45.” The same is likewise so of each particular detail in all their various levels. Each of them is called a particular man (<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם</i>), which includes One Being-<i>Havayah Achat</i>-<i>הוי"ה אחת</i> that divides into four foundations and ten <i>Sefirot</i>.
There is another division that was not explained in the preceding gate, which is that the ten <i>Sefirot</i> also subdivide further into 613 aspects, as will be explained. Nevertheless, it is understood that all the worlds as a whole, as well as each particular world, in and of itself, is created in the form of the lower man. This is the mystery of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">820</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:26</i> “Let us make man in Our image, after Our likeness.” Understand this well.
Now, it has already been explained<sup class="footnote-marker">821</sup><i class="footnote">In Etz Chayim, Shaar 47, Ch. 4</i> that everything from the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i> and down, is called the Tree of Knowledge, in that it includes both good and evil. Additionally, it has been explained that with the successive descent of their levels, there is a diminishment of the good and an increase of the evil, to the point that we find that this lowly world is mostly evil with very little good. It also is explained that “the wicked surrounds the righteous,”<sup class="footnote-marker">822</sup><i class="footnote">Habakkuk 1:4</i> and therefore the good is called the fruit, whereas the evil is called the peel or shell (<i>Kelipah</i>) that covers over the fruit. Moreover, the same is likewise true that the good lights and illuminations are also in this manner, that is, the more refined and spiritual among them are manifest within the remaining lights and illuminations. The same is true of them all, according to the order of their levels. In the preceding gate it was also explained how the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, is the innermost of them all, and that the <i>Sefirot</i> are external to Him, according to the order of their levels, with the crown-<i>Keter</i> being the most inner and kingship-<i>Malchut</i> being the most external.
We now shall begin explaining what has yet to be explained. Namely, just as this unique light, which is called the world of the Ten <i>Sefirot</i>, is in the image of a single man, so likewise, there is another light of man (<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם</i>) that is called the source of the souls of all people. It too includes all the particulars that were explained in regard to the man (<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם</i>) of the Ten <i>Sefirot</i>, literally. That is, the man (<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם</i>) of the Ten <i>Sefirot</i> is considered to be completely Godly, and it manifests within the light and illumination which is the source of the souls, in all their particular details.
There is also another light in the form of man (<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם</i>) which is called the source of the angels. That is, all the angels are hewn from this light, and it too includes all the above-mentioned details. It is the outer garment over the light that is the source of the souls.
There is yet another lesser light, which is called dark light, that consists entirely of harsh judgments. It is from this light that all the shells of the <i>Kelipot</i> of that particular world emanate from. This light, garbs the light that is the source of the souls, and it too possesses the image of man (<i>Adam</i>-<i>אדם</i>). Outside all these lights that we have mentioned, are the firmaments (<i>Raki’im</i>) themselves, as they are in that particular world. They are called the body (<i>Guf</i>) of that particular world, and within them, the five above-mentioned lights are manifest. That is, the light of the Unlimited One (<i>Ohr Ein Sof</i>), blessed is He, as it manifests according to the capacity of that particular world, is innermost. Upon Him, like a garment, is the light of the source of the souls. Upon it, like a garment, is the light of the source of the angels. Upon it, like a garment, is the light of the source of the shells of <i>Kelipah</i>. Upon it, like a garment, is the world itself, which are the firmaments (<i>Raki’im</i>) that are the body (<i>Guf</i>), together with the above-mentioned inner lights. Subsequently, from this body (<i>Guf</i>), which is called the firmaments (<i>Raki’im</i>), the offspring of that world are created, each of which includes all these aspects. For, each of them has a power drawn to it from the firmament, which is its body. That is, within it are the lights of the judgments, and within it are the lights of the angels, and within it is the light from the source of the souls, and within it are the lights of the Ten <i>Sefirot</i>, that rides upon them and enlivens them all.
Now, that power that is drawn to it from the light of the source of the souls is called the Upper Flow (<i>Mazal HaElyon</i>) of that soul of lower man. Understand this very well, and also realize that this aspect, as it exists in the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, is called the Flow (<i>Mazal</i>) of the <i>Neshamah</i>, whereas this aspect in the world of Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, is called the Flow (<i>Mazal</i>) of the <i>Ru’ach</i>, and in the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> it is called the Flow (<i>Mazal</i>) of the <i>Nefesh</i>.
We shall now explain the matter of man’s existence and will begin by explaining his existence starting from kingship-<i>Malchut</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> and going up in ascending order.
We already explained each world in general and the offspring of that world and their substance. Now, in the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, the first and lowest aspect that we shall discuss, is the aspect of the kingship-<i>Malchut</i> within it, which is called the four foundational elements of the lowly world. All of its offspring are constructed of the body (<i>Guf</i>) within these aspects, which is the foundational element of physical earth (<i>Affar</i>). They are divided into four categories, as follows:
The lowest level is the category of precious stones and metals, which consist only of the foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>). These receive from the four elemental foundations (<i>Yesodot</i>) as they are composed in their bodies and intermingled to form that particular metal. However, there is one power within each of them which is the cause of the particular admixture that we mentioned, and is called the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>), and it itself is composed of its five powers and levels, as previously mentioned.
Afterwards, vegetative plants (<i>Tzome’ach</i>) were created, such as trees and grasses. Their bodies also are from the foundational element of earth (<i>Affar</i>), and they too have the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the inanimate (<i>Domem</i>). However, they also have an additional soul, which is the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>) and includes its five powers and levels.
Afterwards, the animate beings (<i>Chay</i>) were created, referring to animals and birds etc. They have the body (<i>Guf</i>) and soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the inanimate (<i>Domem</i>), as well as the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>), and in addition, they also have the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) of the animate (<i>Chayah</i>), which is called the animalistic soul (<i>Nefesh HaBehamit</i>) and includes the power of movement and the sensatory powers.
Afterwards, man the speaker (<i>Medaber</i>) was created. He has all the above-mentioned powers, but in addition, he also has a speaking soul (<i>Nefesh HaMedaberet</i>), which is from the elemental foundation of fire (<i>Aish</i>).
However, know with certainty that all these aspects of body and soul as they are in man, are much more refined than they are in the animate (<i>Chay</i>) and that the animate (<i>Chay</i>) are more refined than the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>), and that the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>) more refined than the inanimate (<i>Domem</i>). This should be clear based on what has already been explained. For, in each of these aspects, all of the other aspects are included, each one being more inner than the other.
Afterwards, He created the Jewish man, who is much more refined in all his aspects than all other created beings, both in his body and in the four aspects of his soul, these being the inanimate (<i>Domem</i>), the vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>), the animate (<i>Chay</i>) and the speaking (<i>Medaber</i>). That is, he is of the innermost and most refined aspect of each of the four foundational elements within them, as well as their form (<i>Tzurah</i>), meaning, the soul (<i>Nefesh</i>) that is within them.
Now, because he is more refined than all other creatures of the earth, he is elevated to a greater extent, since he also includes and is bound to all the worlds in all their particular details, from below to above. That is, initially a soul manifests within him from the firmament of <i>Veelon</i>, and that level of soul and above, until even the highest firmament of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, is all called the soul-<i>Nefesh</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>. This aspect of the soul is called the holy intellectual soul (<i>Nefesh HaSeechleet HaKedoshah</i>) within man. However, this level of soul itself is divided into the five powers of <i>Yechidah</i>, <i>Chayah</i>, <i>Neshamah</i>, <i>Ru’ach</i> and <i>Nefesh</i>.
It also divides into two categories in a different manner. For, all the aspects that it takes from the four elemental foundations are called the soul of the elements (<i>Nefesh HaYesodot</i>) and are taken from the above-mentioned powers of the inanimate (<i>Domem</i>), vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>), animate (<i>Chay</i>) and speaker (<i>Medaber</i>), and the soul-<i>Nefesh</i> from <i>Veelon</i> is the crown-<i>Keter</i> over them all, and is called the intellectual soul (<i>Nefesh HaSeechleet</i>). The aspects that are from the other nine firmaments, are divided into the <i>Ru’ach</i>, <i>Neshamah</i>, <i>Chayah</i> and <i>Yechidah</i> of the <i>Nefesh</i>, and altogether, they are called one soul-<i>Nefesh</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> of the general worlds.
Afterwards he obtains a <i>Ru’ach</i> from the world of Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, and it too is divided into a number of levels in the same manner mentioned before. Nevertheless, in relation to the aspect of the general worlds, it is called a <i>Ru’ach</i>. The same is likewise so with the <i>Neshamah</i> from the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, as well as with the <i>Chayah</i> from the world of Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>, and with the <i>Yechidah</i> from Primordial Man-<i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
We thus have clearly explained the nature of the existence of man, and that he includes all the worlds within himself, whether generally or particularly. In contrast, this is not the case with all the other creatures, be they supernal creatures or lower creatures. For, all the offspring of a particular world, only include within themselves that particular world within which they were created.
Now, everything we have stated to this point explains the matter in a way of ascent from below to above. However, man also includes all the worlds within himself from inner to outer, as follows: In the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, he has a body of earth (<i>Affar</i>) which is called the lowly world. Within it are the elemental souls from the external husks (<i>Kelipot</i>), and within that are the aspects of the angels of this world, which were created for the purpose of maintaining this world, such as causing the plants to grow etc. Within all of that, he possesses an aspect of a <i>Neshamah</i> level of soul from the souls of man. All these aspects are made to be a chariot (<i>Merkavah</i>) for the light and illumination that is drawn from the lights of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, which manifest in the four elemental foundations in order to vitalize them, and they are the most inner of them all. The same likewise applies to the aspects within man that stem from the celestial spheres of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i>, as well as from the three worlds of Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i>, Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, and Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>.
With the above in mind, we now can explain the answers to all the questions written at the beginning of this gate. For, the light of the source of souls, is more inner and loftier than the light of the source of the angels, and this is why the angels are in the service of the souls. For, it is through the souls that light and vitality is drawn to the angels from the ten <i>Sefirot</i>.
This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">823</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 33:7 – The “heralds-Erelam-אראלם” referred to in this verse are the Erelim-אראלים angels, which stem from the higher archangel Ariel-אריא״ל. (See Radak to Isaiah 33:7; See Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah 2:7)</i> “Behold, the heralding angels cried out from outside.” For, when sustenance is not drawn to the souls that are more inner than them, they too lack sustenance, being that they are external to them. This is why they cried out and mourned during the time of the destruction, since they are external to the souls. Moreover, this explains why the angels did not descend to manifest in a physical body in this world, because they necessarily would be destroyed by the judgements and shells of the <i>Kelipot</i>. This is because even the souls do not have the power to withstand the shells of the <i>Kelipot</i>. How much more is this so in regard to the angels. Proof of this is from the <i>Nefillim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">824</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 6:4 and Targum Yonatan ben Uziel; Pesikta Rabbati 34:1; Yoma 67b and Rashi there; Zohar I 37a. The word Nefillim means “the fallen ones” and refers to the fallen angels.</i> who requested to descend to this world and were thus destroyed from the world and are wiped out of the coming future. An even greater reason is that because of their lesser state, they would be incapable of drawing influence to all the worlds, but could only do so from their level and out. Moreover, even this itself would not be possible, since they cannot draw sustenance to themselves except through the medium of the souls. Nevertheless, it is indeed true that a soul of the world of Formation-<i>Yetzirah</i> is lesser than an angel from the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, and the same applies to all the worlds. However, a soul of the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i> is greater than an angel of the world of Creation-<i>Briyah</i>, and the same applies to each of the worlds themselves.
Thus, the greatness of the soul has also been explained, since the soul is a light that is born of and drawn from the light of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> themselves, rather than through the medium of an intermediary. This is why the Jewish people are called,<sup class="footnote-marker">825</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 14:1</i> “the children to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה our God.” For, they are in the aspect of a child who is entirely one with his father and is drawn forth from Him. About this, our sages, of blessed memory, said,<sup class="footnote-marker">826</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Bereishit Rabba 47:6; 69:3, 82:6 and elsewhere.</i> “The forefathers [Avraham, Yitzchak and Yaakov] are the Supernal Chariot (<i>Merkavah</i>),” meaning that they are the vehicle for the light of the ten <i>Sefirot</i>, that rides directly upon them, rather than through the medium of any lesser light. This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">827</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 49:3</i> “You are My servant Israel, in whom I take pride.” For, a person’s garments are his pride, as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">828</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 61:10</i> “Like a bridegroom who adorns himself with pride, like a bride who bedecks herself with her jewelry.”
Now the light of the souls is a garment for the ten <i>Sefirot</i>. This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">829</sup><i class="footnote">Song of Songs 6:2</i> “My Beloved has gone down to His garden,” referring to this world. The verse concludes, “To graze His sheep in the gardens, and to pick roses-<i>Lir’ot BaGaneem v’Leelkot Shoshanim</i>-<i><b>ל</b>רעות <b>ב</b>גנים <b>ו</b>ללקוט <b>ש</b>ושנים</i>,” which forms the acrostic (<i>Notarikon</i>) “garment-<i>Levush</i>-<i>לבוש</i>.” For, he picks the souls of the righteous, who are as fragrant as roses because of their good deeds in this world.<sup class="footnote-marker">830</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Yerushalmi, Brachot 2:8</i> He picks them to manifests His light within them. This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">831</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 4:4</i> “You who adhere (<i>HaDveikim</i>-<i>הדבקים</i>) to <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i> are all alive today,” referring to complete and direct adhesion (<i>Dveikut</i>) to the light of the ten <i>Sefirot</i>, which does not apply to any other creatures. This is as is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">832</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 13:11</i> “For just as a belt is fastened to a man’s loins, so I fastened the entire house of Israel to Myself.”
With all the above in mind, the matter of the good inclination (<i>Yetzer HaTov</i>) and the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>) within man, has also been explained and understood. For, these are two forms (<i>Yetzirot</i>) that were added to man in addition to his soul-<i>Neshamah</i>. The good inclination (<i>Yetzer HaTov</i>) is a radiance that comes from the light of the angels, whereas the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>) is a radiance that comes from the light of the external shells (<i>Kelipot</i>), and constitutes the external shell (<i>Kelipah</i>) of the good inclination (<i>Yetzer HaTov</i>).
However, the soul (<i>Neshamah</i>) of man is itself the innermost of them all. Thus, because it is innermost and also is called the essential self (<i>Atzmut</i>) of man, he therefore possesses the free choice to turn them to whichever place he desires, since he is greater than them all. His soul primarily leans toward the good inclination (<i>Yetzer HaTov</i>), since the good inclination is holy like himself. Moreover, it also is juxtaposed in close proximity to him. However, his body, primarily leans toward the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>), since both the body and the evil inclination are juxtaposed in close proximity to each other. Thus, it is primarily here that there is a battle between the substance (<i>Chomer</i>) and the soul (<i>Neshamah</i>). For, since the soul (<i>Neshamah</i>) can only fulfill the <i>mitzvot</i> through the medium of the body (<i>Guf</i>) which, in and of itself, primary leans toward the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>), it is here that there is great difficulty in subduing it.
We thus have explained that it is within the free choice of the soul (<i>Neshamah</i>) to lean toward the good inclination (<i>Yetzer HaTov</i>). However, because the soul requires the body (<i>Guf</i>) to act, great toil is necessary to subdue the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>). Understand all this very well. Also understand that after a person passes from this world, neither the soul (<i>Neshamah</i>) nor the body (<i>Guf</i>) are judged until they manifest together, as they were when he was alive, as our sages, of blessed memory, explained with the analogy of the lame man on the shoulders of the blind man.<sup class="footnote-marker">833</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 91a-b; Midrash Vayikra Rabba 4:5; Zohar Chadash Ruth 38b; Sefer HaMashalim of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as The Book of Allegories, 110 – When the body and soul are judged on account of sin, they are like a blind man and a lame man who the king gave the responsibility of guarding an orchard, but they blundered and did not properly guard it. When HaShem, blessed is He, brings about judgment, the soul declares, “It was not I who blundered. It was the body, that possesses an evil inclination that makes it sin.” On the other hand, the body declares, “Were it not for the soul I could not have sinned, for a body without a soul is as lifeless as an inanimate stone. Without the soul who moves me, I cannot make even the slightest move.” The two are analogous to a blind man and a lame man who the king charged with guarding his orchard, but they transgressed and ate of its fruits. When the king brought them to judgment the blind man said, “I couldn’t have eaten them, for I could not see where they were,” and the lame man said, “I couldn’t have eaten them, for I could not go to where they were.” What did the king do? He put the lame man on the blind man’s shoulders and said, “The two of you joined in partnership to transgress my will, for you provided the eyes and you provided the legs and both of you ate of the fruits. Therefore, you will be punished together.” In the same manner, HaShem, blessed is He, joined the soul to the body and advised them that if they sin before Him, they will be regarded as a partnership. Regarding this, the Psalmist stated (Psalms 50:4), “He calls to the heavens above and to the earth, that He may judge His people.” The words “He calls to the heavens above” refer to the soul, as we see that the numerical value of the heavens-HaShamayim-השמים-395 is equal to the soul-Neshamah-נשמה-395. The words, “And to the earth” refer to the body, which was taken from the earth. We thus see that both the soul and the body are brought as one in judgement before HaShem, blessed is He.</i>
We now will explain the answer to the first two questions, namely, why was it necessary for man to be created in this world with a soul and a body, and why are there two forms in him, the good inclination (<i>Yetzer HaTov</i>) and the evil inclination (<i>Yetzer HaRa</i>). We also will answer the questions that arise from the verses,<sup class="footnote-marker">834</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 68:35</i> “Give strength to God,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">835</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:18</i> “You have weakened the Rock who bore you,” and the like.
